Grant v. State


No. 94-CA-00032-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


686 So. 2d 1078; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 690



December 19, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 153594 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 16, 1993, W. O. Dillard RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bondholders sought review from the Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), in which they were denied recovery on bonds issued prior to the Civil War. The trial court held that the actions were barred by the running of the statute of limitations and granted defendant state's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court found that Miss. Const. § 258, by which the state repudiated the bonds, did not prohibit the bondholders from bringing suit, but prohibited the state from making any payment on the underlying debt. The court would not allow the bondholders to use equitable principles to circumvent their lack of diligence in bringing their suit over one hundred years after the statute of limitations had run. It was not until one hundred and twenty years after the seven-year statute of limitations went into effect before the bondholders asserted their rights in claiming payment owed by the state. The financial hardship of paying the bonds that would be imposed on the state was the type of hardship that was contemplated by the court when the doctrine of laches was adopted. Regardless of whether § 258 was in conflict with the United States Constitution or not, the statute of limitations began running at the time the right to collect the interest and debt duly owed on the bonds accrued. Thus, the time bar of the claim was dispositive, and it was not necessary for the chancellor to go further and hold § 258 unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court held that the chancellor correctly held that the statute of limitations had run and the bondholders were barred from pursuing their claim. The determination that the repudiation of the bonds was unconstitutional was error because the running of the statute of limitations was dispositive in granting the state's motion for summary judgment in the bondholder's suit.

 

2 of 825 DOCUMENTS


City of Jackson v. Lakeland Lounge


No. 93-CA-00874-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


688 So. 2d 742; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 677; 67 A.L.R.5th 719



December 12, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied December 15, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7519.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 15720D2 from Judgment dated JULY 19, 1993, W. O. Dillard RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: REVERSE AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a ruling from the Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which ruled that its zoning ordinance regulating adult entertainment, particularly topless dancing, was unconstitutional. Appellee adult club had challenged the ordinance when it had difficulty obtaining permits from appellant. Adult entertainment was allowed only in areas zoned light industrial, I-1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city sought to regulate adult entertainment and enacted a zoning ordinance. Appellee adult club opened for business in an area that was not zoned for adult entertainment. A federal circuit court found the ordinance constitutional. The chancery court found it unconstitutional and that females had equal protection to be topless in the same way as males, with the ordinance being enforceable only if the reference to gender was struck. On review, the court found that the statute was not vague and ambiguous and that the chancery court's interpretation led to an absurd result. The court found appellee's challenge to the ordinance barred because it attempted to elude res judicata by raising a new legal theory. The court asserted that the chancery court went outside the scope of the pleadings in ruling that females had equal protection to be topless in the same way as males, that it lacked proper jurisdiction, and that treating males and females differently under these circumstances did not violate the equal protection clause. The court found that the difference in treatment had a substantial relation to appellant's interest in regulation, and the judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the ruling of the lower court, which had ruled against appellant city and in favor of appellee adult club. A common sense reading and interpretation of the ordinance found it not vague or ambiguous. The constitutional challenge to the ordinance was precluded under res judicata. The chancellor erred by going outside the scope of the pleadings and determining that the ordinance violated the equal protection clause.

 

3 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State


No. 95-DP-00407-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


690 So. 2d 276; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 681



December 12, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5165.
Rehearing denied by Brown v. State, 691 So. 2d 1027, 1997 Miss. LEXIS 174 (Miss., 1997)
Writ of certiorari denied Brown v. Mississippi, 522 U.S. 849, 118 S. Ct. 136, 139 L. Ed. 2d 85, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5165 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at Brown v. State, 798 So. 2d 481, 2001 Miss. LEXIS 196 (Miss., 2001)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Brown v. Puckett, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 26359 (N.D. Miss., Mar. 12, 2003)
Application granted by Brown v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 701 (Miss., June 17, 2004)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Partial summary judgment denied by Brown v. Epps, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 89470 (N.D. Miss., Dec. 11, 2006)
Post-conviction relief granted at Brown v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 605 (Miss., Dec. 6, 2012)
Post-conviction relief denied at Brown v. State, 2015 Miss. LEXIS 149 (Miss., Mar. 26, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. CR94201 from Judgment dated APRIL 07, 1995, Andrew Cleveland Baker RULING JUDGE, DeSoto County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER (THREE COUNTS) AND SENTENCE OF DEATH AFFIRMED. EXECUTION DATE TO BE SET WITHIN SIXTY DAYS OF FINAL DISPOSITION OF THIS CASE PURSUANT TO MISS. CODE ANN. § 99-19-105(7)(1972) AND M.R.A.P. 41(a).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the DeSoto County Circuit (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder and sentenced him to die for the death of a child committed during felonious abuse and battery. He was also found guilty and sentenced to serve two consecutive sentences of life imprisonment for the murders of the child's mother and grandmother.


OVERVIEW: After a jury convicted defendant of capital murder, he appealed numerous rulings of the trial court. The court affirmed the convictions, holding that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence of his clothing because these were items seized in plain view during a valid arrest. Evidence of prior drug use by the defendant was allowable under Miss. R. Evid. 404(b) because it was interrelated to his responses to police questioning. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in trying defendant in ankle shackles due to his violent jail behavior. The victim's photographs had evidentiary value that outweighed any prejudice. Relevance and admission of expert testimony was within the trial court's discretion. Prior transcripts were properly used to impeach defendant. A jury instruction regarding defendant's flight from police was proper because the flight was unexplained and probative of guilty knowledge, and the instruction regarding the heinous nature of the crime had appropriate limiting language. An underlying felony was properly used as an aggravating factor under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101. Prosecutorial comments, while questionable, were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder and capital murder, and also affirmed his death sentence and his two consecutive life sentences.

 

4 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Southwest Miss. Regional Medical Ctr. v. Lawrence


No. 90-CA-01182-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


684 So. 2d 1257; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 642; 12 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 605



December 5, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 4669 from Judgment dated OCTOBER 18, 1990, Joe N. Pigott RULING JUDGE, Pike County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Pike County (Mississippi), which awarded appellee employee actual and punitive damages and damages for mental anguish in her suit against appellant for failing to provide compensation for her work-related injuries and firing her for filing a claim. It also challenged the award to appellee employee benefit trust of the costs paid for medical care for appellee employee's injuries.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employer denied appellee employee coverage for injuries she claimed were job-related and terminated her employment. Appellant was not covered by workers' compensation and instead was self-insured. The employee handbook provided that employees would be compensated for on-the-job injuries up to the coverage provided in the Workers' Compensation Act. However, appellee employee's claim for coverage was denied as appellant claimed the injuries were not work-related and terminated her employment. The trial court granted appellee employee judgment for actual and punitive damages and damages for mental anguish. It also entered judgment to reimburse appellee employee benefit trust for costs expended for appellee employee's health care. The court affirmed the award of actual compensatory damages because there was an agreement between appellant and appellee employee that the equivalent of workers' compensation benefits would be provided and the injuries were job-related. The jury award for mental anguish damages and the award to appellee employee benefit trust were also affirmed. The court reversed the award of punitive damages, however, because the facts did not support the award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of compensatory damages to appellee employee, as the parties had an agreement that appellant employer would provide the equivalent of workers' compensation coverage and evidence was sufficient to show the injuries were job-related, and affirmed the award for mental anguish. It also affirmed the award to appellee employee benefit trust. The award of punitive damages was reversed, as the facts did not support the award.

 

5 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Stewart v. Southeast Foods


No. 92-CA-01236-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


688 So. 2d 733; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 643



December 5, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 9112341 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 19, 1992, Gray Evans RULING JUDGE, Washington County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT IS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff customer appealed from a judgment of the Washington County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted defendant store's motion for summary judgment, in her action for malicious prosecution against the store after she was charged with assault and battery in an altercation with the store's security guard. A municipal judge dismissed the charges but in an affidavit stated that he did so to be lenient and that he believed she was guilty.


OVERVIEW: The store's security guard suspected a customer of shoplifting and an altercation arose between the customer and a security guard. The store brought charges against the customer for assault and battery. After a municipal judge dismissed the charges, she brought suit against the store for malicious prosecution. The store's motion for summary judgment was supported by an affidavit from the municipal judge in which he stated that he really believed she was guilty but dismissed the charges in order to be lenient. The circuit judge granted the store's motion for summary judgment and the customer appealed, claiming that it was improperly considered. Upon appeal, the court affirmed the circuit court judgment. The court held that the affidavit constituted relevant and admissible evidence with regard to the issue of whether the municipal court criminal proceedings terminated in the customer's favor. Having so held, it was unnecessary for the court to consider whether the circuit judge properly granted summary judgment on the issue of malice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision to grant the store's motion for summary judgment. The court determined that the circuit court judge properly considered the affidavit of the municipal judge and therefore, the store's summary judgment motion was properly granted.

Medina v. State


No. 93-KA-00238-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


688 So. 2d 727; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 635



November 21, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 27038 from Judgment dated FEBRUARY 26, 1993, Jerry Owen Terry Sr. RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF TRANSFER OF A CONTROLLED SUBSTANCE AND SENTENCE OF THIRTY YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AND PAYMENT OF $ 1,000.00 FINE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted her of transfer of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Having made multiple sales of narcotics to an undercover agent, defendant was subject to life imprisonment without parole under Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(f) (1972). However, the lower court bifurcated the trial, and the jury considered only the evidence regarding the transfer of cocaine, after which defendant was convicted of the offense. In post-trial hearings, the defense successfully demurred to the indictment, arguing that the enhanced penalty of § 41-29-139(f) was unconstitutional. Defendant was sentenced to 30 years in custody and ordered to pay a fine. On appeal, the court affirmed her conviction. The court found that the trial court properly found the indictment correctable because the issue was one of form and not substance and allowed the State to amend the indictment to accurately reflect defendant's age. The court stated that the record failed to show that defendant was unable to prepare a defense due to the omission in or the amendment to the indictment regarding her age. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied defendant's motion for a continuance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the transfer of cocaine conviction.

 

7 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Puckett v. Abels


No. 95-CA-00856-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


684 So. 2d 671; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 636



November 21, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 2519553CIV from Judgment dated JULY 18, 1995, James E. Graves Jr. RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commissioner of the Mississippi Department of Corrections, contested a judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District, (Mississippi), which, in appellee prisoners' declaratory judgment action, ruled that S.B. 2175 (Mississippi) was an ex post facto law as it applied to the prisoners, who were charged with committing crimes prior to July 1, 1995, but were not to be sentenced until on or after July 1, 1995.


OVERVIEW: The retroactive application of S.B. 2175 required that 85 percent of a prisoner's sentence be served, and it eliminated the opportunity for parole. The prisoners were charged with felony crimes that occurred prior to the bill's effective date of July 1, 1995, and their charges were not to be disposed of until after July 1, 1995. The trial court held that S.B. 2175 was an ex post facto law as applied to the prisoners. On the Commissioner's appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the proper method of review was the "effect" review, which provided that when an amendment did not retrospectively change an offense's sentencing range but did make a change that could indirectly affect the length of a prisoner's term, no Ex post facto Clause violation occurred because the possibility of an indirect effect was speculative. Here, however the court found that S.B. 2175 lengthened the prisoners' sentences and eliminated any possibility for parole. Thus, because the amendment directly increased the punishment for covered crimes and the effect on the prisoners was not merely speculative, Senate Bill 2175 was an ex post facto law that violated the United States and Mississippi Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

8 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Trs. v. T.H. by & ex rel. T.H. (in the Interest of T.H.)


No. 93-CA-00441-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


681 So. 2d 110; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 492



September 12, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified December 19, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 12291 from Judgment dated APRIL 12, 1993, Albert S. Johnston III RULING JUDGE, Jackson County Youth Court.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; MODIFIED IN PART; AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school board challenged a judgment from the Jackson County Youth Court (Mississippi), which entered a permanent injunction preventing the school board from taking any further disciplinary action or punitive action against appellee student in connection with or in any manner related to the student's violation of school policy on the consumption of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: The school board suspended the student for violating the school's policy on the consumption of alcohol. As a punishment for the suspension, the student was given no credit for classes missed during the suspension period. The school board's application of the policy meant that the student would be suspended for 10 days, receive a grade of 0 for each day he was suspended, and receive, at best, a grade of 65/F for the semester's work. The youth court found that two provisions of the school's policy violated various constitutional rights of the student. On appeal, the school board contended that the policy could not be declared facially overbroad. The court affirmed the judgment of the youth court in part and modified it in part. The court held that: (1) the school board could constitutionally proscribe consumption of alcohol within limits; (2) the youth court correctly ruled that the punishment was arbitrary and capricious as applied to the student, not on constitutional grounds, but on statutory ones; (3) the injunction should be modified to give the student no credit for his class work for the last five days of his suspension.


OUTCOME: The court modified the permanent injunction by allowing the school board to give the student no credit for his class work for the final five days of his suspension. As modified, the court affirmed the judgment the enjoined the school board from taking further disciplinary action against the student for his violation of the school policy against alcohol consumption.

 

9 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Fisher v. State


No. 92-KA-00933-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


690 So. 2d 268; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 490



September 5, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 91100893 from Judgment dated AUGUST 05, 1992, Bill Jones RULING JUDGE, Jackson County Circuit Court.

Rehearing Denied April 10, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Miss. LEXIS 150.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which entered a judgment convicting him of the capital rape of his 11-year-old niece.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for capital rape on the grounds that the prosecution failed to provide a specific date of the crime so he could maintain an alibi defense; that his wife's testimony in which she stated defendant admitted the abuse to her were confidential and barred by the marital privilege; that the State failed to prove his age at trial; and that the capital rape statute violated the separation of powers doctrine. On appeal, the court reversed and remand for a new trial, holding that while some of defendant's wife's challenged statements were not privileged because they were made in front of a third person, certain statements made by defendant to his wife were in confidence and their admission constituted prejudicial error in violation of Miss. R. Evid. 504. In addition, the trial court found that the indictment was not deficient for failing to provide the exact date of the crime, and that although the State could not admit proof of defendant's age through the regularly conducted activity hearsay exception, it was admissible as a non-hearsay admission. Finally, the court held that statutorily mandated penalties did not violate the separation of powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for capital rape and remanded due to the trial court's admission of inadmissible, prejudicial evidence.

Hoops v. State


No. 93-KA-00530-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


681 So. 2d 521; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 433



August 22, 1996, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [**1] OUNT I: CONVICTION OF AGGRAVATED ASSAULT AND SENTENCE OF FIFTEEN YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED. COUNT II: CONVICTION OF AGGRAVATED ASSAULT AND SENTENCE OF FIFTEEN YEARS IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED. SENTENCE SHALL RUN CONSECUTIVELY WITH THE SENTENCE IN COUNT I.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Mississippi), which convicted defendant, after a grand jury indictment, of two counts of aggravated assault following the involvement of defendant with a gang that shot an individual in another gang.


OVERVIEW: Following a grand jury indictment, defendant was convicted of two counts of aggravated assault for his involvement in the shooting of an individual during a gang altercation. On appeal, the court affirmed. Holding certain arguments as procedurally barred, the court held that the evidence failed to show that the trial judge specifically targeted defendant in his charge to the grand jury. In addition, defendant failed to comply with the requirements of Miss. Code Ann. § 99-15-35 in order to properly support his motion to change venue. The court determined that allegedly damaging testimony was invited by defendant's questions and that the trial judge properly admonished the jury to disregard. In addition, evidence of gang affiliation was admissible to show motive and was not substantially more prejudicial than probative. The court further held that an aiding and abetting jury instruction was properly given and other instructions were properly refused because they were not appropriate lesser offense instructions. The court finally found that the trial judge considered youthful offender sentencing alternatives in determining the sentence, which was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of two counts of aggravated assault in a gang shooting.

Hunt v. State


No. 92-KA-00475-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


687 So. 2d 1154; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 426



August 8, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 30, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 8799 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 04, 1991, William R. Lamb RULING JUDGE, Marshall County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF MURDER AND SENTENCE OF LIFE IMPRISONMENT IN THE CUSTODY OF THE MISSISSIPPI DEPARTMENT OF CORRECTIONS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for the murder of her husband and sentenced to life imprisonment. Her motion for a new trial was denied. She appealed, in forma pauperis, from her conviction and sentence in the Marshall County Circuit Court (Mississippi).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's boyfriend and another man beat the husband with an axe handle; he subsequently died of asphyxiation. The next morning, defendant and her boyfriend went to the sheriff's office to report her husband missing. After being taken to identify her husband's body, defendant was questioned by a lieutenant who noticed a discrepancy between her statement and what she had told the sheriff earlier. Later, defendant called her parents, who contacted an attorney. Defendant was advised of and waived her Miranda rights. The attorney called, but was not allowed to speak to defendant. Later, she was again interviewed and made self-incriminating statements. Although defendant was being interrogated, the court found that defendant's Fifth Amendment right to counsel was not violated because she was not in custody where she voluntarily went to the sheriff's office and was not physically restrained from leaving. Although defendant was told that she could not leave, the court found that she was temporarily detained in order to obtain a missing-person report. The court found that the fact that an attorney was trying to contact defendant was of no consequence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Davis v. State


No. 92-DP-00890-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


684 So. 2d 643; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 292



June 27, 1996, Decided  
June 27, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 11, 1996. Rehearing Denied September 26, 1996. Certiorari Denied, April 14, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2295.
Rehearing denied by Davis v. State, 1996 Miss. LEXIS 562 (Miss., Sept. 26, 1996)
Writ of certiorari denied Davis v. Mississippi, 520 U.S. 1170, 117 S. Ct. 1437, 137 L. Ed. 2d 544, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2295 (1997)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Davis v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 218 (Miss., May 3, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 3065 from Judgment dated JUNE 05, 1992, Bill Jones RULING JUDGE, Greene County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH BY LETHAL INJECTION AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Greene County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder and imposed a sentence of death by lethal injection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the murder of a woman while engaged in the commission of a robbery. On appeal defendant raised 18 points of error. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence, holding that (1) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to quash the regular venire because defendant did not make any request for special venire prior to trial and failed to designate the relevant portion of the record for purposes of appeal; (2) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the prosecutor to ask jurors whether they could consider the death penalty given certain specific circumstances because the prosecution's voir dire was within the permissible range of acceptable questioning; (3) the voluntary intoxication instruction was properly submitted to the jury because the jury was presented with the issue of defendant's intoxication at the time of the murder and the jury was not misled by the "McDaniel rule" instruction; and (4) the trial court did not err in declining to grant a lesser included offense instruction because a reasonable jury could not have found defendant not guilty on the charge of capital murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's capital murder conviction and sentence of death by lethal injection.

City of Jackson v. State


No. 94-CA-00555-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


676 So. 2d 257; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 290



June 26, 1996, Decided  
June 13, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 251940106 from Judgment dated MAY 05, 1994, William F. Coleman RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT IS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order by the Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which granted a motion to dismiss its declaratory judgment action regarding enforcement of local zoning ordinances against appellees, the Mississippi Veterans Memorial Stadium Commission, the Mississippi State Department of Finance and Administration, and the developer.


OVERVIEW: Appellees entered into an agreement whereby appellee developer would lease two parcels of land next to the stadium. The agreement was entered into pursuant to 23-11 Miss. Code Ann. § 55- 23-11(2) and was approved by appellee department as required by Miss. Code Ann. § 55-23-11(3). Appellant brought suit to enforce local zoning ordinances because appellee developer was going to use the leased parcels for commercial purposes. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal. The court held that appellant lacked standing to bring an action based on the legislative intent of 23-11 Miss. Code Ann. § 55- 23-11 that appellee commission had the "full power and authority" to enter agreements regarding stadium property and the usage of that property. The court did not address any of the issues regarding whether appellant had failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted based on its ruling that appellant lacked standing to bring the action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order which dismissed appellant's action against appellees regarding enforcement of local zoning ordinances.

 

14 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Skaggs v. State


No. 91-KA-00626-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


676 So. 2d 897; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 317



June 13, 1996, Decided  
July 3, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 25076 from Judgment dated JUNE 05, 1991. Jerry Owen Terry Sr. RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which convicted him of forcible rape and sentenced him to 30 years imprisonment. Defendant asserted that he was denied his statutory and constitutional rights to a speedy trial and that the trial court erred in its exclusion of certain testimony.


OVERVIEW: At the date set for defendant's trial, which was within the 270-day time period allowed by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-17-1 (1992), the trial court's docket was overcrowded and the case was continued. Defendant asserted that the delay should have been attributed to the State. The trial court overruled defendant's motion. Defendant's discovery stated that his former wife would testify that the victim had stated that she would not have pressed charges if defendant had "kissed her and got her ready." When she took the stand, the wife testified that the victim had stated that she would drop the charges if she were paid. The State objected and defense counsel asserted that he had only recently been made aware of the new information. The trial court ordered the jury to disregard the wife's testimony. On appeal, held that the trial court's crowded docket was a good cause for the delay and that no prejudice to defendant had been shown. No violation of § 99-17-1 occurred because the "good cause" covered the period between the trial settings. The trial court erred by excluding the wife's testimony because there were available less harsh sanctions than exclusion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction for forcible rape. The court ordered a retrial.

 

15 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Sanders v. State


NO. 91-KA-01243-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


678 So. 2d 663; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 300



June 6, 1996, DECIDED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Sanders v. State, 1996 Miss. LEXIS 480 (Miss., Aug. 15, 1996)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Sanders v. State, 846 So. 2d 230, 2002 Miss. App. LEXIS 388 (Miss. Ct. App., 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Sanders v. State, 2010 Miss. App. LEXIS 151 (Miss. Ct. App., Mar. 23, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 13732 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 06, 1991, Joe N. Pigott RULING JUDGE, Pike County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Pike County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of unlawful possession of cocaine with intent to deliver and sentenced him to pay a $ 30,000 fine and serve 30 years, as an habitual offender, in the custody of the Mississippi Department of Corrections without parole, probation, good time, or early release.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for the crime of unlawful possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. He was not indicted, however, until nearly two years later. Defendant was convicted and was sentenced as a habitual offender. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The trial court did not err in refusing to suppress evidence found during a warrantless search of defendant's car. The agents' informant had recorded conversations with defendant in which defendant agreed to go to New Orleans and get the informant cocaine; thus, the agents had probable cause to believe that the promised drugs was somewhere in the car. Moreover, because the car was in motion and was close to the state border when it was stopped, the exigency requirement excusing the issuance of a warrant was satisfied. There was no error in allowing evidence of defendant's prior illegal acts, as it went to his predisposition, which was relevant to his entrapment defense. It was the combination of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139 and the habitual offender statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 that led to defendant's sentence, and as his sentence fell within those guidelines, it was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

16 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Mohundro v. Alcorn County


NO. 92-CA-00152-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


675 So. 2d 848; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 301



June 6, 1996, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of October 12, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Miss. LEXIS 497.

Appeal No. 90433FA from Judgment dated JANUARY 29, 1992, Barry Wayne Ford RULING JUDGE, Alcorn County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, personal injury victim and his wife, sought review of a summary judgment from the Alcorn County Circuit Court (Mississippi) entered in favor of appellees, county, county board of supervisors (board), board members, and corporate sureties, in appellants' personal injury action. The summary judgment was entered in favor of appellees on the basis of sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: The victim sustained a broken neck and was rendered quadriplegic after he drove his truck into a washout in the middle of a county road. The washout occurred after one of the county supervisors decided to replace a rotting bridge with a culvert and, in fact, supervised the installation of the culvert. The responsible county commissioner also discovered the washout, but he did not take any preventive action other than to put up unlighted warning signs. The court reversed and remanded the action with respect to the one responsible supervisor, concluding that genuine issues of material fact remained as to whether he exceeded his authority and whether he was so grossly negligent that his action might be described as constructively intentional. In all other respects, the court affirmed the judgment. The court rejected appellants' argument that the immunity statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-6 et seq., was unconstitutional. Appellants asserted that sovereign immunity was inapplicable where the governmental authority created the hazard, but the court refused to carve out an immunity exception. The court also found no breach of ministerial duty on the part of the board or its members.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the summary judgment in favor of one of the county supervisors in appellants' personal injury action. In all other respects, the court affirmed the summary judgment against appellants.

 

17 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State v. Watkins


NO. 92-CA-01070-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


676 So. 2d 247; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 327



May 30, 1996, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 24069 from Judgment dated SEPTEMBER 11, 1992, Nathan P. Adams Jr. RULING JUDGE, Sunflower County Chancery Court.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Mississippi sought review of the order of the Sunflower County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which held that a portion of Miss. Code Ann. § 41-21-77 was unconstitutional. A special master declared the section unconstitutional during a hearing to show cause why the director of the state hospital should not be held in contempt for failure to comply with a commitment order.


OVERVIEW: The trial court issued a commitment order that required the director to admit an insane person for examination and treatment. The insane person was never admitted. The director and the Attorney General of the State of Mississippi were both ordered to appear at the show cause hearing. The Attorney General did not appear, nor was he given notice that the constitutionality of the commitment statute was being challenged. The trial court held that the portion of § 41-21-77 which provided that no person shall be admitted to the state hospital until the director determined that facilities and services were available was unconstitutional. The court held that the trial court erroneously declared the portion of the statute unconstitutional without proper notice to the Attorney General. The court found that although the lower court had the authority to declare the statute unconstitutional, its actions were improper because the issue could have been easily resolved without reaching the constitutionality of the statute. Also, under Miss. R. Civ. P. 24(d), the Attorney General was required to be notified of the constitutional challenge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and rendered a judgment that the statute remained cloaked in the presumption of constitutionality.

 

18 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Doss v. State


NO. 93-DP-00509-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


709 So. 2d 369; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 267



May 23, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing filed June 6, 1996. As Modified December 11, 1997.
Rehearing denied by Doss v. State, 703 So. 2d 864, 1997 Miss. LEXIS 795 (Miss., 1997)
Writ of certiorari denied Doss v. Mississippi, 523 U.S. 1111, 140 L. Ed. 2d 821, 118 S. Ct. 1684, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 3048 (1998)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Petition granted by, in part, Petition denied by, in part Doss v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 847 (Miss., July 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 6078A from Judgment dated MARCH 30, 1993, James C. Sumner, RULING JUDGE, Grenada County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Grenada County Circuit Court (Mississippi) entered a decision convicting defendant of capital murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his friend robbed a grocery store. During the robbery, defendant and his friend shot the grocery clerk. Defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. Defendant contended that he was entitled to a lesser included offense instruction, the trial judge erred in excusing jurors for cause, the trial court erred in allowing the state to introduce into evidence photographs of the deceased, and the trial court erred in submitting to the jury the robbery-murder aggravating circumstance. On appeal, the court affirmed and held (1) Defendant was not entitled to a lesser-included offense instruction because robbery was neither a lesser-included offense nor a component to capital murder, (2) defendant did not object when the trial court excused the jurors for cause, so he was procedurally barred from appealing the issue, (3) the photographs were properly admitted because they aided in describing the circumstances of the murder, (4) the use of the robbery aggravator was proper, and (5) the fact that the aggravating circumstance was identical to an element of the underlying offense did not violate the Eighth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for capital murder and his death sentence.

 

19 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Foster v. State


No. 95-DP-00750-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


687 So. 2d 1124; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 216



May 16, 1996, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [**1] APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO FILE POST-CONVICTION COLLATERAL RELIEF MOTION TO VACATE CONVICTION AND/OR DEATH SENTENCE DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applied for leave to file a motion for relief under the Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act (Act), Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-1 et seq. (Supp. 1994), based upon ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant's capital murder conviction and death sentence had previously been affirmed by the court on appeal, and writ of certiorari denied. A federal district court granted and vacated a stay of execution. The court stayed his execution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for killing a store clerk during a robbery. On appeal defendant raised 26 assignments of error, including issues related to particularized findings for juvenile death penalty recipients, the "robbery-murder-pecuniary gain" aggravator, and the failure to grant certain jury instructions. In his certiorari petition defendant raised the particularized findings and aggravator issues. Defendant claimed in his application under the Act that counsel was ineffective because he failed adequately to investigate and present mitigation evidence regarding defendant's mental health, intelligence level, and alcohol use; to request transfer to youth court; to raise the denial of certain jury instructions on appeal; to object to the robbery, avoiding arrest, and pecuniary gain aggravators; and to preserve reversible error. The court denied defendant's application. The court held that his claims failed on the merits under the Strickland test or were procedurally barred by res judicata, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(3) (Supp. 1994), or waiver, Miss Code Ann. § 99-39-21(2) (Supp. 1994), because the issues were decided or could have been presented at trial or on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's application for leave to file a post-conviction collateral relief motion to vacate his conviction, his death sentence, or both.

 

20 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


No. 90-DP-00266-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


684 So. 2d 1179; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 194



May 9, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 23, 1997. Certiorari Denied March 24, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 8310202 from Judgment dated JANUARY 20, 1990, Darwin M. Maples RULING JUDGE, Jackson County Circuit Court On change of venue to George County.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE OF DEATH AFFIRMED. EXECUTION DATE TO BE SET WITHIN SIXTY DAYS OF FINAL DISPOSITION OF THIS CASE PURSUANT TO MISS. CODE ANN. § 99-19-105(7) AND M.R.A.P. 41 (a).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the death sentence imposed in the Circuit Court of George County (Mississippi) after conviction for capital murder committed while engaged in the commission of the crime of kidnapping following a new sentence determination hearing ordered by the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death following a resentencing hearing held on remand after the original sentence of death was reversed on appeal. On direct appeal, the court affirmed the sentence of death and rejected all of defendant's numerous grounds for appeal. Despite finding that defendant failed to raise the issue whether kidnapping was properly explained in the court below, the court held that the jury in the resentence-determining phase did not have to be instructed on the elements of capital murder, murder, and kidnapping in order to make a finding beyond a reasonable doubt of the existence of that aggravating circumstance. The omission of the kidnapping instruction in the resentencing phase was cured by that first jury's conviction of murder and kidnapping, which by necessary implication allowed the resentencing jury to consider whether defendant was guilty of the underlying felony of kidnapping for aggravator purposes. The resentencing jury could "reuse" the capital murder conviction to establish the aggravator that the offense was committed while defendant was engaged in the commission of kidnapping.


OUTCOME: The resentencing jury's decision that defendant should suffer death for capital murder was affirmed and the execution date was ordered to be set within 60 days of final disposition of the case.

 

21 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


No. 90-DP-01346-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


672 So. 2d 1246; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 193



April 25, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. F319 from Judgment dated AUGUST 01, 1990, L. Breland Hilburn Jr. RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of September 28, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Miss. LEXIS 489.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AFFIRMED. SENTENCE OF DEATH VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: At trial, defendant was found guilty of capital murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, the First Judicial District of the Circuit Court of Hinds County (Mississippi) affirmed the conviction and sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant threatened to obtain revenge on his ex-wife by harming one of her daughters. After the victim's disappearance, defendant told a friend that he killed the girl prior to discovery of the victim's body. No other direct evidence linked defendant to the murder. On appeal, the court applied a four-part balancing test and rejected defendant's claim that his constitutional right to a speedy trial was denied. The court upheld the admissibility of defendant's prior murder conviction because an element of the State's case required proof that defendant was under a life sentence when he murdered the victim in this case. The court determined that the prosecutor's indirect reference to defendant's failure to testify was harmless error. Defendant was not entitled to a circumstantial evidence instruction because his confession to his friend that he killed his stepdaughter removed the case from the circumstantial context. The court reversed defendant's sentence because the jury was not informed that he could be sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The trial court's instructions on three aggravating circumstances was also error.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for capital murder was affirmed. His sentence of death was vacated and his case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

 

22 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Nicholson ex rel. Gollott v. State


No. 91-KA-00511-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


672 So. 2d 744; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 146



April 18, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 6273 from Judgment dated FEBRUARY 16, 1991, Kosta N. Vlahos RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District On change of venue to Hancock County.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of June 1, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Miss. LEXIS 263.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF MANSLAUGHTER AND SENTENCE OF FIFTEEN YEARS WITH THREE YEARS SUSPENDED MAKING A TOTAL OF TWELVE YEARS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that convicted him of manslaughter in the death of his former wife.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to his former wife's home and while he was there, she suffered a gunshot wound from defendant's pistol and died. Defendant's first trial ended in a mistrial, but the second trial resulted in a conviction for manslaughter. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that there was no reversible error when the circuit clerk was allowed to provide requested information to the prosecution during jury selection. The trial was not barred by the Double Jeopardy Clauses of the United States and Mississippi Constitutions because defendant failed to prove the prosecutor's intent in forcing defendant to request a mistrial. The trial court did not err in refusing to declare unconstitutional the statute setting forth the compensation plan for circuit clerks because circuit clerks had no judicial power to make decisions affecting the outcome of cases. The trial court also did not err in refusing to direct a verdict or to issue a peremptory instruction of not guilty on all counts when the expert testimony and defendant's own testimony supported a finding that the shooting was not accidental. The court found that the jury was correctly and completely charged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that convicted defendant of manslaughter in the death of his former wife.

 

23 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. State


No. 94-KP-00705-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1996 Miss. LEXIS 151



April 18, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 11015 from Judgment dated JUNE 01, 1994, Melvin Keith Starrett RULING JUDGE, Lincoln County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION:  [*1] REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of a decision of the Lincoln County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied without an evidentiary hearing his motion for post-conviction relief. The prisoner alleged that his guilty plea to a charge of armed robbery had been entered involuntarily, and that the trial court failed to inquire and determine that he understood the nature of his plea under Rule 3.03 of the Uniform Rules of Circuit Court Practice.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was indicted for armed robbery and aggravated assault. The prisoner was sentenced to eight years of imprisonment without parole on his guilty plea for armed robbery. The trial court denied the prisoner's motion for a plea transcript on the ground that the plea transcript had not been transcribed, that it was not a part of the trial court's file, and that no showing of need had been made. The prisoner claimed that his plea was involuntary, and that he did not understand the charge and the consequences of the plea. On appeal, the court reversed, and remanded the case for an evidentiary hearing on the voluntariness of the plea. The court found that the prisoner demonstrated a specific need for a transcript of his plea hearing. The trial court did not comply with Rule 3.03 of the Uniform Rules of Circuit Court Practice, by which it was required to inquire and to determine that the prisoner understood the nature and the consequences of his plea, including the sentencing penalties. Without a transcript of the plea hearing, or any other evidence such as the prisoner's plea petition, the court could not conduct a meaningful review of the prisoner's claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of the prisoner's motion for post-conviction relief, and remanded the case for an evidentiary hearing on the voluntariness of his plea.

 

24 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Harris


No. 92-CA-00883-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


705 So. 2d 819; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 127



March 28, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 21, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Miss. LEXIS 381.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. E830 from Judgment dated JUNE 22, 1992, Jon M. Barnwell RULING JUDGE, Leflore County Chancery County.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant illegitimate son sought review of a judgment from the Leflore County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which dismissed as time-barred under Miss. Code Ann. § 91-1-15(d)(ii) his claim as the only direct heir of his deceased father's estate on a motion strike filed by appellee legitimate heir.


OVERVIEW: The illegitimate son contended that an amendment to Miss. Code Ann. § 91-1-15 granted him a window within which to assert his claim as the illegitimate son and only heir of his deceased father. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, finding that the legitimate heir became an executrix de son tort of the unprobated estate of the decedent and that under Mississippi law she was under a duty to use reasonable diligence to ascertain potential heirs. Further, the court fount that the legitimate heir took a position in the estate of the decedent that was beneficial to herself and detrimental to the illegitimate son. The court determined that the legitimate heir was under a duty to act for the rightful heirs of the decedent, not for herself. Thus, equity waived the statutory bar of § 91-1-15 and opened a window to the extent that the illegitimate son should be allowed to prosecute his claim to be the illegitimate son of the deceased. The court remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order that dismissed as time-barred the illegitimate son's claim as the only direct heir of his deceased father's estate. The court remanded for further proceedings.

Blue v. State


93-DP-00534-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


674 So. 2d 1184; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 304



February 15, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of February 15, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Miss. LEXIS 19.



DISPOSITION: Blue's convictions and sentences are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder, armed robbery, and sexual battery in the Circuit Court of Leflore County (Mississippi), and he was sentenced to death plus 60 years of imprisonment. He sought reversal of his convictions and death sentence on 25 different grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant unsuccessfully challenged his murder conviction and death sentence. The court rejected all of defendant's four ineffective assistance claims related to counsel's failure to request an identical offense instruction, his alleged failure to fully utilize available mitigation evidence, and his allegedly deficient guilt-phase and penalty-phase closing arguments. It also rejected, again on the merits, defendant's 10 preserved non-ineffectiveness claims, pursuant to which defendant asserted that his custodial statement should have been suppressed, that an inflammatory videotape was admitted, that his prior conviction was improperly proved via event testimony rather than a certified record, that an unduly vague aggravator was relied upon at penalty phase, that he was improperly restricted in his presentation of mitigating evidence, that the penalty-phase instructions were erroneous, that death was a disproportionate punishment, and that cumulative error existed. Defendant's remaining 11 claims were deemed waived, and lacking in merit anyway.


OUTCOME: Defendant's murder conviction and death sentence were affirmed, with an execution date ordered set within 60 days. Defendant's convictions for armed robbery and sexual battery, and the aggregate 60-year confinement sentence were also upheld.

Holly v. State


No. 93-DP-00263-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


671 So. 2d 32; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 15



February 8, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Holly v. Mississippi, 518 U.S. 1025, 116 S. Ct. 2565, 135 L. Ed. 2d 1082, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 4179 (1996)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, Vacated by, in part Holly v. Mississippi, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 99256 (N.D. Miss., Mar. 23, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 6336 from Judgment dated MARCH 03, 1993, James C. Sumner RULING JUDGE, Grenada County Circuit Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Grenada County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder, kidnapping, and grand larceny and sentenced him to death. Defendant raised 16 alleged errors on appeal, including that because he was convicted of capital murder with armed robbery as the underlying offense, his conviction on the grand larceny charge constituted double jeopardy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 17 years old when he kidnapped, robbed at gunpoint, and killed a taxi driver and was convicted of kidnapping, grand larceny, and capital murder with armed robbery as the underlying offense. Defendant's alleged 16 errors regarding the guilt and sentencing phases of his capital murder and kidnapping convictions that the court found were either without merit or were procedurally barred. For example, the court held that being 17 years old at the time of the killing did not constitutionally preclude the death penalty nor was it necessary for the state to specifically instruct the jury on asportation to sustain a conviction for kidnapping. The court affirmed both his convictions on those charges and his death sentence. However, because the elements of grand larceny were included in the crime of robbery, once convicted of capital murder with armed robbery as the underlying offense, conviction on the grand larceny charge constituted double jeopardy under the particular circumstances of the case. For that reason, the court vacated defendant's sentence and conviction for the lesser included offense of grand larceny.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence as to the charges of kidnapping and capital murder because the assignments of error as to those charges were either without merit or procedurally barred. However, conviction on the grand larceny charge constituted double jeopardy, and as to that charge the court reversed and vacated the conviction.

 

27 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Jordan v. Smith


No. 92-CA-00151-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


669 So. 2d 752; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 8



February 5, 1996, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [**1] REVERSED AND RENDERED ON DIRECT APPEAL. AFFIRMED ON CROSS-APPEAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mayor and defendant city council both sought review of an order of the Chancery Court of Leflore County (Mississippi), which provided that under the mayor-council form of government, the mayor had exclusive power to appoint the city attorney and other municipal court personnel and that the council's voting on claims before they were paid did not infringe on the mayor's executive power over the city budget.


OVERVIEW: After adopting the mayor-council form of government under Miss. Code Ann. § 21-8-1 (1972) et seq., the mayor continued appointing municipal court personnel subject to city council confirmation and city council continued to vote on unpaid claims under earlier ordinances. When a conflict arose over appointment of a new city attorney, the mayor filed an action against the city council claiming he had exclusive authority to appoint a city attorney and administer the city budget. On appeal, the court reversed in part and affirmed in part, finding first that legislative and executive powers were separated under Miss. Code. Ann. § 21-8-9 (1972) and Miss. Code. Ann. 21-15-25 (1972) and vested the governing authorities with the power to appoint the city attorney. Thus, the ordinance requiring city council confirmation of appointments was still valid under the mayor-council form of government. Since Miss Code Ann. § 21-39-9 (1972) mandated actions on unpaid claims at each regularly scheduled meeting of the governing authorities, and the mayor did not meet with himself, the court held that the city council did not usurp executive authority over the city budget when it voted on unpaid claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the trial court's order that held that the mayor had exclusive authority to appoint the city attorney and court personnel. The court affirmed that portion of the trial court's order that held that the city council's voting on unpaid claims did not infringe on the mayor's executive authority over the city budget.

 

28 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Riley v. Jefferson Davis County


No. 92-CA-00848-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


669 So. 2d 748; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 11



February 5, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 7623 from Judgment dated JULY 27, 1992, Michael Ray Eubanks RULING JUDGE, Jefferson Davis County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Jefferson Davis County (Mississippi), which ruled in favor of appellee county and affirmed the judgment of the board of supervisors denying the landowner's petition for reduction or change of assessment and classifying his property as residential for tax purposes.


OVERVIEW: The landowner used his property, which was located in an area zoned for residential use, for growing trees. When he filed a petition to have the property rezoned as agricultural, the county tax assessor held that it was properly assessed as residential. The board affirmed the assessor's order, and the landowner appealed. The trial court affirmed the board's decision and overruled the petition for change of assessment. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision. The court held that the board improperly applied a reclassification test that focused on the use, assessment, and zoning of other lots located in the platted subdivision when assessing the landowner's lot. The court found that Miss. Code Ann. § 27-35-50(4) specifically required the assessment to be based on the current use of the property, regardless of the zoning in the subdivision. The court stated that the board erroneously created a discretion that did not exist and acted beyond its powers when it granted such discretion to the assessor. The court held that the erroneous assessment singled out the landowner as a class of taxpayer and was so disparate as to deny him equal protection of the law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court overruling the landowner's petition for reduction or change of assessment and affirming the board's assessment of the landowner's property as residential. The court remanded the cause for action consistent with its opinion.

McLemore v. State


No. 92-CT-00463-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


669 So. 2d 19; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 9



February 5, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 4438 from Judgement dated APRIL 22, 1992, Marcus D. Gordon RULING JUDGE, Newton County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR A NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the appellate court (Mississippi), which affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of aggravated assault and armed robbery, and sentencing defendant to prison.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of aggravated assault and armed robbery. Defendant was sentenced to prison and he appealed. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and defendant filed a petition for writ of certiorari. The court granted defendant's writ, reversed defendant's convictions for aggravated assault and armed robbery, and remanded to the lower court for a new trial. The court found that the district attorney, in closing arguments, improperly argued to the jury that defendant's four previous convictions for uttering forgery were substantive evidence of his guilt for the crime of armed robbery. Although defendant's prior convictions were brought up in his testimony and through his attorney during voir dire, the prosecution should only have been allowed to use the prior convictions for the limited purpose of impeaching defendant's credibility. The court also found that the trial court erred in denying defendant's request to present evidence of the police officers' bias and prejudice against him in his direct examination because evidence of bias, motive, or interest was relevant and it should not have mattered when defendant sought to introduce this evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for aggravated assault and armed robbery, and remanded to the lower court for a new trial.

Jackson v. State


No. 91-DP-01190-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


684 So. 2d 1213; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 7



January 18, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 10, 1996. As Corrected December 5, 1996. Rehearing Denied December 5, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Miss. LEXIS 702. Certiorari Denied May 12, 1996, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7.
Rehearing denied by Jackson v. State, 691 So. 2d 1026, 1996 Miss. LEXIS 702 (Miss., 1996)
Writ of certiorari denied Jackson v. Mississippi, 520 U.S. 1215, 117 S. Ct. 1703, 137 L. Ed. 2d 828, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2937 (1997)
Post-conviction relief granted at, Remanded by Jackson v. State, 1998 Miss. LEXIS 376 (Miss., Aug. 13, 1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at Jackson v. State, 860 So. 2d 653, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 355 (Miss., 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Request denied by, Certificate of appealability granted, in part, Certificate of appealability denied, in part Jackson v. Epps, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 102562 (N.D. Miss., Sept. 28, 2010)
Motion granted by Jackson v. State, 2012 Miss. LEXIS 273 (Miss., May 31, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Jackson v. State, 672 So. 2d 468, 1996 Miss. LEXIS 718 (Miss., 1996)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER (FOUR COUNTS) AND SENTENCE OF DEATH AFFIRMED. EXECUTION DATE TO BE SET WITHIN SIXTY DAYS OF FINAL DISPOSITION OF THIS CASE PURSUANT TO MISS. CODE ANN. § 99-19-105(7)(1972) AND M.R.A.P. 41(a).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Copiah County Circuit Court (Mississippi), for capital murder and four death sentences imposed, in connection with the stabbing deaths of his four young nieces and nephews, and aggravated assaults upon his sister and another niece while he was in search of money kept in a safe in his mother's home.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended, inter alia, that the presence of the sheriff, a witness for the state, in the courtroom throughout the proceedings violated Miss. R. Evid. 615, the rule of sequestration, and warranted reversal. The record indicated that the sheriff left the courtroom during the testimony of the chief deputy sheriff, who was the investigating officer, but that he was present during the testimony of a witness, whose testimony, defendant asserted, he was then called to rebut. The prosecutor merely stated that he felt that for security purposes the sheriff should be allowed to remain. The court found it appeared that the state was attempting to circumvent the sequestration rule when it made the apparently impromptu decision to designate the sheriff as its representative after defendant raised an objection to his presence in the courtroom at the beginning of voir dire. But defendant failed to demonstrate any prejudice resulting from the sheriff's presence or his testimony. The sheriff's "rebuttal" of the witness' testimony was limited, and the chief deputy sheriff corroborated the details. The court found there was no prejudice to defendant and any error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court found no errors warranting reversal and affirmed the conviction of capital murder and sentence of death.
