Jackson v. State


NO. 91-DP-01190-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


672 So. 2d 468; 1996 Miss. LEXIS 718



January 18, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Corrected by Jackson v. State, 684 So. 2d 1213, 1996 Miss. LEXIS 7 (Miss., 1996)

 

32 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Morrow v. Vinson


No. 92-CA-01296-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


666 So. 2d 802; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 620



December 14, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 32488 from Judgment dated OCTOBER 16, 1992, Roger C. Clapp RULING JUDGE, Rankin County Chancery Court.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant individuals sought review of the order of the Rankin County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which found against them and in favor of plaintiff trustees on the trustees' complaint that alleged certain sixteenth section leases should be declared void due to the gross inadequacy of consideration initially paid for the leases.


OVERVIEW: The individuals' predecessors obtained a leasehold fee on the property in question of one-half cent per square foot. Subsequently, the trustees of the county school board filed a complaint against the individuals, alleging that the certain sixteenth section leases should be declared void due to the gross inadequacy of consideration initially paid for the leases. The individuals argued that the trustees were equitably estopped from challenging the subject lease because they were on notice that the individuals were claiming under their leases, and the board suffered in silence for 33 years. The individuals further claimed that they went to great trouble and expense, in plain view of all, to permanently improve their lands. The trial court found in favor of the trustees and declared the lease void. The court affirmed the order, by holding that the board was not equitably estopped from asserting inadequacy of consideration for the lease of school trust land because the gross leasehold fee of one-half cent per square foot fell within the "grossly inadequate" standard so as to be an unconstitutional donation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, which found against the individuals and in favor of the trustees on their complaint, which alleged that certain sixteenth section leases should be declared void due to the gross inadequacy of consideration initially paid for the leases.

 

33 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Mississippi Transp. Comm'n v. Rector


NO. 93-IA-01329-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


663 So. 2d 601; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 579



November 9, 1995, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 10872211 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 01, 1993, Richard Wayne McKenzie RULING JUDGE, Forrest County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted an interlocutory appeal to review a decision of the Circuit Court of Forrest County, Mississippi, which denied a motion to dismiss by appellant Mississippi Transportation Commission (MTC). MTC claimed that it was protected by sovereign immunity from an action filed by appellees, a motorist and his wife. Appellees claimed that MTC had actual and constructive notice of a dangerous condition and failed to correct it.


OVERVIEW: The court previously reversed the trial court's earlier order that granted MTC's motion to dismiss based on sovereign immunity. The motorist was traveling on a highway and allegedly encountered standing water, which caused his vehicle to hydroplane out of control and into two pine trees. As a result of the accident, he suffered extensive head injuries leaving him permanently and totally disabled. The court determined that its earlier decision finding Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-1 et seq. unconstitutional was not to be applied retroactively. Thus, the court reversed and concluded that the defense of sovereign immunity was available to MTC on the date of the motorist's accident. There was nothing in the record to suggest that MTC waived this immunity. The court rejected the motorist's argument that if the court's earlier decision was prospective, then MTC was still not immune from suit because it did not have immunity for proprietary acts. This argument failed because the distinction between governmental and proprietary functions were applied only to municipalities and not to the state itself.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision that denied MTC's motion to dismiss.

 

34 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Nelson v. Mississippi State Bd. of Veterinary Medicine


NO. 92-CA-00509-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


662 So. 2d 1058; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 556



October 19, 1995, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 17147 from Judgment dated APRIL 23, 1992, Timothy Edward Ervin RULING JUDGE, Prentiss County Chancery Court.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant veterinarian sought review of a judgment of the Prentiss County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which affirmed an order of appellee board of veterinary medicine stripping the veterinarian of his license to practice because he violated Miss. Code Ann. § 73-39-19 (1972), claiming in part that the board's actions were arbitrary and capricious and violated his due process rights and the notice requirements of § 75-39-20, § 25-43-13.


OVERVIEW: The board revoked the veterinarian's license to practice on the grounds that he dispensed narcotics outside the ordinary course of his professional practice and was guilty of dishonorable and unethical conduct likely to harm the public. On appeal he raised claims of procedural and constitutional errors. The court affirmed the board's decision to revoke his license, ruling that the evidence clearly supported the board's ultimate finding that the veterinarian violated § 73-39-19(o), (s). He gave drugs to one person, injected another with drugs, sold the drugs, and traded them for sex. The court ruled that the board complied with the notice requirements in § 75-39-20, § 25-43-13. The veterinarian's state and federal due process rights also were not violated because § 73-39-19 was not vague, he had ample notice of the disciplinary hearing and the charges against him, he appeared and testified at the hearing, he had an attorney, he called witnesses, and he cross-examined the witnesses against him. The court also ruled that because the record clearly supported the board's finding, its failure to make specific rather than general findings did not impede the court's review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board's decision to revoke the veterinarian's license to practice veterinary medicine.

 

35 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Tower Loan of Miss., Inc. v. Mississippi State Tax Comm'n


94-CA-00508-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


662 So. 2d 1077; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 552



October 19, 1995, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 143024 from Judgment dated MAY 16, 1994, Pat Wise RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the judgment of the Chancery Court of the First Judicial District of Hinds County, Mississippi, which affirmed appellee Mississippi State Tax Commission's order and awarded a judgment against the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The Mississippi State Tax Commission had assessed the corporation additional franchise taxes. In affirming the judgment of the lower court, the court found that 1) the chancellor had correctly interpreted Miss. Code Ann. § 27-13-11, and her determination that the book value of accounts as employed by the corporation in conducting its normal business was based upon the equity method of accounting was not arbitrary and capricious, 2) the retained earnings of the subsidiary insurance companies were properly included by the commission in the corporation's franchise tax base, 3) the application of the equity method of accounting in determining the amount of franchise tax owed by a corporation did not result in prohibited double taxation, 4) the commission's position that holding companies should calculate their franchise tax base using the cost method of accounting for investments in subsidiaries did not require that the commission treat other corporations accordingly, and 5) the franchise tax statutes were not discriminatory because the corporation was required to pay franchise tax as would any other operating corporation which employed the equity method of accounting.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against the corporation.

 

36 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Mohundro v. Alcorn County


NO. 92-CA-00152-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1995 Miss. LEXIS 497



October 12, 1995, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal No. 90433FA from Judgment dated JANUARY 29, 1992, Barry Wayne Ford RULING JUDGE, Alcorn County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a motorist and his wife, sought review of a summary judgment from the Circuit Court of Alcorn County (Mississippi), which denied appellants damages from appellees, the county, the board of supervisors, and the supervisors' sureties, based on the allegation that the car that the motorist was driving fell into a hole in the road where the county had placed a culvert to replace a bridge.


OVERVIEW: Appellants claimed that the county was responsible for maintaining the culvert area and when rains had washed out the culvert area it was the duty of the county and its officials to keep people, as the motorist, from driving into the hole. Appellant further claimed the individual supervisors had qualified immunity and that the function of maintaining the roads was a discretionary function. The court held that the county had immunity from the claims, but that the individual supervisors had qualified immunity, and that the function of deciding to replace the bridge with a culvert was discretionary, so there was a genuine issue of material fact as to whether the supervisor in charge of the culvert had exceeded his authority or was so grossly negligent that his action were described as constructively intentional. The court further held that the bonding companies were only liable to the extent of their principals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment as to the county and the board of supervisors based on their sovereign immunity, but reversed the trial court's summary judgment in favor of the individual supervisors and their bonding companies and remanded that part of the proceeding to the trial court for proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

37 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Tighe v. Crosthwait


NO. 91-CA-00882-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


665 So. 2d 1337; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 500; 63 A.L.R.5th 807



October 12, 1995, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 38055 from Judgment dated JUNE 05, 1991, James E. Graves Jr. RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executor sought review of the order from the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which precluded the executor's questions during voir dire regarding the prejudicial effect of public campaigns concerning medical negligence and an insurance crisis. The executor had filed a wrongful death action against defendants, a doctor and a heart clinic.


OVERVIEW: The executor filed a wrongful death action against his father's doctor and the heart clinic alleging that they were liable for his death. Before the voir dire of jurors, the trial court sustained the doctor and heart clinic's objection to the line of questioning regarding medical negligence and insurance crisis. On appeal, the court held that while it was error to refuse to allow a party to question prospective jurors to determine whether they were biased, prejudiced, or had any interest in the outcome of the case, the executor's counsel was not free of limits during voir dire. The court held that the trial court erred in precluding the line of questioning because it might have exposed juror bias affecting their ability to render a fair and impartial verdict, but that the error was harmless because the advertisements in the case were geared toward reducing the amount of damages and at no point was it suggested that jurors should have found the doctor and heart clinic not liable. The court held that the focus of the advertisement was upon punitive damages, which were not sought by the executor and affirmed the order from the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court, which precluded the executor's questions during voir dire.

Walker v. Miss.


NO. 92-DP-00568-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


671 So. 2d 581; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 494



October 12, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 8, 1995. Certiorari Denied December 2, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 7236.
Rehearing denied by Walker v. State, 1996 Miss. LEXIS 201 (Miss., Apr. 18, 1996)
Writ of certiorari denied Walker v. Mississippi, 519 U.S. 1011, 117 S. Ct. 518, 136 L. Ed. 2d 406, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 7236 (1996)
Post-conviction relief denied at Walker v. State, 863 So. 2d 1, 2003 Miss. LEXIS 534 (Miss., 2003)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Walker v. Epps, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 78931 (N.D. Miss., Oct. 24, 2007)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Knox v. State, 75 So. 3d 1030, 2011 Miss. LEXIS 576 (Miss., 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Walker v. Epps, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 41604 (S.D. Miss., Mar. 27, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 25945 from Judgment dated AUGUST 12, 1991, Jerry Owen Terry Sr. RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH AFFIRMED. EXECUTION DATE TO BE SET WITHIN SIXTY DAYS OF FINAL DISPOSITION OF THIS CASE PURSUANT TO MISS. CODE ANN. § 99-19-105(F)(1972) AND M. R. A. P. 41(a).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found the defendant guilty of capital murder during the commission of sexual battery, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-95 (Supp. 1980). Upon the jury's vote that the death penalty be imposed, the Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi) sentenced the defendant to death by lethal injection, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-51(1) (Supp. 1987). The defendant filed 22 separate errors for appellate review.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was indicted for capital murder, rape, and kidnapping. He received a change of venue and was tried in another county, where a jury found him guilty as charged and sentenced him to death on the capital murder count. The defendant was also convicted of the rape and kidnapping and received additional sentences by the trial judge of 30 and 35 years to run consecutively. On appeal, the court noted that most of the issues raised were either procedurally barred or without merit, however, proceeded to address certain issues raised, including whether there was sufficient evidence of felonious intent and that the sexual battery occurred in substantial temporal and factual relation to the murder to support a capital murder conviction, whether the police officers' search exceeded the scope of their warrant, and whether defendant met his burden of showing a pattern of purposeful discrimination as to trigger a Batson analysis. After considering those issues, the court found that the defendant received a fair trial, conducted a proportionality review under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-105(3)(c), and affirmed the conviction and sentence of death.


OUTCOME: The conviction of capital murder and sentence of death was affirmed because it was supported by substantial evidence.

 

39 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Fortson v. Hargett


92-KP-00851-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


662 So. 2d 633; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 495



October 5, 1995, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 923066 from Judgement dated JULY 17, 1992, Howard Q. Davis Jr. RULING JUDGE, Sunflower County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Sunflower County, Mississippi, which dismissed as time-barred his petition for post-conviction collateral relief and motion for reinstatement of parole alleging unlawful and unconstitutional revocation of parole. Shortly after his release on parole from his life sentence for murder, the prisoner was arrested. Although charges were dismissed, the prisoner's parole was revoked.


OVERVIEW: The court observed that pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) (1994), cases in which a prisoner claimed that his parole or conditional release had been unlawfully revoked were exempt from the Post-Conviction Relief Act's three-year statute of limitations. The court found, therefore, that the trial court erred in dismissing the prisoner's petition as time-barred. The prisoner had alleged that his parole had been revoked without probable cause, that the sole basis of the revocation was an arrest, and that the charges filed pursuant to the arrest had been dismissed for lack of evidence. Accordingly, the prisoner argued that appellee parole board's revocation of his parole had been illegal and unconstitutional. The court rejected the State's argument that in cases of parole revocation the three-year statute of limitations began at the time of the parole revocation. The court pointed out that the unambiguous language of Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) exempted a challenge of revocation of parole from the Post-Conviction Relief Act's three-year statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause.

 

40 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Logan v. State


NO. 92-KP-00667-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


661 So. 2d 1137; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 482



September 28, 1995, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 11103 from Judgment dated APRIL 22, 1992, Richard Wayne McKenzie RULING JUDGE, Forrest County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: LOWER COURT'S DENIAL OF MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF IS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of a judgment of the Forrest County Circuit Court, Mississippi, which denied his petition for post-conviction relief as time-barred. Appellant had filed his petition some eight years after having been convicted for armed robbery, arguing that his ineligibility for parole for a period of 10 years was cruel and unusual punishment and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected appellant's argument that Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-3(1)(d) (Supp. 1994), under which he was sentenced and which provided that no person convicted thereunder was eligible for parole until they had served 10 years, was in violation of the Eighth Amendment. Appellant argued that no other crime of violence imposed such minimum requirement and that the statute did not make a distinction between armed robbery cases where individuals were harmed and where there was no harm to the victims, as in appellant's case. The court noted that the maximum sentence allowed under the armed robbery statute was life imprisonment, which had been held not to be so disproportionate as to constitute cruel and unusual punishment. Logically, then, appellant's 23-year sentence could not cruel and unusual, nor could the statutory requirement that he serve 10 years of the sentence. The court held that, in any event, the petition was time-barred, noting that the wrongful-revocation-of-parole exception of Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) cited by appellant could not apply because appellant had never been paroled nor conditionally released; thus, there could be no wrongful revocation of parole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

41 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Marshall v. State


NO. 92-KA-00606-SCT CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 92-KA-00909-SCT, NO. 92-KA-01294-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


662 So. 2d 566; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 492



September 28, 1995, DECIDED



DISPOSITION:  [**1] OBJECTION AND/OR MOTION THAT THE CASES NOT BE REMANDED OR ASSIGNED TO THE COURT OF APPEALS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted of sexual battery, kidnapping, and manslaughter. Both appealed, their appeals were deflected to the Court of Appeals (Mississippi) pursuant to the screening process established under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 9-4-1 to 9-4-17 (Supp. 1994), and they filed motions that the cases not be remanded or assigned to that court.


OVERVIEW: After defendants were convicted of sexual battery, kidnapping, and manslaughter, they appealed their convictions. When their cases were deflected to the appellate court, they filed motions that the cases not be remanded or assigned to that court on the grounds that by establishing the appellate court, the Mississippi Legislature had unconstitutionally usurped the power of the Supreme Court of Mississippi. The court overruled defendant's objections and denied their motions, holding that Miss. Code Ann. §§ 9-4-1 to -17 did not violate Miss. Const. art. 6, §§ 144, 146, 172 because the appellate court was of the same character as the supreme court. Further, the Mississippi Legislature had the power to create a court of the same type and character as any other constitutionally created court. Moreover, the language of Miss. Code Ann. § 9-4-3 made it clear that the appellate court was not co-equal to the supreme court because it did not have original jurisdiction and was subject to limited certiorari by the supreme court.


OUTCOME: The court overruled the objections and denied the motions that defendants' cases not be remanded or assigned to the appellate court.

Ballenger v. State


No. 93-DP-00081-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


667 So. 2d 1242; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 451



September 21, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 22, 1995. Second Correction January 8, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 8337 from Judgment dated JANUARY 13, 1993, Marcus D. Gordon RULING JUDGE, Leake County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH BY LETHAL INJECTION AFFIRMED. WEDNESDAY, OCTOBER 25, 1995, SET FOR INFLICTION OF THE DEATH PENALTY AS PROVIDED BY LAW.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of conviction entered in, and the sentence of lethal injection imposed by, the Leake County Circuit Court (Mississippi) following her jury trial for capital murder while engaged in the commission of the crime of robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed after she was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to die by lethal injection. The court held that: (1) the pre-trial publicity was not so pervasive as to have infected the venire; (2) defendant was not denied her right to voir dire the jurors on the issue of pre-trial publicity; (3) defendant was not improperly denied discovery of grand jury testimony of witnesses; (4) the testimony of the co-conspirator was sufficient to convict defendant because the testimony concerning defendant's participation in the crime was not unreasonable, self-contradictory, or substantially impeached; (5) the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in allowing leading questions during the trial; (6) defendant's age at the time she would be eligible for parole, if given a life sentence, was speculative and was properly withheld from the jury; (7) the jury was not impermissibly precluded from considering sympathy for defendant during the sentencing phase; and (8) under the facts involved, and when compared with similar cases, the death penalty was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of capital murder and the sentence of death by lethal injection. The court set a date for defendant's execution.

Moore v. Board of Supervisors


No. 94-CA-00113-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


658 So. 2d 883; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 366



July 20, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 152094 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 29, 1993, Joe B. Moss RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee board of supervisors brought an action, pursuant to Miss. R. Civ. P. 57, against appellee judges, seeking declaratory relief. The First Judicial District of Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi) entered a decree granting the board's motion for declaratory judgment. The judges appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the action, the board sought to determine the constitutionality of Miss. Code Ann. §§ 43-21-119 and 43-21-123 under Miss. Const. art. 1, §§ 1, 2. The board contended the judges' ability to participate in the development and implementation of the budget as approved by the board demonstrated an encroachment by the judges into executive powers of the board. The trial court agreed and the judges appealed. On review, the court reversed because the judges and their respective employees did not perform any core executive functions and the board failed to prove Miss. Code Ann. §§ 43-21-119 and 43-21-123 were unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt when evaluated in the light of the heavy presumption of constitutionality afforded a statute passed by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decree granting the board's motion for declaratory judgment and rendered judgment in favor of the judges.

 

44 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Hill v. State


No. 93-DP-00392-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


659 So. 2d 547; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 338



June 29, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at: 659 So.2d 547 at 550.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 3427 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 26, 1980, Andrew Cleveland Baker RULING JUDGE, DeSoto County Circuit Court.

Original Opinion of December 21, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Miss. LEXIS 635.



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR REHEARING DENIED. REMANDED FOR A NEW RESENTENCING HEARING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state petitioned for rehearing after the case was remanded for a new sentencing hearing to the DeSoto County Circuit Court (Mississippi), after a finding that defendant was improperly sentenced to death using the unconstitutionally vague "heinous, atrocious, and cruel" aggravator without a limiting instruction.


OVERVIEW: The state's petition for rehearing concerned the retroactive application of statutory changes in the Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-105 (Supp. 1994) and the court's analysis of whether those changes violated the principle of ex post facto laws. In the original opinion, the court held that defendant was improperly sentenced to death using the unconstitutionally vague "heinous, atrocious and cruel" aggravator, without a limiting instruction. The court also held that, consistent with its prior decisions, it lacked the state statutory and constitutional authority to reweigh a flawed jury verdict. The court then remanded the case to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing. The state petitioned for a rehearing and the court held that the changes in Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-105 (Supp. 1994) affected a substantive right of defendant, which was his right to be sentenced under the statute existing on the date of his offense. The court concluded that the changes were barred under Miss. Const. art. III, § 16, the state constitutional provisions against ex post facto law.


OUTCOME: The court denied the state's petition for rehearing and remanded the case for a new resentencing hearing in favor of defendant.

 

45 of 825 DOCUMENTS


TOUART v. JOHNSTON


No. 93-CA-0 1310-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


656 So. 2d 318; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 273



June 8, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 9352183 from Judgment dated OCTOBER 14, 1993, Joe N. Pigott RULING JUDGE, Jackson County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, individuals and a county board of supervisors, appealed from the dismissal of their writ of prohibition sought in the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi) against the Youth Court Judge of Jackson County. At the conclusion of the testimony an order was entered by the ruling judge, dismissing the complaint and assessing the board costs. The board's motion for reconsideration or, in the alternative, for clarification was denied.


OVERVIEW: The youth court judge and the board of supervisors had each hired an administrator for the essentially the same administrative position in the youth court. The court first refused to examine the issue of whether Mississippi's Youth Court Act was unconstitutional because the issue had not been raised at trial. The issue of whether the youth court judge had the authority to hire a new youth court administrator could be determined without considering the constitutionality of the Youth Court Act. The court ruled that appellants' claims had no merit and affirmed the dismissal of the writ. Statutory authority for the appointment of a youth court administrator was clearly granted only to the youth court judge. The court examined the relevant provisions of the Youth Court Act, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 43-21-101, et seq., (Supp. 1979), and held that the youth court judge complied with all appropriate statutes in his appointment of a replacement youth court administrator. The court found that appellants' argument concerning whether the board had statutory authority to hire a youth court facilities administrator was totally devoid of merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

46 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Nicholson ex rel. Gollott v. State


No. 91-KA-00511-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1995 Miss. LEXIS 263



June 1, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal No. 6273 from Judgment dated FEBRUARY 16, 1991, Kosta N. Vlahos RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF MANSLAUGHTER AND SENTENCE OF FIFTEEN YEARS WITH THREE YEARS SUSPENDED MAKING A TOTAL OF TWELVE YEARS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Harrison County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District (Mississippi) convicted defendant of manslaughter and sentenced him to 15 years in prison with 3 years suspended. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that he accidentally shot his ex-wife while he was attempting to commit suicide. Defendant alleged that the circuit clerk illegally assisted the prosecutor in selecting the jurors. The court held that there was no impropriety in the jury selection. The prosecutor conducted jury voir dire and made decisions relative to changes. The circuit clerk simply provided background information about jurors at the prosecutor's request. The same information was available to defendant. The court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion for a directed verdict because the record supported a finding that the shooting was not accidental and was at least manslaughter. Eye witness testimony and forensic evidence conflicted with defendant's version of the circumstances of the shooting. The court held that the trial court did not err in rejecting defendant's proffered jury instruction on murder and that an accident defense was inapplicable. Because the shooting occurred as a result of the unlawful act of suicide, the death was not an accident. The court held that defendant failed to substantiate his allegation that the trial judge should have recused himself.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

47 of 825 DOCUMENTS


King v. State


No. 94-DP-00216-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


656 So. 2d 1168; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 264



June 1, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 6716 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 05, 1980, HARVEY S. BUCK RULING JUDGE, Lowndes County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO FILE MOTION TO VACATE CONVICTION AND DEATH SENTENCE IS GRANTED; MOTION TO VACATE CONVICTION AND DEATH SENTENCE GRANTED IN PART AND DENIED IN PART; MOTION TO CONDUCT REWEIGHING OR HARMLESS ERROR ANALYSIS IS DENIED; CASE REMANDED FOR A NEW SENTENCING HEARING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner condemned prisoner moved to set aside his murder conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner condemned prisoner moved to set aside his murder conviction and death sentence. The court denied the motion as to petitioner's conviction, finding all of the grounds asserted to have been procedurally defaulted, while granting it as to his death sentence. A new sentencing hearing was therefore ordered. As to petitioner's conviction claims, the court noted that this was petitioner's third foray into the state judicial system, and thus he was obliged to have raised his new challenges to his conviction in earlier proceedings. His failure to do so barred appellate review. As to petitioner's sentencing claims, the court held that a federal circuit court's decision that the jury instructions on aggravating factors were unconstitutional was a decision that must be obeyed. The court also declined respondent state government's invitation to reweigh the aggravators and mitigators itself. Accordingly, petitioner's case was remanded to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The motion to set aside the murder conviction was denied, with all grounds raised therein being deemed procedurally defaulted. The motion to set aside the death sentence was granted, inasmuch as a federal court had ordered resentencing. The case was remanded for a new death penalty hearing.

 

48 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


No. 91-KA-00676-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


656 So. 2d 104; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 281



June 1, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 90380CRC from Judgment dated MAY 29, 1991, William F. Coleman RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment by the Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which convicted defendant of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. The issues on appeal were the sufficiency of the evidence on the question of intent and whether the brother of an assistant prosecutor for the district in question could survive a challenge for cause.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the evidence of intent was non-existent and that the challenge for cause should have been sustained. The court reversed and remanded the case for a new trial on the issue of possession of a controlled substance. A jury could not have reasonably inferred that defendant was in possession of crack cocaine with intent to distribute. Although defendant was in an area known for the sale of crack cocaine, in the presence of a drug dealer, with one hand extended into a car and money in the other hand, those circumstances were not sufficient for a jury to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant intended to distribute crack cocaine, as opposed to purchasing the drug. The fact that defendant was in a drug area and leaning into a car might have been indicative of a drug transaction, it gave no clue as to the identity of the seller. While the court could not guarantee defendant a perfect trial, it had to endeavor to ensure that defendant received a fair trial free of implied bias that arose from the presence of a juror who was related to an attorney employed by the district attorney's office that was prosecuting defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed and rendered as to possession with intent to distribute and reversed and remanded as to the offense of possession of cocaine.

 

49 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Associated Press v. Bost


No. 92-CA-00332-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


656 So. 2d 113; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 284; 23 Media L. Rep. 2017



June 1, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 917086 from Judgment dated MARCH 19, 1992, James E. Graves Jr. RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, members of the press (press), appealed from the order of the Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi) holding that Miss. Code Jud. Conduct Canon 3(A)(7), which prevented cameras in the courtroom except under specific circumstances, was constitutionally valid.


OVERVIEW: The press brought an action against defendant, the chairman of the Mississippi Commission on Judicial Performance, seeking to invalidate Canon 3(A)(7) on the basis that it was unconstitutional. The trial court found that the Canon was constitutional, and on appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that Canon 3(A)(7) did not conflict with Miss. Unif. Crim. Rules. Cir. Ct. Prac. 8.06, which was a later pronouncement by the court on camera coverage, and, thus, was not impliedly repealed. Further, the court held that Miss. Code Jud. Conduct Canon 3(A)(7) did not violate the press's First Amendment right to attend and report on public trials and did not discriminate against the electronic media by preventing them from reporting the news. The court found that Canon 3(A)(7) survived rational basis scrutiny because it did not violate any fundamental constitutional rights of the press, and the legitimate and rational reasons for the its existence included the state's interest in preserving order and decorum in the courtroom, preserving the truth-seeking function of a trial, and protecting a defendant's rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order finding that the Canon preventing cameras in the courtroom was constitutional.

 

50 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Murrell v. State


No. 91-KA-01245-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


655 So. 2d 881; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 234



April 27, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal No. 4431 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 10, 1991, Marcus D. Gordon RULING JUDGE, Newton County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision from the Newton County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of assault in the context of resisting an arrest.


OVERVIEW: When police officers attempted to arrest defendant pursuant to a warrant, defendant pushed the police officer and made threats that he would not be handcuffed. The trial court convicted him of simple assault under Miss Code Ann. 97-3-7(1) after it had denied a request for a lesser included offense of resisting arrest and an instruction concerning whether defendant had a right to resist an unlawful arrest. Defendant asserted that the prosecution had failed to prove the offense of simple assault. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial because it determined that the prosecution had not proved that any bodily injury had been suffered as a result of the incident. The court stated that there had been no medical evidence and the police officer had failed to testify that he suffered any injury. The court determined that the trial court erred in failing to allow the lesser included offense of resisting arrest, which could have been completely shown without an assertion that bodily injury had occurred. The court concluded that there was no right to resist a good faith arrest when defendant had no basis to believe that the warrant was issued in bad faith.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the conviction of defendant for assault of a police officer during an arrest for a new trial.

 

51 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Stewart


No. 91-CA-00454-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


655 So. 2d 866; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 223



April 20, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal No. 916791 from Judgment dated APRIL 10, 1991, James E. Graves Jr. RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT IS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist sought review of a decision from the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed her complaint against appellees, state university and an employee, in the motorist's action for personal injuries that resulted from a car accident with the employee. The trial court dismissed the complaint based upon sovereign immunity under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The motorist was in a car accident and sought damages from the state university and the employee. The trial court dismissed the action. On appeal, the motorist argued that the sovereign immunity statutes were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal. The court held that its prior decision that declared the codified principle of sovereign immunity unconstitutional in 1992 did not apply retroactively because the Mississippi Constitution erected no barriers against legislation and it was the legislative branch's prerogative to address limitations upon actions against government entities. Additionally, the court held that the principle of sovereign immunity did not violate the due process clause of the state or federal constitutions because there was no infringement of a liberty or property right. The legislature had withheld that right through its statutes and there was no property right to bring an action against the state. Finally, the court was not able to reach a decision on the university employee's immunity because service of process was never obtained on the employee, and therefore the court lacked jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the motorist's personal injury action against the state university and the employee for damages that resulted from a car accident.

 

52 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Billiot v. State


No. 91-KA-00862-SCT


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


655 So. 2d 1; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 88



February 16, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: The Docket Number of this Case has been Corrected March 30, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 18761 from Judgment dated MAY 16, 1989, James E. Thomas RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: THE LOWER COURT'S JUDGMENT DENYING BILLIOT'S MOTION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF ENTERED BY THE FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARRISON COUNTY IS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. He filed a motion for post-conviction relief, claiming that he was not competent to be executed, and the Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi) denied his motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a mental disorder and claimed that it rendered him incompetent to be executed. At the evidentiary hearing, there was conflicting expert testimony on the issue of his competency. All of the experts acknowledged that it was possible for a person with such a disorder to be competent to be executed. Defendant claimed that the lower court erred by not shifting to the state the burden of proof regarding his competency because there was substantial evidence showing that he was incompetent to be executed. The court upheld the lower court's finding that defendant was competent to be executed. In so holding, the court ruled that (1) defendant was not entitled to a de novo review of the lower court's finding of competency; (2) the lower court's reliance on the testimony of experts that evaluated defendant several months prior to the hearing did not constitute reversible error; (3) under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-23(7), defendant had the burden of proving by a preponderance of the evidence that he was incompetent to be executed; and (4) the lower court's finding that defendant was competent was not against the overwhelming weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion for post-conviction relief.

Giles v. State

SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


650 So. 2d 846; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 62

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR A NEW TRIAL. SENTENCE IS VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Jones County, Second Judicial District, Mississippi, which convicted him for capital murder. In a separate hearing, he was sentenced to death. He alleged that the trial court erred when it refused to grant him an instruction embodying his only theory of defense, and that his right to a speedy trial under both Miss. Const. art. III, § 26 and the federal constitution, had been abridged.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for killing his wife while engaged in the commission of a sexual battery, thus constituting capital murder under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-99 (Supp. 1992). On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the error required reversal because the refusal to grant the instruction deprived defendant of instructing the jury as to his only theory of defense. Further, although not reversible error, the ruled on defendant's claim that he was denied a speedy trial. The court held that the State provided legitimate and justifiable reasons for the delay, and defendant suffered no undue prejudice in the delay.

Carr v. State


No. 90-DP-01106


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


655 So. 2d 824; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 56



February 2, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Carr v. State, 1995 Miss. LEXIS 340 (Miss., June 22, 1995)
Writ of certiorari denied Bivins v. Indiana, 516 U.S. 1077, 133 L. Ed. 2d 734, 116 S. Ct. 783, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 547 (1996)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Application granted by, in part, Application denied by, in part Carr v. State, 2004 Miss. LEXIS 544 (Miss., May 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 5115 from Judgment dated SEPTEMBER 19, 1990, Elzy Jonathan Smith Jr. RULING JUDGE, Quitman County Circuit Court.
Simon v. Mississippi, 513 U.S. 956, 130 L. Ed. 2d 329, 115 S. Ct. 413, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 7532 (1994)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER (FOUR COUNTS) AND SENTENCE OF DEATH BY LETHAL INJECTION AFFIRMED. WEDNESDAY, MARCH 8, 1995, SET FOR INFLICTION OF THE DEATH PENALTY AS PROVIDED BY LAW.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Quitman County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of four counts of capital murder and which sentenced him to death by lethal injection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that one of the jury instructions violated the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment because it relieved the State of the burden of proving that defendant had the intent to commit the underlying felonies. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence and held that because defendant failed to object at trial to the instruction, the objection was not properly preserved for review. The court held that even without the procedural bar, the claim was meritless. The court held that the statement defendant made to the police officer was properly excluded in the guilt phase under Miss. R. Evid. 804(b)(3). The court held that testimony regarding defendant's polygraph test was properly excluded because Mississippi law clearly stated that polygraph tests and their results were inadmissible. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to grant a mercy jury instruction. The court held that the jury was adequately instructed that before it could sentence defendant to death, it had to weigh mitigating circumstances against aggravating circumstances, and, only if the latter outweighed the former, could it return a sentence of death.


OUTCOME: The judgment that convicted defendant and sentenced him to death was affirmed.

Fordice v. Thomas


No. 93-CA-01126


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


649 So. 2d 835; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 34



January 26, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 927438 from Judgment dated JUNE 08, 1993, James E. Graves Jr. RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL: AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED IN PART FOR PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION. ON CROSS-APPEAL: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, governor, department of environmental quality, and environmental quality permit board, sought review of a judgment from the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which enjoined appellants from reviewing hazardous waste permit applications under an illegal and void Capacity Assurance Plan (CAP). Appellee residents cross-appealed the denial of attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellees alleged that the governor engaged in rulemaking under state law and that the governor violated appellees' rights to take part in the rulemaking process under the state Administrative Procedures Law (APL), Miss. Code Ann. § 25-43-1 et seq., because he failed to give notice of his plans to adopt the CAP before submission to the EPA. The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court in all respects except the breadth of the injunction. The court concluded that the APL applied to rule-making by the governor and that the adoption of the CAP, as provided for in federal "Superfund" legislation, was such a rule within the APL. Further, the court determined that the circuit court did not err in concluding that there was a failure to comply with the APL. The court, however, found that the injunctive relief granted by the circuit court was overbroad and, thus, remanded for modification of the judgment. The court determined that appellants should be allowed to proceed with the permitting processes as they related to the non-CAP factors. The court rejected appellees' request to adopt the private attorney general rule as to attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's declaration that the CAP was illegal and void. The court affirmed the judgment in all respects except the breadth of the injunction. The court remanded for entry of a judgment modified to clarify the injunction.

Mack v. State


No. 91-DP-00764


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


650 So. 2d 1289; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 638



December 21, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 7344 from Judgment dated JUNE 29, 1991, Elzy Jonathan Smith Jr. RULING JUDGE, Bolivar County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH BY LETHAL INJECTION AFFIRMED. WEDNESDAY, JANUARY 25, 1995, SET FOR INFLICTION OF THE DEATH PENALTY AS PROVIDED BY LAW.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a jury's judgment in the Bolivar County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District (Mississippi) convicting him of the crime of capital murder and sentencing him to death by lethal injection.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was indicted for the crime of capital murder after being accused of killing a man by repeated blows to the head during a robbery at his home. The defendant pled not guilty, but the jury returned a guilty verdict and sentenced him to death by lethal injection. He appealed both the conviction and the sentence, contending the prosecution used its peremptory challenges in an unconstitutional manner to exclude potential black jurors, there were other problems with the jury venire, the prosecutor committed misconduct in his closings, the court failed to properly instruct the jury, and decisions related to the admission of evidence at his sentencing were error. The court found while evidence of the defendant's flight was improperly entered, it paled in comparison to more direct evidence of guilt. Its admission was harmless error. Moreover, the defendant's Batson challenges were rejected. Also, the prosecutor's remark did not rise to a level to suggest to the jury that someone other than the jury had the power to decide the defendant's sentence. Finally, even in the aggregate, any possible errors did not rise to the level of reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of capital murder and sentence of death.

 

57 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Hill v. State


No. 93-DP-00392


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


659 So. 2d 547; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 635



December 21, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 29, 1995, Reported at: 659 So.2d 547 at 550; 1995 Miss. LEXIS 338.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 3427 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 26, 1980, Andrew Cleveland Baker RULING JUDGE, DeSoto County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: HILL'S APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO FILE MOTION TO VACATE CONVICTION DENIED. HILL'S APPLICATION FOR LEAVE TO FILE MOTION TO VACATE DEATH SENTENCE GRANTED AND REMANDED TO THE CIRCUIT COURT OF DESOTO COUNTY FOR A NEW SENTENCING HEARING. HILL'S MOTION TO STAY PROCEEDINGS DENIED. HILL'S MOTION FOR LEAVE TO PROCEED IN FORMA PAUPERIS GRANTED. STATE'S MOTION TO EXPEDITE DENIED. STATE'S MOTION TO FILE SUPPLEMENTAL BRIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. The conviction and sentence were affirmed by the court on direct appeal. The Fifth Circuit entered an order postponing any decision on the inmate's second petition for rehearing and suggestion for rehearing en banc pending appellee state's resolution of the inmate's then pending third state court petition for post-conviction relief. Before the court was that petition.


OVERVIEW: The "especially, heinous, atrocious or cruel" aggravating factor found in Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101 (5)(h) was submitted to the jury for consideration without a limiting or definitional instruction. The United States Supreme Court had since held that such an omission was error and potentially fatal to a death sentence. The court's task in death penalty cases where, as in the inmate's case, an unconstitutionally vague aggravator was submitted to the jury, was to review, not reweigh, the weighing of aggravating circumstances being a jury function pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101. The court's holding in three specified cases was viable precedent for vacating the death sentence and remanding the case to a state trial court for a new sentencing hearing. The court also determined that consideration and reconsideration of the inmate's allegation that he was entitled to relief from the guilt-finding phase because he was denied certain lesser included offense instructions was barred because the identical issue was considered and decided adversely to him on direct appeal and again on a motion for leave to file a writ of error coram nobis.


OUTCOME: The court granted the inmate's motion for leave to proceed in forma pauperis, his application for leave to file a motion to vacate death sentence, and his motion to vacate death sentence. The court also vacated the inmate's death sentence, denied his motion to stay proceedings, denied the state's motion to expedite, and remanded the case to a state trial court for a new sentencing hearing.

Morreale v. Morreale


Nos. 90-CA-00702, 90-CA-01046


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


646 So. 2d 1264; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 634



December 21, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal No. 18960 from Judgment dated MAY 21, 1990, Jason H. Floyd Jr. RULING JUDGE, Hancock County Chancery Court.

Appeal No. 18960 from Judgment dated AUGUST 17, 1990, John S. Morris RULING JUDGE, Hancock County Chancery Court.

Original Opinion of March 31, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Miss. LEXIS 198.



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR REHEARING DENIED IN PART, GRANTED IN PART. THE JUDGMENT OF THE CHANCERY COURT IS AFFIRMED ON DIRECT APPEAL AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS ON CROSS APPEAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband petitioned for rehearing from the judgment of the Hancock County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which assessed attorney's fees on remand in connection with the first of two judgments in favor of appellee wife. The husband contended that attorneys' fees were awarded for that work in the second judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court denied husband's petition for rehearing on all grounds except with respect to the attorney fee issue. A request for attorney's fees had been made in the complaint that engendered the chancery court's first judgment. The court's original opinion found an abuse of discretion by the chancery court in failing to award attorney fees. However, the court concluded on rehearing that the chancery court apparently never had an opportunity to consider attorney's fees with respect to a request for a specific amount prior to the second judgment. The court withdrew that portion of the original opinion finding an abuse of discretion in the failure to have awarded fees in the first judgment. To the extent that the chancellor's failure to award attorney's fees in the first order was an oversight that was not cured by the second award, the court remanded the matter for further proceedings. On remand, the chancery court could consider questions concerning waiver, timeliness, and the like, as well as the merits of the claim for attorney's fees and the effect of the second order, if necessary.


OUTCOME: The court granted the husband's petition for rehearing with respect to the attorney fee issue and otherwise denied the petition. The court affirmed the judgment of the chancery court on the direct appeal and remanded the judgment for further proceedings on the cross-appeal.

SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI

DISPOSITION: DENIAL OF POST CONVICTION RELIEF AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant challenged a judgment of the Warren County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief following his conviction upon his guilty pleas and sentencing for two counts of robbery, one count of burglary, and one count of grand larceny.


OVERVIEW: The trial court accepted movant's pleas of guilty to two counts of robbery, one count of burglary, and one count of grand larceny and imposed sentence. Movant filed a motion for post-conviction collateral relief to vacate and set aside his guilty pleas, conviction, and sentence. Following an evidentiary hearing, the trial court dismissed the motion. The absence of a prosecutor at the hearing appeared only to harm the State. Movant failed to show how his position was damaged by the absence of a prosecutor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which denied movant's petition for post-conviction relief.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner sought review of a judgment from the Green County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed his pro se prisoner in form pauperis civil rights complaint against defendants, the corrections department commissioner, the corrections department superintendent, and three doctors.


OVERVIEW: After being convicted for grand larceny, burglary, and armed robbery, the prisoner was housed in the state penitentiary. During his imprisonment, the prisoner contracted inactive tuberculosis. In substance, the prisoner asserted that defendants had knowledge of the contagious tuberculosis of an inmate he was housed with. The prisoner further alleged that after acquisition of such knowledge, defendants failed to provide proper care, housing, and medical treatment, which the prisoner suggested would have prevented him from contracting inactive tuberculosis. Upon review, the appellate court found that since the complaint was legally insufficient as a matter of law, the trial court judge did not commit reversible error in dismissing the prisoner's complaint. The trial court's utilization of the Spears evidentiary hearing was proper in determining whether the prisoner's complaint was frivolous. The subsequent dismissal of the prisoner's complaint was proper under Miss. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(6) and the frivolous standard because the prisoner failed to prove that any action of defendants caused him to contract tuberculosis from the other inmate.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the prisoner's complaint against defendants for improper care, housing, and medical treatment, and held that defendant failed to prove that defendants' actions caused him to contract tuberculosis.

Ghoston v. State


No. 91-KA-00384


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


645 So. 2d 936; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 547



November 17, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 8049 from Judgment dated MARCH 21, 1991, Marcus D. Gordon RULING JUDGE, Neshoba County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Neshoba County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor (DUI), and charged him with a felony because of defendant's three prior DUI convictions.


OVERVIEW: The indictment charged that defendant had three prior DUI convictions. Defendant was found guilty at a second jury trial. At the sentencing hearing, the State offered abstracts of court records attesting to defendant's three prior convictions for DUI. Defendant testified that when he pled guilty to the prior charges, he was not represented by counsel, nor was he given warnings as to possible enhanced punishment if charged with a similar offense in the future. Defendant claimed that he was not aware that he could be charged with a felony. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. Defendant's prior convictions were admissible at the sentencing hearing for enhancement of his punishment. Defendant was unsuccessful in overcoming the presumption of validity accorded his earlier DUI convictions, and lack of counsel did not render a conviction arising from a guilty plea irregular or otherwise unfit for purposes of sentence enhancement. The introduction of defendant's prior convictions at the sentencing hearing did not violate Miss. Unif. Crim. R. Cir. Ct. P. 4.06 since defendant was on notice that the State would use these convictions to enhance his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Duplantis v. State


No. 91-DP-01220


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


644 So. 2d 1235; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 529



October 27, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 4414 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 04, 1991, Marcus D. Gordon RULING JUDGE, Newton County Circuit Court


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Newton County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied defendant's motion for a new trial. Defendant was convicted of murder during the commission of a robbery in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e), adjudicated a habitual offender pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81, and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant escaped from a Mississippi jail and subsequently murdered an individual. Defendant was apprehended in Tennessee on unrelated charges and Tennessee law enforcement officials began interrogating defendant. Mississippi law enforcement officials arrived and obtained a confession of the murder. Defendant was convicted of murder during the commission of a robbery, adjudicated a habitual offender, and sentenced to death; the trial court denied his motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court stated that defendant previously requested an attorney and had not initiated a conversation with Mississippi officers, therefore the confession was inadmissible. The court ruled the Mississippi officers were not entitled to subject defendant to further interrogation unless counsel had been made available or defendant initiated further communication. The court also held extradition was not improper, peremptory challenges strikes were not unconstitutional, and the admission of evidence of other crimes was proper. The court further stated that the state made discovery available in a timely manner and other contentions of error were barred, meritless, or moot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court, which denied defendant's motion for a new trial. The court reversed defendant's conviction for murder during the commission of a robbery, adjudication as a habitual offender, and sentence of death.

Wells by Wells v. Panola County Bd. of Educ.


No. 91-CA-00101


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


645 So. 2d 883; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 508



October 13, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. B8906183 from Judgment dated JANUARY 15, 1991, Leon E. Hannaford Sr. RULING JUDGE, Panola County Chancery Court, Second Judicial District


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant student sought review of a decision of the Panola County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which dismissed his suit for compensatory and punitive damages against appellee school board pursuant to a 12(b)(6) motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim. Appellant was severely injured in a school bus accident but the trial court held that the Mississippi Accident Contingency Fund, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 37-41-39 and 37-41-41, was controlling.


OVERVIEW: Appellant student was severely injured in a school bus accident and incurred more than $ 600,000 in medical expenses. Appellant brought suit against appellee school board but the trial court ruled that the Mississippi Accident Contingency Fund statute, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 37-41-39 and 37-41-41, was controlling, determined that appellant's recovery was limited by the statute to $ 10,000, and granted appellee's motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim. Appellant raised numerous arguments to challenge the constitutionality of the statute. They included arguments that the statutory structure usurped judicial power, violated the open court's clause, violated the due process clause, and violated the takings clause. The court considered and rejected each of appellant's arguments and affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that the Mississippi Accident Contingency Fund was rationally related to the proper legislative purpose of conserving limited school resources.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant student's claim against appellee school board. The court held that the Mississippi Accident Contingency Fund statute was constitutional because it was rationally related to the proper legislative purpose of conserving limited school resources.

Artis v. State


No. 92-KP-01046


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


643 So. 2d 533; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 468



September 29, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 9169113 from Judgment dated JANUARY 02, 1992, William F. Coleman RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi) denying his motion for post-conviction relief and ordering that defendant's suspended sentence from a prior criminal conviction be revoked.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and manslaughter upon a guilty plea. He was sentenced to 25 years' imprisonment with 20 years suspended and five years to serve for the armed robbery conviction. He was also sentenced to 20 years' imprisonment with 15 years suspended and five years to serve for the manslaughter conviction. Each of the five years' imprisonment was to run concurrently. Seven years later he was convicted of attempting to obtain a controlled substance by misrepresentation. The State made a motion to revoke his suspended sentence for the armed robbery conviction. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the revocation proceedings. A trial court ordered the revocation of defendant's suspended sentence. On appeal, the court concluded that defendant was never placed on probation and no terms or conditions had been established for the revocation of defendant's suspended sentence. The court determined that due process required that defendant be informed of the terms and conditions upon which his suspended sentence was contingent before it may be properly revoked for violation of the terms and conditions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and reinstated defendant's original suspended sentence.

 

65 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Winder v. State


No. 89-KA-00911, 89-KA-01174


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


640 So. 2d 893; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 347



June 30, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 20439 from Judgment dated JUNE 09, 1989, EUGENE M. BOGEN RULING JUDGE, and from Judgment dated JULY 31, 1989, HOWARD Q. DAVIS RULING JUDGE, Washington County Circuit Court


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged judgments of the Washington County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of burglary, conspiracy, and rape. He claimed the trial court erred in refusing to dismiss his case due to the failure of the state to prosecute him within 270 days of arraignment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with burglary, conspiracy, and rape. His co-defendant pleaded guilty to burglary and conspiracy. The state dropped the rape charge against the co-defendant and he testified against defendant. Defendant was found guilty of burglary and conspiracy in his first trial. A mistrial was ordered on the rape charge after the jury could not agree on defendant's guilt or innocence. Defendant was retried on the rape charge and convicted. On appeal, defendant did not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence; instead, he claimed his case should have been dismissed because he was not timely prosecuted. The court affirmed his convictions, finding that, there was no violation of the 270-day rule. The court found that although defendant filed his motion to dismiss 273 days after arraignment, the motion was premature because the statute had been tolled at least 37 days by plea negotiations and a continuance at the end of one term of court carrying the case over to the next term. The statute was again tolled between the time of the motion to dismiss and the hearing on the motion. As such, a total of 264 days had lapsed and, therefore, the 270-day rule was not violated.


OUTCOME: The court considered the three separate times the statute was tolled and the reasons therefor and determined that there was no violation of the 270-day rule. Accordingly, it affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

66 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Foster v. State


No. 91-DP-00212


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


639 So. 2d 1263; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 670



April 28, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 11229 from Judgment dated JANUARY 18, 1991, Lee J. Howard RULING JUDGE, Lowndes County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH AFFIRMED. WEDNESDAY, JUNE 15, 1994, SET AS DATE OF EXECUTION OF SENTENCE IN THE MANNER PROVIDED BY LAW.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi) convicted defendant of capital murder and imposed the death penalty. Defendant appealed and raised 26 assignments of error including that the jury venire's death qualification process violated U.S. Const. amends. VI, VIII, and XIV, and that the imposition of the death penalty for a juvenile violated U.S. Const. amends. VIII and XIV, and Miss. Const. art. III, § 28.


OVERVIEW: The court determined that issues that were not properly raised in the trial court were procedurally barred from consideration. Nonetheless, the court reviewed all of defendant's claims. After careful consideration, the court found defendant's claims to be without merit. Initially, the court reviewed the guilt phase of the proceedings. The court held that defendant was not denied the opportunity to interrogate the venire on the issue of the death penalty, and in fact did question the venire members about their views on the death penalty and whether it should be imposed in the event of a murder conviction. The jury knew that the death sentence was not automatic and that they were not required to impose a death sentence. The court then reviewed the sentencing phase. Defendant failed to bring a motion pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 43-21-159(3) (1992) for his case to be sent back to the youth court. Similarly, defendant failed to bring a motion for a special hearing for persons under the age of 18 who were charged with a capital offense. Finally, imposition of the death penalty on defendant as a 17 year-old offender did not constitute a per se violation of U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

Miller v. State


No. 91-KA-00057


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


636 So. 2d 391; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 204



April 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified on Denial of Rehearing June 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 2897 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 14, 1990, Alfred G. Nicols Jr. RULING JUDGE, Rankin County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF UNNATURAL INTERCOURSE AND SENTENCE OF TEN YEARS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Rankin County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of unnatural intercourse as proscribed by Miss. Code Ann. § 97-29-59 (1972).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a male, was convicted under the sodomy statute of performing fellatio on a 17-year old male to whom he had served alcohol. Defendant contended that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-29-59 violated his constitutional right of privacy and was unconstitutionally overbroad. The court held that appellant's privacy claim failed because no right of privacy attached to sexual acts committed with children who were illegally supplied with alcohol. The court held that the sodomy statute was not overbroad because its sweep did not invade an area of protected freedom and it had previously been interpreted to include acts of fellatio. The court affirmed the conviction and found that there was no reversible error because defendant was not entitled to an accomplice instruction or an instruction that a finding of penetration was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of unnatural intercourse.

 

68 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Bender v. North Meridian Mobile Home Park


No. 91-CA-00425


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


636 So. 2d 385; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 160



April 7, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 88CV144B from Judgment dated MARCH 20, 1991, Robert Walter Bailey RULING JUDGE, Lauderdale County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenant challenged a finding by the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County (Mississippi) in favor of appellee landlord in a dispute of the eviction of the tenant.


OVERVIEW: The tenant was evicted by the landlord for failure to pay rent; the landlord used self-help by changing the locks on the trailer. The landlord took an inventory of the items left in the trailer, stored them for two months, and then sold the items at a rummage sale. The tenant filed suit, claiming that he was wrongfully evicted pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 89-7-51 and that the statute at issue was unconstitutional; he also alleged conversion. The landlord counterclaimed for past due rent and storage fees. The trial court found in favor of the landlord on all issues. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment on the tenant's eviction claim, holding that, absent a lease provision, the landlord could not resort to self-help remedies. Furthermore, § 89-7-51 did not allow for ejectment for failure to pay rent. As to the constitutionality of the statute, it was raised for the first time on appeal and, therefore, was not preserved. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the landlord on the tenant's conversion claim, holding that the amount of damages assessed was credible and not subject to review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment as to the conversion action, but reversed in part and remanded as to the finding of proper eviction.

State v. Hinds County Bd. of Supervisors


No. 91-CA-00717


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


635 So. 2d 839; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 163



March 31, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 38048 from Judgment dated July 10, 1991. L. Breland Hilburn, Jr., RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state and department of corrections, sought review of a judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which ruled in favor of plaintiff county board of supervisors (county) that the reimbursement limitation contained in Miss. Code Ann. § 47-5-112 was unconstitutional on its face and in its effect.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the statute's reimbursement payment to the county of $ 10 per day per prisoner was inadequate to carry out the legislative purpose of relieving overcrowding in the state penitentiary. The trial court construed the language of the statute to include reimbursement for all actual costs incurred by the county for the housing of state inmates. The trial court also found that the statute operated to tax citizens of the county on a basis peculiar only to the county in violation of Miss. Const. art. IV, § 112. The court found that the action was not barred by sovereign immunity because the county sought a declaration that the statute was unconstitutional. However, the court found that the county enjoyed no constitutional right that was violated. The court held that the fact that the legislature chose to pay the county only $ 10 per day per prisoner did not make the statute inadequate to relieve overcrowding and that if the legislature had intended to pay all costs, it would not have placed a cap on the compensation. The court also ruled that nothing in § 112 affected the validity of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered the judgment that found in favor of the county in its constitutional challenge to the statutory reimbursement provision.
