Lanier v. State


No. 91-KP-00875


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


635 So. 2d 813; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 165



March 31, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 91CV071R from Judgment dated AUGUST 20, 1991, Robert Walter Bailey RULING JUDGE, Lauderdale County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded for Resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his sentence by the Lauderdale County Circuit Court, (Mississippi) that had sentenced him for conviction of murder, kidnapping, and aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of the denial of his petition for post-conviction relief by the circuit court. Defendant challenged the propriety of his sentence even though he had waived his right to parole. Defendant had been convicted of murder, kidnapping, and aggravated assault. The issue before the court was whether the trial court erred in its holdings that the waiver of defendant's future right to apply for parole was valid and the no parole provision was a valid part of the sentence. The court concluded that enforcement of the contract between defendant and the state would result in a sentence not authorized by law. The court held that a life sentence qualified by the preclusion of parole was not available to defendant. The court concluded that defendant had the right to be sentenced by a jury and the State once again had the right to seek the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the circuit court because the contract with the state was void as against public policy.

 

71 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Frank v. Dore


No. 91-CA-00528


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


635 So. 2d 1369; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 138



March 17, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 18443 from Judgment dated APRIL 24, 1991, Jason H. Floyd Jr. RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Chancery Court, Second Judicial District


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bingo winner challenged a decision from the Harrison County Chancery Court, Second Judicial District (Mississippi), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, management company and the Mississippi Coast Coliseum Commission based on its finding that Miss. Code Ann. § 87-1-1 (1972) barred suit for the collection of winnings from legal bingo games.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-33-51 exempted charitable bingo games from the definition of illegal gambling. Thus, bingo was a lawful activity, not a lottery, and the winner could maintain an action to collect her winnings, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 87-1-5. The winner also argued that the trial court erred in denying her request to amend her complaint and that no written findings or basis for the denial were contained in the order denying the request. The court held that motions for leave to amend were left to the sound discretion of the trial court and were not to be reversed absent abuse of discretion. However, leave to amend was to be freely given when justice so required. It was apparent that the proposed amended complaint contained additional theories of recovery, stemming from the same transactions and events. The court ruled that there were genuine issues in dispute as to material facts which precluded summary disposition. Because no grounds were given for the denial of the motion to amend, there was no guide whereby the court could determine if there was an abuse of discretion. Thus, remand was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision which granted summary judgment to the management company and commission for failing to pay bingo winnings because there were numerous facts in dispute and the trial court had committed manifest error in denying the winner's request to amend her pleadings without an explanation.

Marx v. Broom


No. 91-CC-00476, CONSOLIDATED WITH: 91-CC-00474, CONSOLIDATED WITH: 91-CC-00475, CONSOLIDATED WITH 91-CC-00422


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


632 So. 2d 1315; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 117; 18 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1054



February 24, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 91-CC-0476: Appeal No. 142765 from Judgment dated APRIL 02, 1991, Denise Sweet-Owens RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.

91-CC-0474: Appeal No. 142944 from Judgment dated MARCH 28, 1991, Denise Sweet-Owens RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.

91-CC-0475: Appeal No. 141652 from Judgment dated APRIL 23, 1991, Denise Sweet-Owens RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.

91-CC-0422: Appeal No. 139915 from Judgment dated MARCH 21, 1991, Denise Sweet-Owens RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED ON DIRECT APPEALS AND CROSS-APPEAL OF JOHN THOMAS TODD AND PHILIPS T. COOLEY.  


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state tax commission (commission) challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which found that appellee federal retirees were entitled to a refund of state income taxes paid under the state's unconstitutional tax scheme that taxed federal retirees while exempting the state's own retired employees. The federal retirees cross-appealed on the denial of their motion for certification of a class action.


OVERVIEW: The federal retirees sought refunds of state income taxes paid under a tax scheme that was unconstitutional based on its differential treatment of federal retirees from that of the state's own retired employees. After being denied relief by the commission, the federal retirees sought declaratory relief from the trial court. The trial court denied the federal retirees' motion for class certification. However, based a prior decision, the trial court found that the tax scheme at issue was unconstitutional and held that the federal retirees were entitled to a refund pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 27-7-313 (1989). On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The plain words of § 27-7-313 provided that any overpayment of state taxes for any reason shall be refunded to the taxpayer. Thus, the federal retirees clearly were entitled to refunds. The amendment to § 27-7-313 during the pendency of the action did not accord with due process requirements. Nothing in § 27-7-313 required that the payment of taxes be under protest in order to get a refund. The Rules of Civil Procedure enacted by the state intentionally omitted Rule 23 pertaining to class actions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court holding that the state tax scheme was unconstitutional and that the federal retirees were entitled to refunds as a matter of state law. The order denying the federal retirees' motion for class certification was affirmed.

Dillon v. Beal (In re Estate of Dillon)


No. 90-CA-00700


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


632 So. 2d 1298; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 113



February 24, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. P8278 from Judgment dated APRIL 16, 1990, John Stuart Robinson RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AWARDING RETIREMENT BENEFITS TO DILLON'S THREE CHILDREN, MYRTLE DILLON BEAL, LAWRENCE T. DILLON, JR. AND CRAIG DILLON, IN EQUAL SHARES, AFFIRMED. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the deceased's daughter, filed a petition for probate and for letters of administration and filed a motion for injunctive relief against appellant, the deceased's wife. The wife sought review of the order of the Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which appointed the daughter as executrix and determined that the deceased's children were the legal beneficiaries of the deceased's state retirement funds.


OVERVIEW: The deceased was a state employee and designated his three children as the beneficiaries of his state retirement funds. The deceased married and did not designate another beneficiary subsequent to his marriage. The deceased executed a holographic will and codicil naming his daughter as executrix and designating his three children as beneficiaries. The wife claimed that she was entitled to the state retirement funds pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 25-11-103(f) (Supp. 1993). The court affirmed the chancery court's order. The court held that although § 25-11-103(f) provided that the lawful spouse of a public employee was the beneficiary of retirement funds unless the employee designated another beneficiary subsequent to the date of marriage, the deceased's clear intention was to divide his retirement benefits between his three children, that § 25-11-103(f) did not defeat the clear intention of the deceased, and that the deceased's failure to comply with § 25-11-103(f) was irrelevant in light of his clear intention to designate his children as beneficiaries of his state retirement benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the chancery court's order awarding the deceased's state retirement benefits to the deceased's three children.

 

74 of 825 DOCUMENTS


In the Interest of R.G.


No. 92-CA-1295


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


632 So. 2d 953; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 108



February 17, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 2981 from Judgment dated OCTOBER 15, 1992, William Stratton Agin RULING JUDGE, Madison County County Court Youth Court Division



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state attorney general, sought review, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 7-5-1 (1991) and Miss. R. Civ. P. 24(d), of a decision of the Madison County Court Youth Court Division (Mississippi), which found that the Compulsory School Attendance Law, Miss. Code Ann. § 37-13-91 (1990), was unconstitutional insofar as it required the selection and supervision of school attendance officers to be undertaken by youth court judges.


OVERVIEW: In a delinquency action, appellee truant contested testimony by a school attendance officer on the grounds that the officer's position violated Miss. Const. art. I, § 2, the separation of powers provision. Although Miss. Code Ann. § 37-13-91 came to the court clothed with a heavy presumption of validity, the court found that the truant met his required burden. The State alleged that the attendance officer was a local office and that the separation of powers provision applied only to state governmental positions. The court found that the officer was a position within the executive branch of the state government. Therefore, because the youth court judge was a part of the state judicial system, the judge's selection of the officer was a violation of the separation of powers. Further, the court found that Miss. Const. art. I, § 2 made no distinction between ministerial and discretionary duties. Thus, even if the officer's duties were ministerial, the separation of powers would be violated. Because of the finding of unconstitutionality, the county judge divested himself of any authority over the officers. Therefore, the judge was without authority to reassign the officers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment as to the finding of unconstitutionality but reversed that part of the judgment that placed the attendance officers under the jurisdiction of the department of education.

Mississippi High Sch. Activities Ass'n v. Coleman


No. 91-CA-0486


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


631 So. 2d 768; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 32



January 27, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 143862 from Judgment dated APRIL 11, 1991, Pat Wise RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff student brought suit against defendant Mississippi High School Activities Association, Inc., in the Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi). Student alleged that as a result of being denied eligibility to play basketball under anti-recruiting regulation, he would suffer immediate and irreparable injury. The trial court granted a temporary restraining order allowing student to play. Association appealed.


OVERVIEW: The challenged regulation prohibited any student from participating in interscholastic athletics unless he resided in the district where he attended school. The court held that the regulation's constitutionality was a moot question in this case; however, the case was capable of repetition, yet evading review, and therefore was reviewable. The court held that the rule was a form of state action; however, there was no property interest in participation in high school athletics, so no procedural due process analysis was necessary. As to substantive due process, student's right to travel was not impermissibly burdened because no penalty was imposed on the exercise of the right. The regulation did not interfere with any religious practice. The regulation was rationally related to the state's interest in promoting fair competition and preventing overzealous recruiting. As to student's equal protection claim, the classification at issue, based on bona fide residence requirements, was rationally related to the legitimate purpose of deterring recruitment practices and encouraging fair competition. The court concluded that the anti-recruitment rule was constitutional and enforceable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the chancery court's judgment and rendered judgment that the regulation was constitutional and enforceable.

In re Inquiry Concerning Mun. Judges


No. 92-CC-1248


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


631 So. 2d 758; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 34



January 27, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 92064 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 13, 1992, William M. Bost Jr. RULING JUDGE, Mississippi Commission Judicial Performance



DISPOSITION: RECOMMENDATION OF MISSISSIPPI JUDICIAL PERFORMANCE COMMMISSION IS AFFIRMED. W. T. GRANT, ERNEST HERRING, JOHN BEAMON AND HAROLD WARD, SR. ARE HEREBY SUSPENDED ACCORDING TO STATUTE AND THE RULE OF THE COMMISSION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Mississippi Commission on Judicial Performance recommended to the court that four judges be suspended as municipal court judges as long as they were mayors of their municipalities. The Commission also held that Miss. Code Ann. § 21-23-5 (1972), which allowed mayors of small municipalities to also serve as municipal judges, was unconstitutional under Miss. Const. art. I, §§ 1, 2. One respondent judge appeared and argued his case.


OVERVIEW: Upon receiving complaints about mayors also serving as municipal judges, the Commission advised the mayor judges that their dual positions created a conflict that violated the Mississippi Constitution and Miss. Code Jud. Conduct Canon 3C(1)(d)(i) and filed the instant action against those who did not resign. The court found that Miss. Code Ann. § 21-23-5 (1972) was constitutional because the separation of powers doctrine applied to the state and not to municipalities, which were governed by charters and other statutes enacted by the legislature. Nonetheless, under the authority of Miss. Const. art. 6, § 177A, the court proscribed the use of Miss. Code Ann. § 21-23-5 (1972), finding the functions of the offices of mayor and judge inherently incompatible. The offices being held by the same person promoted conduct prejudicial to the administration of justice, which brought the judiciary into disrepute and could potentially violate a defendant's right to due process. The court's concern as to the one judge who appeared was to remove all appearance of the impropriety of a city's chief executive also presiding over the court cases that generated fines that were a source of revenue.


OUTCOME: The court accepted the recommendation of the Commission and ordered that the municipal judges be suspended according to statute and the rules of the Commission. The court also determined that the statute at issue would have no future application in Mississippi.

State v. Molpus


No. 91-CA-0975


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


633 So. 2d 1004; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 35



January 27, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 51580 from Judgment dated SEPTEMBER 10, 1991, Robert H. Oswald, RULING JUDGE, Jackson County Chancery Court



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a suit involving the constitutionality of 1989 Tidelands Legislation enacted by the Mississippi Legislature, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 29-15-1 et seq. (Supp. 1991), and arising out of plaintiff's claim of adverse possession of low-lying property along a certain bayou, to which defendant asserted record title, an appeal was taken from the Jackson County Chancery Court (Mississippi). On the appeal, the parties were the state and its secretary of state.


OVERVIEW: The suit arose from the subject claim of adverse possession. The upland was adjacent to tidelands across which private persons had dredged a canal and basin between 1952 and 1959. The spoils were deposited on tidelands that were then, and remained, below mean high tide. The involvement of the tidelands implicated and made the state a party. The subject land was located within the area of the Special Management Area Plan adopted by the federal government and the state. As the appeal addressed the same question as to the constitutionality of the Tidelands Legislation presented in another suit decided concurrently, the dispositive issue on appeal in the case sub judice involved constitutional questions, and there were no unique issues of fact or law, the holding in the other case governed the case before the court and warranted a reversal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and rendered a decision, holding that the court's decision rendered the same day in another related case controlled the disposition of all salient issues raised in the case sub judice.

Coplin v. Francis


No. 90-CA-0705


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


631 So. 2d 752; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 40



January 27, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 24803 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 07, 1989, Thomas J. Gardner III RULING JUDGE, Monroe County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff family appealed the judgment of the Monroe County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted a summary judgment in the wrongful death action brought against defendants, county and county supervisor.


OVERVIEW: A minor child was killed in a head-on collision. The vehicle in which the child was riding as a passenger was knocked off of a bridge. The complaint charged the county's supervisor with negligently permitting grass to grow along the bridge, failing to post warning signs and rails on the bridge, permitting holes in the bridge, and maintaining a dangerously narrow bridge. The county was charged with vicarious liability. The court held that, generally, county supervisors were immune from liability for injuries sustained as a result of the negligent maintenance of public roads. Here, however, Miss. Code Ann. § 65-21-1 mandated that any bridge was to be built or rebuilt at a certain width and with banisters at either side. The court held that there was a genuine issue of material fact regarding whether the supervisor exceeded his authority in rebuilding a one-lane bridge without adequate warnings. Construction of road bridges in accordance with Miss. Code Ann. § 65-21-1 was a ministerial function. Accordingly, the supervisor was not protected by qualified immunity. The court affirmed that the county enjoyed sovereign immunity under Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-1 et seq. (Supp. 1985).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the county supervisor and remanded. The court affirmed the judgment as to the county.

Secretary of State v. Wiesenberg


No. 90-CA-0692


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


633 So. 2d 983; 1994 Miss. LEXIS 36



January 27, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 17879 from Judgment dated JUNE 08, 1990, William Leonard Stewart, RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Chancery Court, Second Judicial District



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee landowner brought suit in the Harrison County Chancery Court (Mississippi) to confirm title on waterfront property. Appellant Secretary of State (secretary) intervened in the suit, seeking to have the Tidelands Legislation of 1989 (legislation) declared unconstitutional. The court denied a petition to intervene filed by appellant individual and declared the legislation constitutional. The secretary and the individual appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected all of the challenges to the legislation's constitutionality and affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court rejected the secretary's claims that the legislature had no authority to authorize the sale of tidelands to private individuals, holding that such sale was an incident to the overall public interest and purpose in accommodating an expanding population, commerce, tourism and recreation. The court noted that the sale of individual lots to private owners could not be separated from the general context of the overall public purposes involved in the legislation. The court also concluded that because the legislation was an effort to manage and protect the public trust lands, it was a general, and not a local or private law; that the legislation was not unconstitutionally vague; and that the legislation did not grant the secretary the power to make laws, which would violate the separation of powers principles. The court also rejected the individual's claim that the duties delegated to the secretary by the legislation were quasi-judicial and therefore constitutionally impermissible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, upholding the constitutionality of the legislation.

Neely v. State ex rel. Tate County


No. 91-CA-0304


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


628 So. 2d 1376; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 562



December 16, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. CV90124CT from Judgment dated FEBRUARY 26, 1991, George C. Carlson Jr. RULING JUDGE, Tate County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Tate County Circuit Court (Mississippi) in favor of plaintiff state in a civil forfeiture action pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-1-101 et seq. (Supp. 1993) in which the state sought forfeiture of defendant's car and money found on defendant.


OVERVIEW: The police based on a tip from a confidential informant that defendant was dealing in crack stopped defendant and found cocaine in his car after he consented to a search. Subsequently the police found a large sum of money on defendant's person. The trial court held that the car and money were subject to forfeiture. The court rejected defendant's contention that the police did not have probable cause for the stop and that the search and seizure of his car violated the Fourth Amendment and Miss. Const. § 23. The court held probable cause was not a prerequisite for a brief investigatory stop, when the police had reasonable suspicion based on articulable facts that criminal activity was afoot. The court found the police corroborated the informant's information and that the stop was lawful. The court held defendant neither denied that the substance found in his car was not cocaine or that it did not belong to him. The court held there was insufficient proof of the necessary nexus between the money and the cocaine to warrant its seizure pursuant to Miss Code Ann. § 41-29-153(a)(5), (a)(7) (Supp. 1993) because the money found on defendant's person was not in close proximity to his car.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered in part the judgment as it pertained to the seizure of the money found defendant's person. The court otherwise affirmed the judgment as it pertained to the seizure of defendant's car.

 

81 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Conner v. State


No. 90-DP-0927


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


632 So. 2d 1239; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 541



December 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified on Denial of Rehearing, March 17, 1994. Rehearing Denied March 17, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Miss. LEXIS 142.
Writ of certiorari denied Conner v. Mississippi, 513 U.S. 927, 130 L. Ed. 2d 276, 115 S. Ct. 314, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 7088 (1994)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Motion denied by Conner v. State, 684 So. 2d 608, 1996 Miss. LEXIS 296 (Miss., 1996)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 13490 from Judgment dated JULY 27, 1990, Robert Walter Bailey RULING JUDGE, Lauderdale County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION FOR CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE TO DEATH BY LETHAL INJECTION AFFIRMED. WEDNESDAY, JANUARY 19, 1994, SET FOR INFLICTION OF THE DEATH PENALTY AS PROVIDED BY LAW.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that convicted him of capital murder and sentenced him to death by lethal injection. On appeal, he claimed the trial court made several errors in the guilt and sentencing phases of his trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder, and sentenced to death by lethal injection in a separate hearing. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the trial court did not err in not ordering a competency hearing; (2) sufficient evidence was contained in the record to support his conviction of capital murder; (3) the evidence in the record did not require the trial court to give a lesser-included offense instruction; (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion by permitting the prosecution to introduce evidence concerning a witness' agreement to take a lie detector test; (5) the trial court did not err when it permitted the prosecution to impeach defendant with his post crime statement; and (6) the trial court did not deprive defendant of his right to confront a witness when it refused to permit him to impeach that witness on a collateral employment issue. Additionally, the court concluded that the trial court did not make any reversible errors in the sentencing phase of the trial, as the death sentence imposed upon defendant was proportionate when compared to other cases where the death penalty had been imposed in the state. The trial court's judgment was thus affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of capital murder and that sentenced him to death by lethal injection was affirmed. The trial court made no errors in either the guilt or sentencing phase of defendant's trial that compelled reversal of the conviction or sentence.

 

82 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Michael S. Fawer v. Evans


No. 92-FC-122


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


627 So. 2d 829; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 533



December 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Answer conformed to, Remanded by Fawer v. Evans, 12 F.3d 1099, 1993 U.S. App. LEXIS 34623 (5th Cir. Miss., 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 911628 from Judgment dated FEBRUARY 06, 1992, REYNALDO G. GARZA RULING JUDGE, Fifth Circuit Court of Appeals



DISPOSITION: CERTIFIED QUESTION ANSWERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Court of Appeals for the Fifth Circuit, pursuant to Miss. Sup. Ct. R. 20, certified a question as to the applicable statute of limitations period under Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-29 (Supp. 1992) in plaintiff attorney's action against defendant client for fees pursuant to an unwritten agreement or understanding.


OVERVIEW: The attorney filed suit in state court to recover payment for services provided to the client in the successful defense of a criminal matter. The client removed the case to federal district court on diversity grounds. The district court granted summary judgment, holding that the action was subject to a one-year statute of limitations applicable to unwritten contracts of employment. When the attorney appealed that decision, the federal appellate court certified a question as to the appropriate statute of limitations. The court held the one-year statute of limitations for actions on unwritten contracts of employment in Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-29 (Supp. 1992), applied only to traditional employer-employee situations and did not apply to an unwritten contract between an attorney and client for legal representation. The court found that a contract for an attorney's services was not synonymous with an employment contract because the client was not concerned with controlling the attorney's work, rather the client was concerned with receiving a skilled defense. Therefore the suit was subject to the three-year statute of limitations for an action on an unwritten contract.


OUTCOME: The court answered the question certified to it by the federal appellate court, holding that the suit was subject to the three-year statute of limitations for an action on an unwritten contract.

 

83 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Beatty v. State


No. 90-CA-1325


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


627 So. 2d 355; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 520



November 24, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 10509 from Judgment dated JUNE 01, 1990, Lee Jackson Howard IV RULING JUDGE, Lowndes County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order by the Lowndes County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which affirmed defendant's conviction by the lower court for the possession of illegal gambling devices. Defendant claimed that the machines were seized pursuant to a defective search warrant. The trial court affirmed the lower court's decision and remanded the cause to the county court for destruction of the machines.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that because the slot machines were not being used for gambling purposes they were not subject to confiscation and destruction pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 97-33-7 (1972). At the time the trial court rendered its decision, § 27-27-12 had yet to be enacted. Section 27-27-12 provided an exception from § 97-33-7 for antique coin machines. The court stated that defendant's case had not proceeded to final judgment. Defendant's due process remained an issue pending a final determination as to whether the machines fell within the explicit exception provided for in § 27-27-12, which was enacted to protect and preserve the slot machine's place in the state's history. If defendant could show that the seized slot machines were at least 25 years old and were not connected with any unlawful gambling activities, then the machines should be returned to defendant pursuant to § 27-27-12. Therefore, the court reversed and remanded for further findings due to the fact that § 99-33-7, as amended, no longer made "antique" slot machines automatically subject to forfeiture proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Town of Winstonville v. Demco Distrib. Co.


No. 91-CA-0198


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


630 So. 2d 40; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 521



November 24, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 23152 from Judgment dated JANUARY 31, 1991, Harvey T. Ross RULING JUDGE, Bolivar County Chancery Court, Second Judicial District



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town challenged a decision of the Bolivar County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which placed the town under a permanent injunction and found it in violation of a preliminary injunction previously issued by the court on behalf of appellee residents.


OVERVIEW: A town ordinance directed those located on the service lines of the town's gas system to connect their individual service lines to the municipally owned utility. Appellees filed a complaint obtained a temporary restraining order prohibiting the town from enforcing the ordinance. Time passed, during which appellees did nothing, and the court clerk issued an order pursuant to Miss. R. Civ. P. 41(d) remanding the case to the court's inactive files due to appellees' inaction. Later, two town employees disconnected the propane tanks of certain residents. After a flurry of litigation, the trial court issued an order declaring the ordinance unconstitutional and unenforceable, and permanently enjoined the town from enforcing the ordinance. The trial court held the town in civil contempt for violating the temporary injunction. The town appealed. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and dismissed the case. The trial court was without jurisdiction to hear any feature of this case following the date of the remand of the matter to the inactive files.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court permanently enjoining enforcement a town ordinance and holding the town in contempt. The court dismissed appellees' complaint.

Woodward v. State


NO. 03-DP-0081


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


635 So. 2d 805; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 442



October 7, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 14, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 3789 from Judgment dated APRIL 29, 1987, Perry County Circuit Court;


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an application for leave to file a motion to vacate the judgment and death sentence that he had received after he was convicted of capital murder. Defendant's conviction had previously been affirmed on appeal, and the United States Supreme Court had denied certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted based on overwhelming evidence of guilt that included separate written and videotaped confessions and a large amount of physical and circumstantial evidence. He was sentenced to death. His conviction was affirmed. He then filed an application for leave to file a motion to vacate his conviction and death sentence. Defendant's motion was based on a U.S. Supreme Court decision that required reversal of the sentence of death because of an erroneous instruction to the jury on especially heinous crimes. The court reversed defendant's sentence and remanded for a new trial on sentencing. Several of defendant's claims were waived pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-21(1) (Supp. 1993) when he did not raise them on direct appeal. He could not show cause or actual prejudice with respect to the guilt phase of his trial. The court, however, determined that defendant's counsel were ineffective during the penalty phase of his trial when they decided to rely on evidence of mental illness without fully presenting the expert testimony. They had no other evidence to present in mitigation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the death penalty sentence of the trial court and remanded the case for a new trial on sentencing.

Wilcher v. State


NO. 03-DP-0032, 03-DP-0037


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


635 So. 2d 789; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 447



October 7, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied March 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] No. 03-DP-0032: Appeal No. 3707 from Judgment dated JULY 31, 1982, Scott County Circuit Court on change of venue to Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District;

No. 03-DP-0038: Appeal No. 3708 from Judgment dated SEPTEMBER 16, 1982, Scott County Circuit Court on Change of venue to Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State filed a motion to reconsider the order of the Supreme Court of Mississippi, which held that it would not engage in harmless error analysis on the issue of the "especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel" jury instruction after defendant was convicted of capital crimes and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Following defendant's convictions and sentences of death, defendant filed a motion for leave to file a motion to vacate the death sentences asserting that the sentencing instructions foreclosed the jury's proper consideration of mitigating circumstances. Thereafter, the state filed a motion to reconsider through which it asked the court to engage in harmless error analysis on the same issue. The court held that Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-101 (Supp. 1992) required that the jury had to make the weighing of aggravating and mitigating factors, and if it were to engage in such analysis, it would run afoul of previous a previous decision rendered by the United States Supreme Court, which stated that appellate reweighing violated the federal due process requirements because § 99-19-101 would not be complied with. Accordingly, § 99-19-101 prevented the court from performing either reweighing or harmless error analysis as a matter of state law. Further, defendant's motion for leave to file a second post-conviction petition was granted, and defendant's motion to vacate the death sentences was also granted.


OUTCOME: State's motion to reconsider was denied; defendant's motions for leave to file a second post-conviction petition and motion to vacate death sentences were granted.

State Tax Comm'n v. Veazey


No. 91-CC-0194


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


624 So. 2d 997; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 429



September 30, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 138866 from Judgment dated JANUARY 29, 1991, W. O. Dillard RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Mississippi State Tax Commission entered an order suspending the package store permit of appellee permittee, who filed a complaint to restrain the Commission from enforcing the order. Finding that the permittee had standing, the Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi) determined that Miss. Code Ann. § 67-1-83(2) (1972) was unconstitutional and granted a permanent restraining order. The Commission sought review.


OVERVIEW: The Commission's order was based on its finding that an employee of the permittee's package store sold liquor to a prohibited purchaser in violation of § 67-1-83(2). The Commission's argued on appeal, inter alia, that the chancery court erred in finding that the permittee had standing to attack the constitutionality of § 67-1-83(2). The court agreed, holding that the Commission properly suspended the permittee's package store license because the permittee framed his entire attack against § 67-1-83(2) on his view that the statute was defective in its failure to provide notice and a hearing to the prohibited purchaser. However, the permittee clearly lacked standing to raise such argument because he was not prejudiced by any failure of due process in the operation of the statute. Therefore, the chancery court erred in finding that the permittee had standing to assert a challenge on this point. The permittee was fully informed of the decision to prohibit alcohol sales to the prohibited purchaser. A notice was first mailed and another was hand-delivered to the permittee's package store with instructions to post a photograph of the prohibited purchaser.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered the chancery court's decision. Accordingly, the order of the Commission was reinstated.

Simon v. State


No. 90-KA-0904


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


633 So. 2d 407; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 431



September 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Simon v. State, 1994 Miss. LEXIS 141 (Miss., Mar. 17, 1994)
Motion granted by, Vacated by, Remanded by Simon v. Mississippi, 513 U.S. 956, 115 S. Ct. 413, 130 L. Ed. 2d 329, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 7532 (1994)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Stay denied by, Motion denied by, Motion dismissed by, As moot, Certificate of appealability granted Simon v. Epps, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 54712 (N.D. Miss., May 20, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 5105 from Judgment dated JULY 06, 1990, John L. Pearson RULING JUDGE, Quitman County Circuit Court On change of venue to Jones County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Quitman County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder, sexual battery, and kidnapping. Prior to trial, the trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress and for a change of venue, the case already having been transferred from another county. Defendant was sentenced to two consecutive 30-year terms in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in the denial of his motion for a second change of venue and in improperly allowing the state to strike potential jurors on the basis of their race and gender. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. In so holding, the court found that 1) the trial court's ruling that the state's reason for striking an African-American juror was an acceptable, race-neutral reason was not in violation of the prohibition against striking jurors bases on race in violation of Batson; 2) there was no merit to defendant's claim that the state was required to give a gender-neutral reason for the peremptory challenge of women jurors because Batson did not apply to challenges based on gender; 3) the record did not support defendant's contention that a change of venue was warranted on the basis of pre-trial publicity; and 4) defendant failed to present any evidence that would have made a prima facie case that he was denied a trial by an impartial jury or that he was entitled to a second change of venue to a county with a population similar to that of the county he requested a change of venue from.


OUTCOME: The trial court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for capital murder, sexual battery, and kidnapping.

Phipps v. Irby Constr. Co.


No. 89-CA-0174


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


636 So. 2d 353; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 418



September 16, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 17156 from Judgment dated SEPTEMBER 12, 1988, JOE N PIGOTT RULING JUDGE, Copiah County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants electrical worker and insurer sought review from a Copiah County Circuit Court (Mississippi) judgment dismissing their suit against appellees construction company and industrial design company pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-41 (1972), alleging that the statute in question did not bar suit because it was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: An electrical worker and his insurer filed suit against a construction company and an industrial design company alleging that defective design and installation of power lines had contributed to the electrical worker's serious injuries suffered while working on the power lines. When the lower court dismissed based on the finding that Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-41 (1972) barred suit, the electrical worker and insurer sought review. The court held that (1) the power line improvement had been an improvement to real property, (2) Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-41 (1972) was the applicable statute of limitations, (3) the removal of wrongful death actions from the statute at issue did not raise a Fourteenth Amendment equal protection issue and did not apply to the electrical worker, whose suit was not one for wrongful death, and (4) therefore Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-41 (1972) acted as an absolute bar to the suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment against the electrical worker and his insurer.

Mississippi Bureau of Narcotics v. Harrison County


No. 90-CA-1320


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


623 So. 2d 267; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 345



August 26, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 24883 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 13, 1990, James E. Thomas RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Bureau of Narcotics sought review of a judgment from the Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which allowed money seized in a drug arrest to be forfeited to appellee county pursuant to Miss. Const. art. 14, § 261 (1890).


OVERVIEW: The Bureau and the county both filed petitions that sought a forfeiture of money seized in a drug arrest. The circuit court allowed money seized in a drug arrest to be forfeited to the county's general fund pursuant to Miss. Const. art. 14, § 261 (1890). The circuit court's forfeiture of the contraband money was affirmed. The court held that because the forfeiture was adjudicated as part of a criminal proceeding, Miss. Const. art. 14, § 261 was controlling over the civil forfeiture statutes as set forth in Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-177 (2) (1972). When a forfeiture was adjudicated in conjunction with criminal proceedings, the contraband money was to be deposited into the county's general fund under Miss. Const. art. 14, § 261 (1890).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's forfeiture of the contraband money to the county's general fund.

Ashland Pipe Line Co. v. Marx


No. 91-CC-50


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


623 So. 2d 995; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 329



August 19, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 127394 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 10, 1990, Patricia Wise RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant foreign corporation sought review of a decision of the Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which affirmed the decision of appellee Mississippi State Tax Commission that assessed additional income tax and interest against the foreign corporation.


OVERVIEW: The foreign corporation filed a complaint against the Mississippi State Tax Commission (Commission) alleging that the Commission incorrectly charged the foreign corporation in additional income tax for the taxable years of 1979, 1980, and 1981, plus interest. The trial court affirmed the Commission's assessment of additional income tax and interest against the foreign corporation. On appeal, the foreign corporation maintained that the Commission acted arbitrarily and without statutory authority. The court found that since both parties conceded that the foreign corporation's operation was a multi-state unitary operation, its "business income" was subject to apportionment because it could not be allocated to any particular state and direct or separate accounting for Mississippi net business income was impossible. Taking the statute as a whole, the court held that the Commission correctly determined that the dividends were subject to apportionment. The court held that the foreign corporation failed to present "clear and cogent" evidence that the Commission incorrectly included the dividend income from the subsidiaries.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

92 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Medders v. United States Fidelity & Guar. Co.


No. 07-CA-59570


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


623 So. 2d 979; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 313



August 5, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 7999 from Judgment dated AUGUST 26, 1988, ELZY J SMITH RULING JUDGE, Boliver County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant wrongful death beneficiaries sought review of a judgment from the Boliver County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District (Mississippi), which held decedent, as the co-employee of an uninsured motorist, was not entitled to recover from the uninsured motorist policy of decedent's employer because workers' compensation had been decedent's exclusive remedy.


OVERVIEW: While acting in the course and scope of employment, an uninsured motorist had an accident, and a co-employee died. After numerous claims were filed against the employer, plaintiff insurer filed an interpleader action against defendant wrongful death beneficiaries, having defendants assert rights to the amounts due under the insurance policy. Thereafter, defendants asserted a right to the uninsured motorist benefits. As workers' compensation benefits had been paid to defendants, the court held the workers' compensation remedy had been exclusive, thereby prohibiting defendants from reaching the uninsured motorist benefits. Following a grant of summary judgment in plaintiff's favor, defendants sought review, and the court affirmed. Initially, the court noted that under Miss. Code Ann. § 71-3-9 (1972), workers' compensation was the exclusive remedy for a work-related injury caused by a co-employee. Interpreting the phrase "legally entitled to recover" found in Miss. Code Ann. § 83-11-101 (1972), the court held uninsured motorist coverage had not been mandated because the tortfeasor, who had been the deceased's co-employee, was immune from liability under § 71-3-9.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment which held decedent, as the co-employee of an uninsured motorist, was not entitled to recover from the uninsured motorist policy of decedent's employer because workers' compensation had been decedent's exclusive remedy. The court held that because the exclusivity of workers' compensation had protected the co-employee, the decedent had not been "legally entitled to recover" under the uninsured motorist statute.

Valley Forge Ins. Co. v. Strickland


NO. 90-CA-0933


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


620 So. 2d 535; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 205



May 13, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 53835 from Judgment dated JUNE 26, 1990, Robert H. Oswald RULING JUDGE, Jackson County Chancery Court



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer challenged the decision of the Jackson County Chancery Court (Mississippi) that ruled that appellee was entitled to the benefit of an insurance policy from another insurer, that appellant must again tender its policy limits due to its failure to obtain court approval, and that appellant committed bad faith that resulted in an unconditional award of a large amount of punitive damages. Conditional punitive damages were awarded.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurer filed a complaint seeking a declaration that it was entitled to the proceeds under the subrogation rights in an insurance contract, pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. §§ 83-11-103 and 83-11-107. Appellee counterclaimed for the automobile liability policy limit and asserted a claim for a second payment of the policy limits of appellee's insurance binder with appellant because the first payment was not court approved. Appellant sought review after the chancellor awarded appellee the proceeds, the additional policy limit, unconditional punitive damages for bad faith, and conditional punitive damages if appellant failed to satisfy certain corrective and preventive measures described in the judgment. The court held that there was no requirement that the lower court choose between the in-state and the out-of-state law for purposes of assessing punitive damages. The court affirmed the unconditional punitive damages because the lower court reached the proper result. The attorney fees, expenses, and prejudgment interest awards were affirmed because the punitive damages were proper. The court reversed and rendered the conditional punitive damage award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the unconditional punitive damages. The court affirmed the additional policy limit payment order. The court affirmed the award of attorney fees and expenses because the unconditional punitive damages were proper. The court reversed and rendered the award of conditional punitive damages and the alternative affirmative measures.

 

94 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Govan v. Medical Credit Servs., Inc.


NO. 90-CA-0533


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


621 So. 2d 928; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 127



April 8, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 20721 from Judgment dated MAY 10, 1990, Jerry Owen Terry Sr. RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband sought review of a decision from the Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which granted appellee creditor's motion for judgment on the pleadings, in the creditor's action for unpaid medical bills incurred by the former wife prior to the parties' divorce.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found the former husband liable for certain unpaid medical bills of his former wife, which were incurred prior to their divorce. On appeal, the former husband asserted that liability to third party creditors for debts incurred by his former wife during their marriage was a violation of equal protection under the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution, as well as a violation of Miss. Const. art. 4, § 94. Finding that, absent any express agreement with a third party to do so, a spouse was not obligated to pay the debts of the other, the court reversed the decision of the circuit court. The court found that the circuit court erred in finding the former husband liable for his former wife's hospital bill. Nothing in Mississippi jurisprudence obligated one spouse to be liable to a third party for the debts of the other without express consent. To hold otherwise would have violated Miss. Const. art. 4, § 94, and opened the door for either spouse to control or deplete the other's separate estate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's decision, which granted the creditor's motion for judgment on the pleadings. The court rendered judgment for the former husband.

Townsend v. Estate of Gilbert


NO. 90-CA-0899


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


616 So. 2d 333; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 112



April 1, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 7852 from Judgment dated JULY 23, 1990, John L. Pearson RULING JUDGE, Coahoma County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, estate administrator, sought review of a judgment of the Coahoma County Circuit Court (Mississippi), in favor of appellees, estate and others, in a wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted summary judgment for the estate and others in the estate administrator's wrongful death action that alleged that his decedent was killed by the negligence of the estate and others' decedent in an automobile accident. The trial court found that the cause of action was time-barred by Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-25. On appeal, the estate administrator argued that the trial court erred in not applying the general six year statute of limitations found in Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-49. The court found that statutes dealing specifically with a matter were to be preferred over those of a more general nature. Therefore, the specific statute of § 15-1-25 preempted the general statute of § 15-1-49. Section 15-1-25 specifically stated that suits against estate administrators had to be filed within four years of the qualification of said administrator.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the estate and others in a wrongful death action brought by the estate administrator and held that the action was time-barred by the applicable statute of limitations.

McNeal v. State


NO. 90-KA-1147


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


617 So. 2d 999; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 126



March 25, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 27, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Miss. LEXIS 219.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 8610065 from Judgment dated SEPTEMBER 01, 1990, Clinton Lockard RULING JUDGE, Jackson County Circuit Court on change of venue to Adams County Circuit Court;



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Adams County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted defendant of murdering his wife.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in refusing to exclude a juror that the defense learned, after voir dire, had lost a daughter to murder. The court held that its research reveals no case or statutory law which could have been construed to disqualify the juror simply because a member of her family was the victim of a crime. The court held that the fact that the juror's daughter was murdered six years earlier was tragic; however, it did not prove that defendant was prejudiced by the participation of the juror in his trial. Defendant next contended that police provided false information to the magistrate who issued the search warrant. The court rejected this contention, holding that defendant failed to prove that the information contained in the affidavit was false or misleading. Defendant next contended that the trial court erred in admitting evidence seized from defendant's automobile. The police had a warrant for defendant's house but not his car. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that substantial evidence existed on which the trial court could have based a finding that probable cause existed to search the automobile without a warrant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murdering his wife.

 

97 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Churchill v. Pearl River Basin Dev. Dist.


NO. 07-CA-59194


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


619 So. 2d 900; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 74



February 25, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 4553 from Judgment dated APRIL 14, 1988, JOE N PIGOTT RULING JUDGE, Pike County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded for Proceedings Consistent with Opinion of the Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual challenged a decision of the Pike County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted appellees', a development district and a county (district), motion of summary judgment on the basis of sovereign immunity on the individual's claims of negligence, strict liability in tort, and breach of implied contract.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the individual's breach of implied contract charge was not precluded by the sovereign immunity defense. According to the court, an implied contract existed between the district and the individual, who paid an admission fee to use the water park facility where the individual's injury occurred. The court held that sovereign immunity did not bar the action against the district that was brought on a breach of contract theory. Furthermore, the court held that sovereign immunity was waived to the extent that the district was covered by liability insurance. According to the court, the district was amenable to suit to the extent of coverage of any available liability policy or indemnification plan.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which granted the district's motion for summary judgment. The court remanded for a new trial.

 

98 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Mississippi Ins. Guaranty Ass'n v. Byars


NO. 90-CA-1035


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


614 So. 2d 959; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 76



February 25, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 37261 from Judgment dated AUGUST 27, 1990, Fred L. Banks Jr. RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant reinsurer sought review of an order of the Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which granted appellee claimant's motion for summary judgment in the claimant's suit seeking coverage under the Mississippi Insurance Guaranty Association Law.


OVERVIEW: After a claimant had entered into the settlement of a products liability suit with a retailer, it filed a claim with the reinsurer of the retailer's insolvent insurer. However, the reinsurer denied the claim. The claimant filed a suit against the reinsurer seeking coverage under the Mississippi Insurance Guaranty Association Law (MIGA). Both parties filed summary judgment motions, but only the claimant's motion was granted. On appeal, the court affirmed the circuit court's order, holding that the express language of Miss. Code Ann. § 83-23-109(c) of the MIGA required coverage. The court further held that although the retailer may not have been a state resident, it was undisputed that the claimant was a state resident, so coverage was extended under § 83-23-109(c). The court also held that the claimant had not been required to obtain a judgment against the retailer prior to seeking coverage from the reinsurer. Finally, the court held that because of the reinsurer's bad faith denial of the claim, it was bound by the claimant and the retailer's settlement agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the circuit court, which granted a claimant's motion for summary judgment in the claimant's suit against a reinsurer seeking coverage under the Mississippi Insurance Guaranty Association Law.

 

99 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Van Slyke v. Board of Trustees of State Inst. of Higher Learning


NO. 89-CA-0007


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


613 So. 2d 872; 1993 Miss. LEXIS 55



February 11, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 133080 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 30, 1988, James Arden Barnett RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED AS TO ISSUE OF STANDING; AFFIRMED AS TO GRANTING OF SUMMARY JUDGMENT MOTION


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former legislator challenged an order from the Chancery Court for the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee Board of Trustees of State Institutions of Higher Learning in an action challenging the constitutionality of the composition of the board. The trial court held that the former legislator lacked standing to bring the action.


OVERVIEW: The former legislator was involved in protracted legal battle with the board in which he challenged the constitutionality of the composition of the board. The former legislator sought access to documents pertaining to the discipline of computer science as it applied to the University of Southern Mississippi. He was given copies of the non-confidential documents. The former legislator then sought records pertaining to all leadership roles of the three major universities. Upon denial of his request, the former legislator filed a second lawsuit, claiming that denial of his request for documents under the Open Records Act constituted an injury. The trial court held that the former legislator lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the composition of the board. The court disagreed, holding that the state constitution granted citizens the right to challenge the constitutionality and/or review of governmental action. The court, however, affirmed summary judgment in favor of the board because the one-man, one-vote rule did not apply to appointed positions where the choice of members did not involve an election.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the summary judgment order that held that the former legislator lacked standing. The court affirmed that part of the order that held that the board as composed was constitutional.

 

100 of 825 DOCUMENTS


FSC Sec. Corp. v. McCormack


NO. 89-CA-0293


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


1993 Miss. LEXIS 43



February 11, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Withdrawn January 13, 1994. Substituted Opinion of January 13, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Miss. LEXIS 15.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal No. 133530 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 28, 1988, W O DILLARD RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, securities broker-dealer employer whose employee converted a client's funds to his own use, sought review of a Hinds County Chancery Court (Mississippi) judgment, which found the employer vicariously liable for the employee's actions. Appellee investors filed suit against the employee, the employee's corporate entity, various limited partnerships owned or controlled by the employee, and the employer.


OVERVIEW: The employer was held jointly and severally liable with the employee for the investor's actual damages, under the doctrine of respondeat superior, when the trial court found the employee to have been an agent of the employer who acted within the scope of his employment. The court reversed and held that: (1) the trial court made no findings that the employer negligently hired or supervised the employee; (2) there was substantial evidence challenging the reasonableness of the investors' belief in and reliance on the employee's authority from the employer; (3) it was clear that the employee was acting outside the scope of his representative status, that the investors' had notice of this, and that the employer was not vicariously liable for the actions of the employee; (4) absent evidence of the employer's gross negligence, the trial court's decision to award punitive damages against the employer was error; and (5) the trial court's decision to give half the punitive damage award to the state was not founded on statutory or common law authority and was error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered the trial court's judgment, which found the employer vicariously liable for the employee's actions.

Irving v. State


NO. 92-DP-979


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


618 So. 2d 58; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 831



December 31, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 8563 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 13, 1981, Neal Brooks Biggers Jr. RULING JUDGE, Pontotoc County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: Remanded to Pontotoc County Circuit Court for Resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a decision from the Pontotoc County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which denied his motion to vacate his death sentence. The motion was made as a successive writ for post-conviction relief, as provided under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-27(9) (Supp. 1992).


OVERVIEW: After a first federal request for habeas corpus, petitioner's sentence was again presented to a jury. The resentencing jurors were instructed they could consider the "especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel element" as an aggravating circumstance, but it denied petitioner's request to define the meaning of those terms. The jury again assessed the death penalty. Petitioner again exhausted his state remedies and filed a second federal request for habeas corpus. While that was pending, petitioner filed the successive motion to vacate his sentence, asserting that he was entitled to a determination if he was eligible for resentencing based on two recent decisions. Because the decisions did not announce new rules, they were applicable. In one, the court had held that it was error to give the heinous, atrocious, or cruel element instruction without defining the terms. The second case held it was up to the court considering the motion to vacate to determine if the invalid instruction constituted harmless error. No court had yet considered it. The appellate court could not determine what sentence a capital jury would have returned in the absence of the invalid aggravator.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter for resentencing.

 

102 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Bankston v. Pass Rd. Tire Center, Inc.


NO. 07-CA-59544


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


611 So. 2d 998; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 833



December 31, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 18579 from Judgment dated MARCH 18, 1988, JERRY O. TERRY RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, purchaser of tires stolen by false pretenses, filed an action against appellees, owners of store where tires were stolen, police officers, and the city, alleging malicious prosecution and deprivation of property in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi) granted a motion for a directed verdict against the purchaser, holding that his claim was time barred and he had not made a prima facie case.


OVERVIEW: The purchaser bought tires from an individual who obtained the tires from the tire storeowners through the use of worthless checks. The purchaser then sold some of the tires to a third party. The grand jury brought back an indictment against the individual who presented worthless checks and directed that the tires be recovered. The police recovered the tires from the third party and the purchaser. The purchaser won a suit brought by the third party for claim and delivery. The court first reversed the holding that the purchaser's suit was barred by the statute of limitations. The court applied the six-year rule for the § 1983 claim and the one-year rule for the malicious prosecution claim, and found that the purchaser's time to act accrued when the trial court entered a nolle prosequi. The court affirmed the circuit court's holding that the purchaser had not presented a prima facie case of malicious prosecution because he failed to prove one or all of the six elements. The storeowners were not state actors for purposes of the § 1983 claim, and the police officers had qualified immunity. Since the city did not have a policy or custom of the objectionable conduct it was not liable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the directed verdict that held that the purchaser's action was time-barred, but held that the directed verdict was correct as to his claims of malicious prosecution and deprivation of property because he did not make a prima facie showing of the elements of malicious prosecution or of liability under § 1983. There was no abuse of discretion in the denial of attorney's fees on behalf of the defendants.

Ivy v. General Motors Acceptance Corp.


NO. 89-CA-1359


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


612 So. 2d 1108; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 805; 20 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 381



December 17, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 6160 from Judgment dated NOVEMBER 24, 1989, Luther David Pittman RULING JUDGE, Smith County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant delinquent debtor sought review of a decision of the Smith County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which upheld a jury award of actual damages but granted appellee creditor's motion for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict on the punitive damage award after a repossession.


OVERVIEW: Appellant delinquent debtor brought an action against appellee creditor in which he complained about the manner in which appellee repossessed his van. A jury granted appellant actual and punitive damages because it found that the repossession resulted in a breach of the peace and was malicious. The trial court granted appellee's motion for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict on the punitive damages award. The court affirmed the award of actual damages and the denial of punitive damages. The court found that although self-help repossession was permitted in Mississippi, appellee did commit a breach of the peace during the repossession. The court determined that the trial court did not commit any reversible errors during the course of the trial and thus dismissed appellee's arguments in support of a new trial. The court held that because appellant failed to show that the repossession of his van was attended by malice, fraud, or oppression, he was not entitled to punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of actual damages to appellant delinquent debtor for the breach of the peace that occurred during the repossession of a van and affirmed the trial judge's grant of a judgment notwithstanding the verdict to appellee creditor on the award of punitive damages.

Culberson v. State


NO. 90-KA-0651


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


612 So. 2d 342; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 778



December 10, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 23, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 20344 from Judgment dated MAY 11, 1990, Jerry Owen Terry Sr. RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which denied his post conviction request to set aside a 1971 conviction which was used as an aggravating factor justifying the imposition of the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: On March 14, 1989, more than 17 years after entry of his guilty plea to the assault and battery with intent to kill charge, defendant filed a motion pursuant to the provisions of Mississippi's Uniform Post Conviction Collateral Relief Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-1 et seq., (Supp. 1991) to set aside the plea and conviction alleging that he entered his plea of guilty because his attorney had told him he should, and without an understanding of the nature and consequences of that plea. On review, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court found that the trial court properly permitted defendant's 1977 prior conviction to be used as an aggravated circumstance. The time limitation clock prescribed by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) began running in October 1977. Defendant's capital murder conviction or sentence was not actually adversely affected unless and until his prior conviction, used as an aggravating factor, was properly and successfully challenged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for post conviction relief.

Gilliard v. State


NO. 92-KA-1061


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


614 So. 2d 370; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 782



December 10, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 21, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 5553 from Judgment dated OCTOBER 17, 1981, RULING JUDGE, Jones County Circuit Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: DEATH PENALTY VACATED; REMANDED TO JONES COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion under the Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-1 et seq. (Cum. Supp. 1991), to vacate the sentence of death imposed by the Jones County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi). Defendant had pled guilty to capital murder.


OVERVIEW: The state claimed that defendant's petition was barred as a successive writ. Defendant contended that his claims fell under the exceptions to the successive writ bar and the procedural bar contained in the Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act. Specifically, defendant argued that one of the aggravating circumstances submitted to the sentencing jury was that the crime was "especially heinous, atrocious or cruel" but the aggravating circumstance was submitted without a limiting instruction. The court vacated defendant's death penalty and remanded to the circuit court for resentencing. Defendant's capital murder conviction was undisturbed. During defendant's appeals the United State Supreme Court ruled that the aggravating circumstance of "especially heinous, atrocious, and cruel" was unconstitutionally vague when given without a limiting instruction. The court concluded that the Supreme Court's decision was an intervening decision that adversely affected the outcome of defendant's conviction and sentence and excepted defendant from the successive writ bar. Moreover, the procedural bar was not applicable because the issue raised by defendant was of constitutional dimension.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's death sentence and remanded to the circuit court for resentencing. Defendant's capital murder conviction was undisturbed.

 

106 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Saunders v. Alford


NO. 89-CA-185


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


607 So. 2d 1214; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 605



October 8, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 11905 from Judgment dated JUNE 21, 1988, JAMES C SUMMER RULING JUDGE, Leflore County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED ON DIRECT APPEAL AND RENDERED ON CROSS APPEAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lover sought review of the judgment of the Leflore County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which found in favor of appellee husband on his claim against the lover for criminal conversation with the husband's wife.


OVERVIEW: The husband's wife had an affair with the lover for over 20 years. After the husband and wife divorced, the husband instituted an action against the lover, alleging the torts of alienation and criminal conversation. The jury found for the lover on the alienation count, but awarded damages, actual and punitive, to the husband on the conversation count. On appeal, the court reversed and rendered. The court held that the tort of criminal conversation had outlived its usefulness. The tort was not more or less than an act of adultery between the lover and the husband's spouse, and 32 states had already abolished the tort, either by legislative enactment or judicial decree. Mississippi offered no general crime of adultery, nor was there any intent to give an individual a private cause of action in such a case. Because the tort had been created at common law, it could also be taken away at common law, without causing constitutional problems. As such, the court held that it was ceasing to recognize the tort of criminal conversation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment against the lover on the husband's tort claim for criminal conversation.

Cole v. State


NO. 90-KA-1094


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


608 So. 2d 1313; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 557



August 31, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 11, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 895 from Judgment dated AUGUST 13, 1990, Elzy Jonathan Smith Jr. RULING JUDGE, Coahoma County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: LOWER COURT'S DENIAL AND DISMISSAL OF POST-CONVICTION RELIEF AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Coahoma County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which dismissed, as time barred, defendant's motion under the Mississippi Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act (UPCCRA) to vacate and set aside a prior conviction.


OVERVIEW: After a prior manslaughter conviction was used against him during murder sentencing proceedings, defendant filed a motion, pursuant to UPCCRA, to vacate and set aside the prior conviction. The circuit court dismissed the motion as time barred under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-5(2) of UPCCRA. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal. It held that the savings clause provided under Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-59 (Supp. 1991) did not apply to defendant's UPCCRA claim. The court further held that because the savings clause was inapplicable to defendant's claim, the circuit court had properly determined that the claim was barred by the UPCCRA's three-year statute of limitations period. The court also held that the UPCCRA's statute of limitations period did not unconstitutionally suspend the writ of habeas corpus. Finally, the court held that intervening case law had not served as an interruption in the running of the statute of limitations period because the decisions had not adversely affected the outcome of defendant's prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the circuit court, which dismissed, as time barred, defendant's motion, pursuant to the UPCCRA, to vacate and set aside a prior conviction.
