Presley v. Mississippi State Highway Com.


NO. 90-CC-0644


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


608 So. 2d 1288; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 581



August 31, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 8932CP1 from Judgment dated MAY 18, 1990, George C. Carlson Jr. RULING JUDGE, Panola County Circuit Court, First Judicial District



DISPOSITION: Petitions for Rehearing Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, administratrix and as wrongful death beneficiary, sought review of a judgment of the Panola County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that dismissed her wrongful death action against appellee state highway commission on the grounds of appellee's sovereign immunity granted under the Sovereign Immunity Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-1, et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, administratrix and as wrongful death beneficiary, filed a wrongful death action against appellee state highway commission for negligent design of the warning signs at an intersection after her daughter was killed in a car accident. The circuit court sustained defendant's motion to dismiss on the grounds that defendant was immune from suit under section 3 of the Sovereign Immunity Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-6 (Supp. 1991). The court reversed the circuit court judgment, holding that § 11-46-6 was unconstitutional and void to the extent that it required the court to determine sovereign immunity by applying the case law as it existed five years prior to the court's decision in a 1982 case in which the court abolished all judicially-created state and political subdivisions' sovereign immunity existing under the common law of Mississippi. The court held that § 11-46-6 required the court to apply legal principles which the court had specifically rejected and improperly delegated authority to the court which came perilously close to delegation of the power to legislate on the particular subject, which under Miss. Const. art. IV, § 33 only the legislature could do.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment that dismissed the wrongful death action filed by appellant, administratrix and as wrongful death beneficiary, on the grounds of appellee state highway commission's sovereign immunity. The court held that the Sovereign Immunity Act was unconstitutional and void to the extent that it required the court to decide sovereign immunity cases by applying rejected case law. The case was remanded.

OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the lower court erred in determining that the minor was competent to testify and in denying his motion to have the minor evaluated by a competent psychologist. Butler v. State

SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


608 So. 2d 314; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 588



August 26, 1992, Decided

Related proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Butler v. Wallace, 1994 U.S. App. LEXIS 42479 (5th Cir. Miss., Dec. 7, 1994)

Code Ann. § 99-17-20 (Supp. 1991), a criminal procedure statute in capital murder cases. The court also held that defendant's confession was admissible and that she voluntarily waived her Miranda rights.

Reining v. State

SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


606 So. 2d 1098; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 542



August 19, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 3388 from Judgment dated JULY 24, 1989, CLINTON E. LOCKARD RULING JUDGE, George County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the George County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted defendant of simple assault on a law enforcement officer and resisting arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with simple assault on a law enforcement officer and resisting arrest. The trial court convicted defendant. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred when it denied defendant's motion to transcribe the grand jury proceedings. The court held that: (1) defendant did not argue any particularized need that would override the policy of secrecy in grand jury proceedings and it was unlikely that exculpatory evidence would be presented to the grand jury inasmuch as the grand jury heard only the prosecution's side of the story; (2) the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied a change of venue; (3) the statute under which defendant was convicted of simple assault was not unconstitutionally vague; (4) the guilt issue was decided against defendant and the decision was supported by substantial evidence; and (5) there was no merit to defendant's contention that the verdict was against the overwhelming weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

D. L. D. v. Wilkinson County


NO. 91-CA-0325


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


606 So. 2d 1125; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 543



August 19, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 90 from Judgment dated FEBRUARY 21, 1991, John Newton Hudson RULING JUDGE, Wilkinson County Chancery Court-Youth Court Div.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father and appellee state sought review of a decision of Wilkinson County Chancery Court-Youth Court Div. (Mississippi), which limited the father's visitation rights by an order, which was in direct conflict with a chancellor's order of visitation as part of a divorce decree.


OVERVIEW: The youth court adjudicated that the minor child was an abused child. The youth court's order limited the father's visitation rights by an order, which was in direct conflict with a chancellor's order of visitation rights as part of a divorce decree. The conflicting custody decrees in the chancery court and youth court resulted in petitions by each party for contempt being filed in those courts. A petition for writ of prohibition was denied except that the matter was remanded to the youth court for resolution of the conflicting orders. The youth court responded by entering an order reaffirming and ratifying its previous order. On appeal, the order of the youth court was affirmed. The court held that under law the juvenile court had exclusive authority to render its decision concerning the child's custody, in contrast to an earlier superior court decree.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the youth court's decision which limited the father's visitation rights by an order, which was in direct conflict with a chancellor's order of visitation as part of a divorce decree.

Rush v. North American Van Lines, Inc.


NO. 89-CA-0540


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


608 So. 2d 1205; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 488



August 12, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 3485 from Judgment dated APRIL 25, 1989, LARRY E. ROBERTS RULING JUDGE, Kemper County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant debtor sought review of the judgment of the Kemper County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which entered a default judgment against the debtor in the secured creditor's replevin action.


OVERVIEW: The debtor purchased a tractor from the secured creditor for $ 60,195. Through a written security agreement, the debtor granted to the creditor a purchase money security interest in the tractor to secure the performance of his obligations in the premises. Eventually, the debtor stopped making payments and under an acceleration clause in the agreement, the creditor declared the entire unpaid balance past due. On November 22, 1988, the creditor commenced the action. The debtor failed to appear or plead in response to the complaint. On March 21, 1989, the trial court ordered that the debtor had to appear, plead, or have someone appear on his behalf on or before April 5. On April 25, 1989, an attorney finally appeared on behalf of the debtor. The attorney filed a motion to dismiss or a motion for a continuance. The trial court denied the motions and entered default judgment in favor of the creditor. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The debtor had more than ample time to respond to the creditor's complaint. The debtor presented no evidence to reasonably excuse his failure to appear or plead by the court-appointed deadline.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgement of the trial court, which entered a default judgment in favor of the secured creditor in its replevin action.

 

115 of 825 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Mississippi Bureau of Narcotics v. Lincoln County


NO. 90-KA-0112


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


605 So. 2d 802; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 485



August 12, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 10816 from Judgment dated JANUARY 10, 1990, Joe N. Pigott RULING JUDGE, Lincoln County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Mississippi Bureau of Narcotics sought review of a judgment from the Lincoln County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which adjudged the Mississippi forfeiture statutes unconstitutional and invalid where they conflicted with Miss. Const. art. XIV, § 261 and ordered the Bureau to surrender forfeited money to appellee Lincoln County, Mississippi.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered state police to surrender to the county money seized in a drug arrest. After a declaration of the forfeiture of money had been entered and the money distributed pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-181 (Supp. 1990), the Bureau requested amendment of the trial court's order. Instead, the trial court issued an order adjudging the Mississippi forfeiture statutes unconstitutional and invalid where they conflicted with Miss. Const. art. XIV, § 261 and ordered the Bureau to surrender forfeited money to the County. The Bureau appealed. On appeal, the court held that the forfeitures under Miss. Code Ann. §§ 41-29-176 to 41-29-181 (Supp. 1990) were civil in nature and therefore did not conflict with Miss. Const. art. XIV, § 261. The context of § 261 indicated that it applied to fines and forfeitures that were the result of criminal prosecutions. The forfeiture at issue was against the property and not as a penalty upon conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and rendered the trial court's judgment, which had adjudged the Mississippi forfeiture statutes unconstitutional and invalid where they conflicted with the Mississippi Constitution and ordered the Bureau to surrender forfeited money to the County.

 

116 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Hewlett v. State


NO. 89-KA-1105


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


607 So. 2d 1097; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 451



August 5, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 12573 form Judgment dated APRIL 14, 1989, Robert Kenneth Coleman RULING JUDGE, Lafayette County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Lafayette County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him on three counts of manslaughter and sentenced him to three consecutive 20-year terms as a habitual offender for the deaths of three family members in an automobile collision that resulted from defendant's criminal negligence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on three counts for the killing of three members of a family while driving drunk. He was found guilty of manslaughter on all three counts and he was also found to be a habitual offender. Defendant was sentenced to three consecutive 20-year sentences. On appeal, defendant complained of eight errors in the trial and sentence. The court affirmed because the trial court had not improperly excluded evidence that the deaths were caused by defects in the decedents' car. In addition, the admission of photographs of the victims in connection with the medical examiners testimony was not unduly prejudicial but the use of a photograph of defendant was not relevant, although it was not prejudicial. The court held that the admission of evidence of other crimes was irrelevant but was not prejudicial. Corroborated evidence of defendant's driving behavior just before the accident was properly admitted. As to the sentences, the fact that defendant had not served prior felony sentences in prison was irrelevant under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 (Supp. 1991), there was no evidence that his prior guilty pleas were not voluntary, and the sentences were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the offense of manslaughter and sentence of three consecutive 20-year terms of imprisonment as a habitual offender.

 

117 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Abram v. State


NO. 03-DP-55


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


606 So. 2d 1015; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 448



July 29, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 388412 from Judgment dated APRIL 19, 1984, MICHAEL R. EUBANKS RULING JUDGE, Marion County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: Conviction of Capital Murder Reversed; Sentence of Death Vacated and Set Aside and this Cause is Remanded to the Circuit Court of Marion County for such Further Proceedings as may be appropriate.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Marion County Circuit Court (Mississippi) entered judgment upon a jury verdict convicting defendant of capital murder and sentencing defendant to the death penalty, but subsequently held that the jury's sentence of death was unconstitutional and sentenced defendant to life without parole pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-107 (Supp. 1991). Defendant appealed, and the state cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two victims were murdered during the course of an armed robbery in which defendant participated. Defendant's conviction was based upon his confession. The evidence revealed that a sheriff obtained warrants for defendant's arrest on the basis of information provided by confidential informants. Defendant was taken into custody and confessed after three days of incarceration and repeated interrogation. Defendant was also given a polygraph test. Defendant was not provided with an initial appearance or access to counsel until after he had confessed. The court reversed defendant's conviction, vacated and set aside his death sentence, and remanded. Defendant's confession was involuntary and inadmissible because (1) it was proximately caused by improper inducements and promises by law enforcement interrogators and third parties, (2) defendant had not voluntarily waived his rights to remain silent and to counsel, and (3) the state failed to provide defendant with a prompt initial hearing. Moreover, the trial court erred in setting aside defendant's death sentence because the evidence justified the jury's finding that defendant possessed the necessary level of culpability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of capital murder, vacated and set aside defendant's sentence of death, and remanded the cause to the trial court for further appropriate proceedings.

 

118 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Ross v. State


NO. 89-KA-0069


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


605 So. 2d 17; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 419



July 22, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Ross v. Jenkins, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 33761 (N.D. Miss., May 24, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Ross v. Jenkins, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 53891 (N.D. Miss., Aug. 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 5568 from Judgment dated SEPTEMBER 29, 1988, WILLIAM R. LAMB RULING JUDGE, Tippah County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Tippah County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of rape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of rape. He appealed, alleging constitutional and statutory speedy trial violations. The court held that the 378-day delay from arrest to trial constituted a presumptively prejudicial delay, so that the State bore the burden of proving no prejudice to defendant. The court noted the four events that caused the delay of defendant's trial: first, defendant moved for a change of venue, which tolled the clock; second, the State successfully moved for a continuance, which did not toll the clock; third, defendant moved to suppress identification, which tolled the clock and caused defendant to miss a trial date; and last, the missed trial date pushed the trial into the next term, several months away. The court found that no constitutional or statutory right to a speedy trial was denied defendant because, despite the fact that he went to trial 378 days after his arrest, his constitutional speedy trial clock ran for only 164 days, or just over five months.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Towner v. Moore


NO. 90-CC-0875


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


604 So. 2d 1093; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 424



July 22, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 6217 from Judgment dated JULY 09, 1990, John L. Pearson RULING JUDGE, Quitman County Circuit Court



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant spouses sought review of the judgment of the Quitman County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that entered judgment in favor of plaintiff school district in a suit in which the spouses were accused of violating a law proscribing an employment contract wherein a public school board employed one whose spouse was a member of the board.


OVERVIEW: The spouses were employees of a school district. The trial court found that the state constitution proscribed an employment contract wherein a public school board employed one whose spouse was a member of the board. The spouses contended that Miss. Code Ann § 25-4-109 and Miss. Code Ann § 25-4-113 were separate and distinct claims which could not be joined in one action because they required different burdens of proof. The court was of the opinion that this contention was meritless. The court held where there were no genuine issues of material fact and no necessity for trial by it, the trial court was not concerned with the burden of proof because there were no issues to be tried. The spouses argued that summary judgment was not applicable to their proceeding. The court held there was no violation of the right of trial by jury when judgment was entered summarily in cases where there was no genuine issue of material fact and the moving party was entitled to judgment as a matter of law. The court held that the spouses' actions had violated the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which found that the spouses' had violated the law.

 

120 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Pinkney v. State


No. 03-DP-761


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


602 So. 2d 1177; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 384



June 24, 1992, DECIDED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at Pinkney v. State, 2000 Miss. LEXIS 95 (Miss., Apr. 20, 2000)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Pinkney v. State, 2015 Miss. App. LEXIS 614 (Miss. Ct. App., Nov. 24, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 4000 from Judgment dated July 26, 1985, L. BRELAND HILBURN RULING JUDGE, Hinds County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District
Pinkney v. Mississippi, 494 U.S. 1075, 110 S. Ct. 1800, 108 L. Ed. 2d 931, 1990 U.S. LEXIS 1903 (1990)



DISPOSITION: REMANDED TO HINDS COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT, SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT, FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death, and his conviction and sentence were affirmed by the court. Defendant, thereafter, sought en banc review of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: The court had no authority to uphold a death sentence in the light of an invalid or improperly defined aggravating circumstance by reweighing remaining aggravating circumstances, nor was there authority to find evidence to support a proper definition of an aggravating circumstance in order to uphold a death sentence by reweighing. Only the jury could impose the death penalty as to aggravating circumstances. The court had authority to determine if the evidence supported the finding of a statutory aggravating circumstance. Neither was there authority for the court to find evidence to support a proper definition of an aggravating circumstance in order to uphold a death sentence by reweighing. As to harmless error, it was a duty of the court to find whether the error that occurred during sentencing was harmless. Because it had no authority as a matter of state law to engage in a reweighing analysis, and because it declined to engage in harmless error analysis, the court held that it was for a jury to decide under the facts of the case and with proper and properly defined aggravating circumstances, weighed against mitigating circumstances, whether defendant should be sentenced to death.


OUTCOME: The court remanded to the circuit court for resentencing.

Fleming v. State

OVERVIEW: Defendant and his two codefendants attacked and robbed a truck driver. The State introduced the testimony of material rebuttal witnesses, whom the State failed to disclose to defendant's counsel in violation of the rules of discovery. However, the court was not permitted to reverse on such grounds because defendant failed to object to the witnesses' testimony. The court determined that defendant could not complain about the introduction of his prior felony convictions because he testified to such during his direct examination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for strong-arm robbery and aggravated assault.

 

122 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


No. 03-DP-601


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


602 So. 2d 1170; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 345



June 10, 1992, DECIDED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 2357 from Judgment dated APRIL 03, 1985, J. Ruble Griffin RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District



DISPOSITION: REMANDED TO HARRISON COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Supreme Court remanded a decision of the court for reconsideration, which affirmed the trial court's conviction for capital murder and sentence of death imposed on defendant after the jury found insufficient mitigating circumstances despite a limiting instruction offered by defendant, which was denied by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by the jury of capital murder and sentenced to death. The jury was allowed to consider the aggravating circumstance that the crime was "especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel" along with two others, "engaged in the commission of a robbery" and "committed for pecuniary gain." There was no limiting instruction given in conjunction with the "especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel" aggravating circumstance. The Supreme Court granted certiorari and remanded to the court to reconsider the issue of aggravating circumstance in light of its opinion in another case. The issue was whether in the face of the invalid aggravating circumstance the court could nonetheless uphold defendant's death sentence or whether the case should be remanded for resentencing. The court held while the conviction could remain undisturbed, the court was not convinced beyond a reasonable doubt that under the facts, the jury would have found that the actual commission of the capital felony was accompanied by such additional acts as to set the crime apart from the norm of capital felonies as a conscienceless or pitiless crime which was unnecessarily tortious to the victim.


OUTCOME: The court remanded to the trial court to impanel another sentencing jury to determine punishment consistent with the court's opinion.

Odom v. Raypress Corp.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which entered judgment for plaintiff in plaintiff's replevin action that resulted in the seizure of property allegedly owned by defendant, contending that the judgment was erroneously based upon Miss Code Ann. § 11-37-101 (1972), which was declared unconstitutional.

In re Appeal of Final Decisions of Public Service Com.


91-CC-0033


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


604 So. 2d 218; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 192



April 22, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 89111058 from Judgment date DECEMBER 05, 1990, Dennis M. Baker RULING JUDGE, DeSoto County Chancery Court



DISPOSITION: LOWER COURT'S DECISION VACATED AND APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant North Mississippi Utility Company (NMUC) sought review of a judgment of the DeSoto County Chancery Court (Mississippi), which declared the notice provisions of the Rules and Regulations of the Public Service Commission (PSC) and applicable parts of the Mississippi Code unconstitutional for lack of procedural due process to NMUC's customers. Appellee customers supported affirmance.


OVERVIEW: NMUC filed notices of intent to increase rates. The PSC reviewed the notice and entered a suspension order. The commission received numerous telephone calls and letters of protest from the customers objecting to the increase. Notice of the rate change was published in a major newspaper pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 77-3-47 (1991) advising of the right to intervene. No customer, however, intervened or sought intervention pursuant to the PSC rules. The chancery court found in favor of the customers in their appeal of the PSC's order setting rates and charges. NMUC and the PSC asserted that the chancery court erred in determining that the notice provisions of the Public Utilities Act and the PSC's rules were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed due to a lack of jurisdiction in the chancery court. The court determined that the customers failed to avail themselves of their rights to intervene. The court concluded that their failure to do so was fatal because having failed to intervene, they never became parties. They were not, therefore, a "party aggrieved by any final finding" and had no right to appeal from the final order of the PSC.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the chancery court and dismissed the proceedings for want of jurisdiction.

Scott v. Ball


NO. 90-CA-0508


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


595 So. 2d 848; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 92



February 26, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 6842 from Judgment dated MARCH 01, 1990, Andrew Cleveland Baker RULING JUDGE, Panola County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant widow sought review of a judgment of the Panola County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District (Mississippi) that was in favor of appellee doctor in the widow's wrongful death malpractice action. The widow claimed that the trial judge erred in failing to exclude certain jurors for cause and in allowing the doctor to exercise peremptory challenges to exclude African American jurors.


OVERVIEW: During jury selection, the widow, who was African American, challenged for cause several potential jurors because they or their family members had been treated by the doctor. The trial court sustained some of the challenges and denied others. The doctor, who was Caucasian, exercised all of his peremptory challenges to exclude African Americans from the jury. When asked to state a racially neutral basis for the challenges, the doctor's attorney stated that he had not challenged other African Americans. The trial court determined that a racially neutral basis for the peremptory challenges was unnecessary in a civil case. On appeal, the court held that although the trial court may have erred in failing to excuse a juror for cause, the error was not a basis for reversal because the widow could have had him excused on a peremptory challenge. However, the court held that the failure to show a race neutral reason for using peremptory challenges to exclude the African Americans from the jury warranted a new trial although in some cases only an evidentiary hearing was necessary to determine the existence of a race neutral basis for the peremptory challenges.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that was in favor of the doctor in the widow's medical malpractice wrongful death action.

 

126 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Patterson v. State


No. 91-KP-0606


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


594 So. 2d 606; 1992 Miss. LEXIS 42



January 29, 1992, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [**1] DENIAL OF MOTION TO VACATE GUILTY PLEA, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Lamar County (Mississippi) that denied his motion to vacate his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to armed robbery and was incarcerated at a state correctional facility. He filed a motion to vacate his guilty plea, which the circuit court denied. Defendant appealed. In affirming, the court concluded that defendant's application for post-conviction relief was time barred under the Post-Conviction Relief Act, § 99-39-5, Mississippi Code 1972 Annotated. The act applied prospectively from its date of enactment, and individuals convicted prior to that date had three years from the enactment date to petition for post-conviction relief. Where defendant's motion was filed more than four years after the enactment date, it was untimely. The court refused to consider defendant's argument that the statute was unconstitutional. The court could not pass upon a question that was not raised before the circuit court, and the rule that questions not raised in the lower court would not be reviewed on appeal was particularly true where constitutional questions were involved. Such questions were waived if not asserted at the trial level.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's motion to vacate his guilty plea was affirmed.

Hansen v. State


NO. 89-DP-0823


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


592 So. 2d 114; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 876



December 18, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Substituted Opinion of December 18, 1991, Reported at 1991 Miss. LEXIS 876. Rehearing Denied December 18, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 22133 from Judgment dated OCTOBER 30, 1987, James E. Thomas RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Opinion of September 11, 1991, Reported at 1991 Miss. LEXIS 605.



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR REHEARING DENIED; OPINION MODIFIED; CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of a Harrison County Circuit Court of the First Judicial District (Mississippi) that convicted him for capital murder and sentenced him to death. On appeal, he raised several contentions regarding whether his substantial right to a fair trial might have been compromised during either the guilty or penalty phase of his trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the capital murder of a state trooper, and the jury sentenced him to death. On appeal, defendant raised several contentions regarding whether his substantial right to a fair trial was compromised during either the guilt or penalty phase of his trial. On appeal, the trial court reviewed all of defendant's claimed errors relative to the guilt phase of his trial and determined that any viable claims of error merely constituted harmless errors that did not require reversal. Notably, the court concluded that prosecution should not have been permitted to question a witness on her statement in offense of defendant's Confrontation Clause rights under state and federal constitutions; however, overwhelming evidence in support of defendant's guilt rendered the error harmless. Additionally, the court determined that the trial court made no errors in the penalty phase of defendant's trial. Accordingly, the trial court's conviction and sentence were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of conviction and capital sentence was affirmed. The trial court did not commit any errors during either the guilt or penalty phases of his capital murder trial that compromised defendant's substantial right to fair trial. Prosecution's improper questioning of witness on her statement in offense of defendant's Confrontation Clause rights constituted harmless error.

Jones v. State


No. 90-CA-0730


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


607 So. 2d 23; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 985



December 18, 1991, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [**1] AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant arrestee appealed a decision of a trial court (Mississippi), which granted a petition by plaintiff State of Mississippi seeking civil forfeiture of property found in the arrestee's automobile following his arrest for possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee was stopped for speeding. While writing the citation, the officer was informed that the arrestee had previously been convicted of controlled substance possession. The officer asked the arrestee, who at that time was not under arrest, to sign a consent form for a vehicle search, which the arrestee did. An arrest was made after the arrestee admitted that a marijuana cigarette was his and a large amount of money was found. The arrestee claimed that he had asked continuously for an attorney. The trial court granted the State's petition for forfeiture of the cash found and on appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the arrestee's consent to the search was valid. The arrestee did not put on any proof of duress or coercion. The only evidence presented to support the arrestee's contention that the search was invalid was his own testimony, which the trial court had the sole authority of judging for veracity. The arrestee was informed of his right to consent and he was Mirandized after being detained. Finally, the State met its burden of proof pursuant to the Mississippi Uniform Controlled Substance Law and demonstrated that the currency was forfeitable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the forfeiture ordered by the trial court.

 

130 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Nichols v. Gulfport


NO. 89-CA-0123


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


589 So. 2d 1280; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 796



November 20, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 92215 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 21, 1988, MICHAEL L. CARR RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lounge complained of the decision of the Harrison County Chancery Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which upheld appellee city's noise ordinance, Gulfport, Miss., Ordinance No. 628.


OVERVIEW: The lounge brought a lawsuit against the city which challenged the constitutionality of the city's noise ordinance. The owners had been arrested on multiple occasions and complained that they could not know when the noise from their lounge was so loud as to violate the ordinance. The police chief testified that the ordinance was enforced strictly dependent on the sensitivity of the complainant, that no objective criteria were employed. The trial court upheld the ordinance. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court and rendered judgment in favor of the lounge. The court held that, where a statute has a standard which is subjective, and can be interpreted differently by some people as opposed to others, the statute effectively has no standard at all. The court noted that a noise ordinance touches the first amendment freedom of speech and, as such, is subjected to heightened scrutiny. The court noted the testimony of the police chief, who admitted that the interpretation of the ordinance depended on what any given complainant considered "annoying". The court held § 1 of the ordinance did not give adequate notice of the conduct which was being prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, ruled that the city's noise ordinance was unconstitutionally vague, and rendered judgment in favor of the lounge.

Flores v. State


No. 89-KA-1083


Supreme Court of Mississippi


586 So. 2d 811; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 671



September 18, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 3984 from Judgment dated February 19, 1986, L. Breland Hilburn Ruling Judge, Hinds County Circuit Court, Second Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND APPELLANT DISCHARGED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Hinds County (Mississippi) convicting him of conspiracy to distribute more than one kilogram of marijuana and sentencing him to 15 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his co-defendant were convicted of conspiracy to distribute more than one kilogram of marijuana and were sentenced. On appeal, the court reversed and discharged defendant because the State failed to prosecute him within 270 days in violation of the Mississippi speedy trial statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-17-1 (Supp. 1990). A continuance sought by the co-defendant was attributable to the State, which resulted in the State violating the statutory 270-day rule by 19 days. Thus, defendant was denied a speedy trial and was entitled to have his conviction reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and discharged him.

 

132 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Fisher v. Eupora


Nos. 89-KA-1066, 89-KA-1067 Consolidated


Supreme Court of Mississippi


587 So. 2d 878; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 669



September 18, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal Nos. 3096, 3089 from Judgment dated September 28, 1989, James C. Sumner Ruling Judge, Webster County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF DRIVING UNDER THE INFLUENCE OF INTOXICATING LIQUOR AND SENTENCE OF NINE (9) MONTHS IN THE COUNTY JAIL AFFIRMED AS TO LENARD FISHER; CONVICTION OF DRIVING UNDER THE INFLUENCE OF INTOXICATING LIQUOR AND SENTENCE OF NINE (9) MONTHS IN THE COUNTY JAIL AFFIRMED AS TO LARRY D. WALLS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, defendants sought review of the judgments by the Webster County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which affirmed defendants' convictions on separate charges of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquors in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 63-31(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: A defendant contended the breath test was given with less than a 15-minute observation period from the time of the arrest when the testing procedures required a 20-minute period. The court held there was no merit with the issue, as the officer was not required to stare at defendant and there was 15 minutes between the arrest and administration of the test and the defendant was observed for at least 8 to 10 minutes prior to arrest. Both defendants contended they were denied due process when their request for the appointment of an expert in the field of the testing device was denied. The court held there was no abuse of discretion, as defendants had the state's experts who were available for rigorous cross-examination. The court determined the sentences, three-months in excess of the six-month maximum under Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30(1)(c) (Supp. 1988), were proper, as the sentences were within the maximum allowed under Miss. Code Ann. § 21-13-19. Also, when defendants filed their appeals for trial de novo in the circuit court, they took the chance the penalties would have been enhanced. Finally, in affirming, the court held the intoxilyzer test was valid and properly administered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions on separate charges of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquors.

 

133 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Hansen v. State


No. 89-DP-0823


Supreme Court of Mississippi


1991 Miss. LEXIS 605



September 11, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Substituted Opinion of December 18, 1991, Reported at 1991 Miss. LEXIS 876. Rehearing Denied December 18, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from No. 22133 from Judgment dated October 30, 1987, James E. Thomas Ruling Judge, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH AFFIRMED. WEDNESDAY, OCTOBER 30, 1991, SET FOR EXECUTION OF SENTENCE IN THE MANNER PROVIDED BY LAW.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi) that convicted him for capital murder and sentenced him to death. On appeal, he raised several contentions regarding whether his substantial right to a fair trial might have been compromised during either the guilt or penalty phase of his trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the capital murder of a state trooper, and the jury sentenced him to death. On appeal, defendant raised several contentions regarding whether his substantial right to a fair trial was compromised. The court determined that any viable claims of error merely constituted harmless error that did not require reversal. Notably, the court held that: (1) although the circuit court erred when it denied defendant's motion for a preliminary hearing, the error was harmless; (2) although the circuit court erred when it refused defendant's request for voir dire examination of two prospective jurors who had stated their opposition to the death penalty, the error was harmless; and (3) although the circuit court's error in allowing the prosecution to attempt a cross-examination of defendant's adverse witness, who invoked her self-incrimination privilege, regarding her prior statement to a police officer offended defendant's Confrontation Clause rights, the error was harmless. The court concluded that overwhelming evidence in support of defendant's guilt rendered the errors harmless. Accordingly, the circuit court's conviction and sentence were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's capital murder conviction and death sentence.

Holland v. State


No. 90-DP-0024


Supreme Court of Mississippi


587 So. 2d 848; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 648



September 11, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Holland v. State, 705 So. 2d 307, 1997 Miss. LEXIS 388 (Miss., 1997)
Rehearing denied by Holland v. State, 2010 Miss. LEXIS 249 (Miss., May 20, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from No. 22497 from Judgment dated December 11, 1987, Kosta N. Vlahos Ruling Judge, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: GUILT PHASE: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AFFIRMED.

SENTENCING PHASE: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which convicted him of killing a 15-year old girl with malice aforethought while engaged in the commission of the crime and felony of rape as a felony offender.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the conviction but reversed the sentence of death and remanded for re-sentencing. The court held that defendant's utterance regarding the possible exercise of his right to an attorney during questioning was ambiguous, but that the detectives properly clarified the ambiguity, and thereafter, defendant waived his Miranda rights and the confession was properly admitted. The court held that evidentiary rulings were proper with respect to: 1) exclusion of impeachment testimony of another witness's alleged sexual fantasies of the victim; 2) the admission of a video of the burial site and a wash cloth found there, which were inadmissible but harmless error; 3) admission of a doctor's opinions as to the time of bruising, which objection was waived; and 4) the timeliness of rape kit samples. The court held that instructions on the lesser included offense of manslaughter were properly denied. However, the court held that the jury's premature decision to impose the death sentence, which came after the guilt phase but before the sentencing phase, constituted reversible error where the trial court's instruction was insufficient to insure defendant's right to a fair hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of capital murder but reversed the sentence of death and remanded the matter for re-sentencing.

 

135 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Threlkeld v. State


No. 90-CA-0091


Supreme Court of Mississippi


586 So. 2d 756; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 533



August 21, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 23, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 12164 from Judgment dated January 02, 1990, Robert Kenneth Coleman Ruling Judge, Lafayette County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded for Proceedings Consistent with Opinion of this Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lafayette County (Mississippi), which forfeited the owner's pick-up truck and rifle seized by appellee Department of Wildlife Fisheries and Parks for the State of Mississippi.


OVERVIEW: An officer of the Department seized the owner's property after observing her son "headlighting" deer in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 49-7-103 (1972). The owner initiated judicial review of the proposed administrative forfeiture. The trial court upheld the forfeiture because there was not an innocent owner exception § 49-7-103 (1972). On review, the court reversed because Miss. Const. art. 3 § 14 stated that no person shall be deprived of life, liberty, or property except by due process of law. Read literally, Miss. Code Ann. §§ 49-7-251 to 257 (1972) was violative of the Mississippi Constitution's due process guarantee. The court construed the statute to include an innocent owner exception. Moreover, forfeiture statutes were penal in nature and had to be strictly construed. The burden was upon the State to prove forfeiture by a preponderance of the evidence. The State failed to present evidence sufficient to meet that burden.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Department's order of forfeiture of the owner's property and remand for proceedings consistent with the opinion.

McDonald's Corp. v. Robinson Indus.


No. 07-CA-59270, 07-CA-59419 (Consolidated)


Supreme Court of Mississippi


592 So. 2d 927; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 526



August 21, 1991, Decided


NOTICE: Petition for Rehearing Denied February 12, 1992.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied February 12, 1992. As Amended February 12, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 134855 from Judgment dated April 06, 1988, Stuart Robinson Ruling Judge, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.

Appeal No. I-1059 from Judgment dated April 27, 1988, Jack A. Travis Ruling Judge, Hinds County Special Court of Eminent Domain, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRM DISMISSAL OF CHANCERY COURT ACTION; REVERSE AND RENDER AS TO RULE 11 SANCTIONS; REVERSE AND REMAND TO SPECIAL COURT OF EMINENT DOMAIN TO PROCEED IN A MANNER NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.

AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART; AND REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an owner and its lessee, sought review of the condemnation award in the Special Court of Eminent Domain in the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), in a retrial, on remand, of appellee highway commission's action. The owner also appealed the order of the Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District, which dismissed the owner's suit to determine title in the subject property and sanctioned the owner.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were awarded compensation in a condemnation action for property located on a frontage road to a highway. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for a retrial, finding that the owner had only a revocable permit giving it access to the frontage road and that appellants were paid for property they did not own. The owner filed suit in chancery court to prove that it had been deeded access rights to the road and asked to enjoin the retrial until these rights were determined. The chancery court dismissed the suit and imposed sanctions under Miss. R. Civ. P. 11. The eminent domain court awarded compensation based on the permit rights. In consolidated appeals, the court affirmed the chancery court's dismissal order, but reversed the order imposing sanctions when the owner in good faith believed that the chancery court had the sole jurisdiction to try title. Also, the court held that the eminent domain court was allowed to decide questions of title on the basis of pendent jurisdiction. The eminent domain court's decision was reversed and the matter was remanded for a determination of the owner's title claims when adherence to the prior ruling on appeal worked an injustice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the chancery court's decision to dismiss the owner's action to try title in property subject to the highway commission's condemnation action, but reversed the chancery court's imposition of sanctions against the owner and rendered judgment as to these sanctions. The court reversed the condemnation award rendered by the eminent domain court and remanded the matter for further consistent proceedings.

Board of Educ. v. Hudson


No. 07-CA-58804


Supreme Court of Mississippi


585 So. 2d 683; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 460



July 31, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 18, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 12135 from Judgment dated July 23, 1987, Sebe Dale, Jr Ruling Judge, Lamar County Chancery Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered as to Validity of the Lease; Reversed and Remanded to Board of Education of Lamar County for Initiation of Appraisal Procedure; Reversed as to Chancery Court costs which were taxed to the Board of Education.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court of Lamar County (Mississippi) denied appellant county board of education's request for relief in its action to void appellee's leasehold of Sixteenth-Section School Trust Land and confirmed appellee's leasehold. Appellant challenged that decision.


OVERVIEW: Appellant county board of education (board) filed an action seeking to void appellee's leasehold of Sixteenth-Section School Trust Land which had been originally leased by another individual for a fee alleged to be unconscionably and unconstitutionally low. Specifically, 3.5 acres had originally been leased for 99 years at a one-time fee of $ 150, and appellee acquired 2.5 of the 3.5 acres for a one-time fee of $ 45,000. The Board contended specifically that Hudson's leasehold should be declared void because the original conveyance was so low that it constituted a donation in violation of Miss. Const. art. IV, § 95. The court reversed the chancery court's denial of the relief sought by the board. The court held that, as a matter of law, a one-time leasehold fee of a nominal 46 cents per acre per year was inadequate consideration and was essentially an illegal donation of land held in the public trust. Mere compliance with statutory formalities and procedures did not vitiate substantive violation of constitutional prohibitions. Pursuant to state constitutional dictates, the common law of trusts, and prior decisions of the court, the leasehold was declared void.


OUTCOME: The court declared appellee's lease void, reversed and remanded to appellant county board of education for the initiation of an appraisal procedure, and reversed the decision of the chancery court. During the appraisal process, appellee was to remain in possession of the leasehold and have the right of first refusal.

Willie v. State


No. 89-DP-1285


Supreme Court of Mississippi


585 So. 2d 660; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 454



July 24, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Willie v. State, 738 So. 2d 217, 1999 Miss. LEXIS 163 (Miss., 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 11694 from Judgment dated September 28, 1989, Harvey S. Buck Ruling Judge, Oktibbeha County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AFFIRMED. SENTENCE OF DEATH REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR A NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court of Oktibbeha County (Mississippi), for capital murder and sentence of death by lethal injection.


OVERVIEW: Found guilty of killing a store owner while committing a robbery, defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. After finding that no errors in the guilt phase required reversal, the court held that the trial judge abused his discretion by restricting defendant's closing argument during the sentencing phase to 15 minutes instead of allowing the additional time requested. The court was unable to conclude that defendant's right to be heard was not impaired. By offering to read to the trial court portions of his closing argument that he never had time to say, defendant clearly demonstrated that he was prejudiced by not being allowed to make a full and complete closing argument. The court ruled that the two instructions, that the capital murder was committed for pecuniary gain and that the capital murder was committed while in the commission of a robbery, were improperly given as separate and distinct aggravating circumstances. When life was at stake, a jury was not to be allowed the opportunity to doubly weigh the commission of the underlying felony and the motive behind the underlying felony as separate aggravators. The decision was to be prospective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment of conviction but reversed the sentence of death and remanded for a new sentencing trial. The court further directed that the jury instruction be revised.

Ladner v. State

Supreme Court of Mississippi

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for capital murder and death sentence from the Hancock County Circuit Court (Mississippi), alleging that the lower court erred in refusing to allow him to inform the jury that he was ineligible for parole even though at that time in the trial the court had not adjudicated his habitual offender status.


OVERVIEW: At the sentencing phase, defense counsel requested an instruction that defendant was a habitual offender and would not be eligible for parole, but withdrew the instruction prior to argument. There was no ruling on that instruction by the lower court. During oral argument, counsel for the defense attempted to argue the fact of no parole to the jury, if it returned a verdict imposing life imprisonment. Defendant's status as a habitual offender was uncertain during the sentencing phase. The habitual offender hearing was held after the jury retired to consider its verdict. No ruling was rendered on the habitual offender status by the lower court until after the jury returned with its sentence of death. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in refusing to allow him to inform the jury that he was ineligible for parole. The court held that the identical issue had been recently decided against the state in two other cases. Therefore, the sentence and judgment imposing the death penalty were reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed on the guilt phase of defendant's capital murder trial and was reversed and remanded for a new trial on the sentencing phase.

Vance v. Lincoln County Dep't of Public Welfare


No. 89-CA-1173


Supreme Court of Mississippi


582 So. 2d 414; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 360



June 5, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 26524 from Judgment Dated September 18, 1989, Michael L. Carr, Jr., Ruling Judge, Lincoln County Chancery Court.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mother sought review of the decision of the Lincoln County Chancery Court (Mississippi) that terminated her parental rights to two of her minor children in the action of plaintiff, Lincoln County Department of Human Services, brought pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 93-15-103 (Supp. 1987), seeking to terminate the mother's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the evidence did not support a finding that her parental rights should have been terminated and that § 93-15-103 was unconstitutionally vague and violated her equal protection rights. The court affirmed the judgment, finding ample evidence that the relationship between the mother and the minor children was practically non-existent. The court explained that the consequence of the mother's incarceration for murder and armed robbery was tantamount to an abandonment. The court noted that § 93-15-103 permitted a court to consider a parent's long term imprisonment in reaching a decision regarding the termination of that parent's parental rights. The court found that § 93-15-103(3) was not vague, explaining that a rule was not objectionable merely because it was stated in general terms and was not susceptible of precise application. The court found that § 93-15-103 was racial neutral on its face and, as such, that the mother had the burden of showing that there was a racially discriminatory intent or purpose behind the statute in order to show a violation of the right of equal protection. The court stated that the mother failed to meet that burden.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Carson v. Natchez Children's Home


No. 90-CA-0142


Supreme Court of Mississippi


580 So. 2d 1248; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 304

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff children's home filed an action against defendant mother seeking to terminate her parental rights under Miss. Code Ann. § 93-15-103(3)(b). The Adams County Chancery Court (Mississippi) entered a judgment terminating the mother's rights, and she appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother was a victim of sexual abuse. She placed her children in the care of the children's home because she did not have the financial means to provide for them. Later, adults began to report that the children were engaging in sexualized play and showing other signs of sexual abuse. When the children were questioned, they reported that the mother and others had engaged in various sexual acts with them on numerous occasions. An expert witness testified that it was his opinion that the children had been the victims of sexual abuse and that it would be in the best interests of the children for them to be separated in order to prevent future sexual activity between them. The mother claimed that the judgment terminating her rights and separating the children was improper. The court held that (1) the findings that the children were sexually abused and that the mother was a participant were supported by the record; and (2) the evidence of sexual abuse was sufficient for termination of the mother's parental rights under Miss. Code Ann. § 93-15-103(3)(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment terminating the mother's parental rights.

Smith v. Estate of King


No. 07-CA-59300


Supreme Court of Mississippi


579 So. 2d 1250; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 250



April 24, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. P234 from Judgment Dated March 31, 1988, John S. Morris Ruling Judge, Harrison County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded in Part; Reversed and Rendered in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant potential heir, the illegitimate daughter of the decedent, sought review of an order of the Harrison County Chancery Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which found that no fraud had been perpetrated on the lower court by appellee administratrix for failing to disclose the potential heir's existence to the lower court.


OVERVIEW: Following the court's earlier remand after holding that the administratrix had had an affirmative duty to disclose the existence of known potential heirs and claimants to the lower court, the lower court found that the administratrix's failure to notify the lower court of the potential heir had not been fraudulent. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment, holding that the lower court erred in determining that the administratrix had not committed a fraud. The administratrix, to her benefit, failed to use reasonable diligence to ascertain potential heirs and to file their names in the lower court pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 91-7-293 (1972). The administratrix knew of the potential heir, but determined that she was not an heir and forwent having the lower court adjudicate the heirs until the potential heir was barred by the 90-day nonclaim statute. Further, the court held that the administratrix was required to provide actual notice to known or reasonably known ascertainable illegitimate children who were potential heirs and whose claims would have been barred by the running of the 90-day period under Miss. Code Ann. § 91-1-15(3)(c) (1990).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment that no fraud had been perpetrated on the lower court by the administratrix for failing to disclose the existence of a potential heir. The court further held that the administratrix was required to provide actual notice to the potential heir whose claim would have been barred by the running of the 90-day period from the publication notice.

Supreme Court of Mississippi

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdraw Opinion of April 4, 1990, Reported at 1990 Miss. LEXIS 195.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation filed a bill of complaint to confirm and quiet the interest conveyed under an oil and gas lease pursuant to Miss Code Ann. § 11-17-29 and § 29-3-103. The County Chancery Court, Second Judicial District (Mississippi) held that the corporation had no right under the oil and gas lease to explore, over 25 years later, for oil and gas. The corporation appealed and defendant state and superintendent cross appealed.


OVERVIEW: After compliance with Miss. Code Ann. § 6600, the superintendent executed an oil and gas lease to a third party. The county received a bonus for executing the lease. Moreover, defendants asked for an accounting. The chancery court held that the corporation could not have retained indefinitely all undeveloped areas of the lease and thereby cancelled the oil, gas, and mineral lease as to all non-producing areas and horizons. On appeal, the court held that § 211 limited sixteenth section land leases (including mineral leases) to a maximum term of 25- years. However, the court held that the chancery court's decision to favor economic realties and not award an accounting was an error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the chancery court's decision with respect to the corporation's rights to the leased property. However, the court reversed and remanded the chancery court's decision denying the state's and superintendent's request for accounting.

State ex rel. Moore v. Molpus


No. 90-CA-696


Supreme Court of Mississippi


578 So. 2d 624; 1991 Miss. LEXIS 186



April 3, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 9064320 from Judgment Dated June 29, 1990, Taylor M. Seldge Ruling Judge, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: On Direct Appeal Affirmed. On Cross-Appeal Dismissed as Moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, state attorney general and legislators, challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), which dismissed appellants' action against defendant secretary of state concerning an initiative to repeal a constitutional ban on state lotteries. Appellants sought a declaratory judgment that an initiative and referendum amendment to the state constitution was valid and enforceable.


OVERVIEW: Defendant secretary of state refused to place on the ballot for a statewide general election an initiative to repeal the ban on state lotteries in Miss. Const. Art. 4, § 98. Plaintiffs, state attorney general and legislators, filed an action for a declaratory judgment that an initiative and referendum amendment to the state constitution was valid and enforceable. The trial court granted defendant's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the action with prejudice. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment against plaintiffs. The court held that collateral estoppel precluded relitigation of whether the initiative and referendum amendment was proposed and ratified in accordance with Miss. Const. art. 15, § 273 (amended 1959). The court found that the validity and enforceability of the amendment to § 273 was fully and finally adjudged in a prior case and that the prior decision did not perpetuate a specific adverse or harmful effect. The court concluded that plaintiffs were successors in office or had sufficient identity with the parties in the prior case for collateral estoppel to bar the action. The court determined that the amended § 273 had no retroactive effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of defendant secretary of state. Collateral estoppel precluded relitigation by plaintiffs, state attorney general and legislators, of whether the initiative and referendum amendment to the state constitution was properly proposed and ratified. The validity and enforceability of the amendment was fully and finally adjudged in a prior case.

 

146 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. State


No. 89-CA-0302


Supreme Court of Mississippi


574 So. 2d 1338; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 842



December 27, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. C578 from Judgment dated December 2, 1988, Fred L Banks, Jr Ruling Judge, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded for a Hearing on the Appropriate Amount of Expenses.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorneys sought review of a judgment from the Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which denied the attorneys' motion for compensation of $ 60.00 an hour for representing an indigent.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys filed a motion with the trial court for compensation of $ 60.00 an hour for representing an indigent. The trial court denied the motion because compensation for attorneys who represented indigents was governed by Miss. Code Ann. § 99-15-17, which allowed a maximum of $ 1,000 per attorney. The attorneys challenged the constitutionality of § 99-15-17. The court upheld the constitutionality of the statute, reversed the judgment of the trial court, and remanded the case for the trial court to redetermine the attorneys' compensation. The court held that: (1) although § 99-15-17 limited the compensation that an attorney could receive for representing an indigent, it allowed for reimbursement of actual expenses; (2) if a statute could be interpreted as constitutional or unconstitutional, the court adopts the constitutional construction; and (3) the court was able to save the statute from unconstitutionality by interpreting the language to include reimbursement for all actual costs to the lawyer for the purpose of keeping his door open to handle the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which denied the attorneys' motion for compensation of $ 60.00 an hour for representing an indigent, and remanded the case to the trial court to determine the attorneys' compensation.

Mackbee v. State


No. 03-DP-89


Supreme Court of Mississippi


575 So. 2d 16; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 831



December 27, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 10635 from Judgment Dated December 10, 1986, Joe N Pigott Ruling Judge, Lincoln County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, Reversed and Remanded in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Covington County Circuit Court (Mississippi) for capital murder with an underlying felony of robbery, under Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-19(2)(e). Defendant was also indicted as an habitual offender under § 99-19-83 and challenged the death sentence imposed by the jury after his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted in separate instruments for the capital murder of two victims whose charred bodies were found in the trunk of a car. At the time of trial in the case, defendant had not yet been tried for the murder of the second victim. On appeal, he argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred when it overruled his motion in limine to exclude evidence and argument that pertained to the second murder. The trial court's ruling was based upon the fact that the events of the common scheme or plan were so intertwined that they could properly be submitted to the jury pursuant to Miss. R. Evid. 404(b). The court agreed and found that presentation of evidence regarding the second murder was substantially necessary to present "the complete story of the crime." With regard to sentencing, the court held that the trial court erred when it denied defendant's request to instruct the jury regarding the effect of the habitual offender indictment. According to the court, the jury should have been informed that defendant's prior convictions would enhance his punishment and that he was ineligible for parole pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for capital murder with an underlying felony of robbery. The court reversed the sentence imposed and remanded for a new sentencing hearing before a different jury.

149 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Knight v. State


No. 90-CA-0568


Supreme Court of Mississippi


574 So. 2d 662; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 848



December 21, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 140677 from Judgment dated April 27, 1990, Wilmer Oras Dillard Ruling Judge, Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered as to the Issue of the Constitutionality of Miss. Code Ann. Sec. 97-33-51 (Supp. 1990). Affirmed as to the Remaining Issues.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bingo operators challenged a decision of the Hinds County Chancery Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which granted summary judgment and permanent injunctive relief to appellee, Office of Attorney General (attorney general), in his suit seeking a declaration that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-33-51 (Supp. 1990) legalizing bingo was unconstitutional under Miss. Const. art. IV, § 98.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general sought a declaration that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-33-51 (Supp. 1990), which legalized bingo, was unconstitutional under Miss. Const. art. IV, § 98, which prohibited lotteries. The trial court granted summary judgment to the attorney general and permanently enjoined the bingo operators from further bingo activity. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that, under the plain language of Miss. Const. art. IV, § 98, bingo was not a lottery because it did not involve the selling of tickets. In so holding, the court refused to follow the precedents of many sister states, noting that it would not in clear conscience blindly concur in the conclusion that bingo was a lottery simply because other courts had so concluded. After declaring that Miss. Code Ann. § 97-33-51 (Supp. 1990) was constitutional, the court warned that strict guidelines and enforcement measures via legislation were needed to avert further personal profiteering and circumvention of the statute's purpose, which was to benefit nonprofit civic, educational, wildlife conservation, or religious organizations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the chancellor's decision as to the constitutionality of the statute and affirmed the chancellor's decision as to other issues, which the court declared moot or devoid of merit.

Berry v. State


No. 89-DP-199


Supreme Court of Mississippi


575 So. 2d 1; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 849



December 19, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Mississippi v. Berry, 500 U.S. 928, 111 S. Ct. 2042, 114 L. Ed. 2d 126, 1991 U.S. LEXIS 2673 (1991)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Berry v. State, 703 So. 2d 269, 1997 Miss. LEXIS 639 (Miss., 1997)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Petition dismissed by Berry v. Epps, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 72879 (N.D. Miss., Oct. 4, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 9122 from Judgment Dated November 1, 1988, R. Kenneth Coleman Ruling Judge, Chickasaw County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to Guilt. Reversed and Remanded for a Sentencing Trial Conducted in Accordance with This Opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Chickasaw County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder and sentenced him to death in accordance with the jury's verdict. Although the trial court held that defendant was a habitual offender who would be ineligible for parole, the jury was not informed that defendant would never get parole prior to entering into deliberations regarding defendant's death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for capital murder. The court ruled that defendant's confession was admissible even though there was a dispute as to whether he requested counsel prior to giving the confession. The court further held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for change of venue as a result of pretrial publicity. Defendant's claim of error relating to his challenge for cause as to specific jurors was rejected because he failed to exhaust all of his peremptory challenges. In addition, the court ruled that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing several photographs of the victim into evidence. Finally, with regard to defendant's guilt, the court ruled that the trial court properly refused to give a lesser included charge on manslaughter because the evidence was clear that defendant acted with malice in beating the victim to death. As to defendant's sentencing, however, the court held that because the trial court determined that defendant was a habitual offender, the jury should have been told that defendant was ineligible for parole before deliberating on defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court with regard to defendant's conviction of capital murder. The court, however, remanded the case for a new sentencing trial because the jury should have been apprised that defendant was ineligible for parole.
