In Interest of C.B.


No. 07-CA-59340


Supreme Court of Mississippi


574 So. 2d 1369; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 835



December 19, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 22637-91 from Judgment dated January 05, 1988, C A Henley Ruling Judge, Hinds County Youth Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father sought review of an order from the Hinds County Youth Court, First Judicial District, (Mississippi), which awarded permanent custody of his daughter to petitioner mother and denied the father visitation rights. The judgment was based on a finding that the father had sexually abused the child in his home during visitation. The sole evidence was hearsay testimony of statements allegedly made by the child.


OVERVIEW: After their divorce, the mother complained to the department that the father had sexually abused their daughter during visitation. The mother filed a petition to determine that the child was sexually abused, to confirm her permanent custody of the child, and to deny the father visitation. Based solely on hearsay testimony of statements made by the child to others, the trial court granted the petition and ordered continued treatment for the child. The child did not testify. The father filed a motion to set aside the judgment, which was denied, and the father sought review. The court held that: (1) before it admitted the hearsay evidence, the trial court was required to determine whether the testimony fell within any of the hearsay exceptions enumerated in Miss R. Evid. 803, and the failure to make this determination required reversal and remand; (2) under Miss. Code Ann. § 43-21-559(1), the trial court was to admit evidence that would be admissible in a civil proceeding; (3) the right of confrontation should have been accorded to the father; and (4) the child was available and could have been called to testify.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that confirmed permanent custody of the child in the mother, ordered continued treatment of the child, and denied the father visitation, and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

152 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. State


No. 89-KA-0301


Supreme Court of Mississippi


574 So. 2d 1324; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 845



December 19, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. C578 from Judgment dated October 03, 1988, Fred L Banks, Jr Ruling Judge, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to life imprisonment without the benefit of probation or parole.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to life imprisonment. The defendant claimed that he was denied the right to counsel at a post lineup confrontation between an identifying witness and the police, the lineup was so suggestive as to violate due process, identification evidence should have been suppressed because the state failed to preserve the photographic lineup, and he was impermissibly interrogated after invoking the right to counsel. The court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that: (1) the defendant did not have a right to counsel during a post lineup confrontation between a witness and the police; (2) the fact that the witness could not identify the defendant from a pictorial lineup prior to the live lineup did not disqualify his testimony; (3) the identification procedure was not impermissibly suggestive where the defendant was not singled out; (4) where there was no bad faith on the part of the police in failing to preserve the photographic lineup, the defendant was not denied due process; and (5) the explanation by the police of lineup procedures after the defendant invoked the right to counsel was not an impermissible interrogation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of the defendant of capital murder and affirmed its sentence of a mandatory term of life imprisonment.

 

153 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Owens-Illinois, Inc. v. Edwards


No. 90-IA-0370


Supreme Court of Mississippi


573 So. 2d 704; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 837; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,708



December 12, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 885422 from Judgment Dated March 27, 1990, Darwin M. Maples Ruling Judge, Jackson County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, corporations and asbestos compensation fund, sought review by interlocutory appeal of an order by the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which granted partial summary to plaintiff personal injury claimant on his allegation that a discovery rule existed in Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-49 (1972) that was applicable in a products liability and negligence action involving latent diseases.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff personal injury claimant filed suit against defendants, corporation and asbestos compensation fund, for personal injuries allegedly sustained by plaintiff by exposure to asbestos. Defendants argued that the action was barred by the six-year statute of limitations found in Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-49 (1972). Plaintiff subsequently filed a motion for summary judgment on the issue of whether his action was barred by Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-49 (1972). Plaintiff sought an adjudication that at the time of the filing of his complaint a discovery rule existed, so that his cause of action did not accrue until he was diagnosed with asbestos-related disease. The trial court granted the motion, and the court affirmed, holding that under Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-49 (1972), the cause of action accrued and the statute of limitations began to run when plaintiff could have been held to have had knowledge of the injury or disease. A cause of action accrued only when the right to sue became vested. Thus, because plaintiff filed suit one month after the discovery of asbestos-related disease, he was well within the six-year statute of limitations found in Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-49 (1972).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of partial summary judgment to plaintiff personal injury claimant, and against defendants, corporations and asbestos compensation fund, on plaintiff's claim that a discovery rule existed in the six-year statute of limitations that was applicable in a products liability and negligence action involving latent diseases. The cause of action accrued when plaintiff reasonably could have discovered the disease or injury.

 

154 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Barnes v. State


No. 89-KA-0552


Supreme Court of Mississippi


577 So. 2d 840; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 822



December 12, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified March 6, 1991. Rehearing Granted March 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. C387 from Judgment Dated March 24, 1989, William F. Coleman Ruling Judge, Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR REHEARING GRANTED; REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR A NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance with intent to distribute.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that he was denied his right to a speedy trial and his right to effective assistance of counsel. The court held that Miss. Code Ann. § 99-17-1 (Supp. 1990) was violated. It provided that unless good cause was shown and a continuance duly granted, all offenses for which indictments were presented to the trial court had to be tried no later than 270 days after the accused had been arraigned. The total number of days that transpired from arraignment to trial, not including the time of continuances, was 418 days. The court concluded that the prosecution missed the statutory deadline for a speedy trial by 148 days. It also found that defendant established all of the elements of a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. Defense counsel's performance was so sub-standard that he was not functioning as counsel as guaranteed by the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments and by Miss. Const. Art. 3, § 26 (1890). There was a reasonable probability that but for defense counsel's errors and deficient performance, the outcome of the proceedings against defendant could well have been different.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case for a new trial. On remand, the trial court was directed to consider whether there was good cause for the delay. If the State was unable to show good cause for enough of the delay to bring the case under the 270-day limitation, the indictment against defendant had to be dismissed, and he had to be finally discharged.

Supreme Court of Mississippi


1990 Miss. LEXIS 774

OVERVIEW: After being diagnosed with pulmonary pleural asbestosis because of exposure to asbestos, the worker filed an action under the theories of negligence and strict liability tort against the corporations. The worker filed a motion for partial summary judgment on the issue of whether his action was barred by Miss. Code Ann. § 15-1-49 (1972). On interlocutory appeal, the court held that a discovery rule existed in conjunction with § 15-1-49 in the case of a negligence or products liability cause of action involving latent disease. The court held that the cause of action accrued and the limitations period began to run when the worker could have reasonably have been held to have had knowledge of the injury of the disease, the date of the diagnosis. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, as modified, the order from the trial court.

Turner v. State


No. 03-DP-0082


Supreme Court of Mississippi


573 So. 2d 657; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 792



December 12, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 13051 from Judgment Dated May 29, 1987, Joe N. Pigott Ruling Judge, Pike County Circuit Court.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of November 22, 1989, Reported at 1989 Miss. LEXIS 483.



DISPOSITION: REQUEST FOR RECUSAL DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Pike County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted him of capital murder and imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder, and the trial court imposed the death penalty. The court held that defendant was not discriminated against because the foreman of the grand jury was not black. Pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 13-5-26 (Supp. 1981), the foreman was appointed by the trial judge after the jurors were selected in a random procedure. The court held that the state had the burden of proving any aggravating circumstances. The court held that the trial court's limiting instruction on the aggravating circumstances was not constitutionally sufficient. Pursuant to the Mississippi habitual-offender statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-83 (1990 Supp.), defendant's sentence should not have been reduced or suspended nor should he have been eligible for parole or probation. The court held that the jury was required to know by instruction whether defendant was eligible for parole. The court affirmed a conviction of the trial court but vacated and remanded for re-sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of capital murder, but the trial court vacated and remanded for re-sentencing the imposed death sentence. The court held that the state had the burden of proving aggravating circumstances and that the trial court's limiting instruction on such circumstances was not constitutionally sufficient. The jury was required to know whether defendant was eligible for parole.

White v. State


No. 07-KA-59188


Supreme Court of Mississippi


571 So. 2d 956; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 758



December 5, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 13538 from Judgment Dated December 06, 1985, Joe N. Pigott Ruling Judge, Copiah County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Copiah County Circuit Court (Mississippi) that, following the jury trial, convicted him of burglary and grand larceny and adjudicated him an habitual criminal.


OVERVIEW: After defendant allegedly burglarized a home, police obtained items taken in the burglary while searching the residence of defendant's girlfriend. Defendant was convicted of burglary and grand larceny and also was adjudicated an habitual criminal. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, finding that defendant did not have a legitimate expectation of privacy in his girlfriend's apartment. Even though the search may have violated the girlfriend's Fourth Amendment rights, defendant failed to satisfy his burden of proving that his own constitutional rights were violated by the search. The court also held that the mere legitimate presence in the girlfriend's apartment was insufficient to create the protectable expectation of privacy. Canning v. State, 226 So. 2d 747 (Miss. 1969) and Fuller v. State 230 So. 2d 213 (Miss. 1970) were overruled to the extent they were inconsistent with the decision. The court concluded that defendant's motion to suppress the evidence obtained in the residence properly was denied and rejected defendant's other contentions. Finally, the court held that defendant properly was adjudicated an habitual offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Ryals v. Pigott


No. 07-CA-59531


Supreme Court of Mississippi


580 So. 2d 1140; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 694



November 28, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearings Denied June 12, 1991, Reported at 1991 Miss. LEXIS 362.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 33196 from Judgment Dated March 23, 1988, R B Reeves Ruling Judge, Pike County Chancery Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, Reversed in Part, and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents file suit against defendants, owners and sheriff, seeking to prevent the owners from closing a portion of the Bogue Chitto River to the public. The Pike County Chancery Court (Mississippi) found that, under Miss Code Ann. § 1-331 or § 51-1-3, a portion of river was not a navigable waterway and, under Miss. Const. art. 3 §§ 14, 17, public could not acquire rights in river without payment of compensation to property owners.


OVERVIEW: The landowners were riparian owners and contended that they had rights in the Bogue Chitto River and that the portion of the river that they had rights in was not navigable. The trial court held that the landowners had riparian rights in the river because it was navigable in the section that was the subject of the parties' dispute. The court held that pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 51-9-103, the river was navigable and public water for recreational use because the river was the principal tributary of another navigable river, the average depth was greater than three feet, and the average water flow exceeded 100 cubic feet per second. The court also held that Miss Code Ann. §§ 1-3-31 and 51-1-1, which established the 200 bales of cotton steamboat test of navigability did not apply because the river was declared public by 3 U.S. Stat. §§ 348, 349 before the statute was enacted, and the state did not have the power to make the public waterway private.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, in part, the judgment and concluded that the residents were entitled to a declaratory judgment finding that the Bogue Chitto River was a navigable public river.

Bryant v. State


No. 07-KA-59141


Supreme Court of Mississippi


567 So. 2d 234; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 558



September 19, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 8510461; Robert T. Mills Judge, Jackson County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Jackson County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which entered a judgment of conviction for the crime of child desertion, in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-5-3. Defendant was sentenced to two years in prison and was ordered to make restitution to the child.


OVERVIEW: The child had serious ailments since birth. Defendant stopped paying support when his wife remarried, and the wife was unable to work because of the needs of the child. Defendant alleged that he did not know where the child lived and that the wife refused to accept support. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction where defendant was financially able to pay while the child was destitute, there was no credible evidence that defendant attempted to pay support, and the former wife had attempted to collect support. There was no undue prejudice for the jury to see the child in the hallway at the conclusion of the trial because the State made no effort to make a prominent display of the child. Section 97-5-3 was not unconstitutional because it was not imprisonment for debt and the State had a legitimate interest in prosecution a financially able parent who willfully deserted or failed to support his child when the child was in destitute circumstances. Finally, there was no error in the allowance of testimony of a physician regarding the child's condition because it was relevant to demonstrate the extreme needs of the child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Mississippi State Tax Com. v. One (1) 1984 Black Mercury Grand Marquis


No. 07-CA-59208


Supreme Court of Mississippi


568 So. 2d 707; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 564



September 19, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 5774; Edward A. Williamson Judge, Newton County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered on Issues I and II; Reversed and Remanded on Issue III.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Mississippi State Tax Commission filed an action for forfeiture of respondent's vehicle, which had been seized while transporting intoxicating liquor in a dry county. The Newton County Circuit Court (Mississippi) denied the commission's motion for summary judgment and granted respondent's motion to dismiss, finding the seizure provisions of Miss. Code Ann. § 67-1-17 (1972) resulted in an unreasonable seizure. The commission appealed.


OVERVIEW: A large quantity of intoxicating liquor was found in the trunk of respondent's vehicle, which was being driven in a dry county. The court narrowed its decision to the question of the reasonableness of the state's seizure of the automobile under the Fourth Amendment. The court noted that if the seizure had been based on the use of the vehicle to possess with the intention to resell or deliver for resale and the facts had substantiated that claim, the seizure would have been reasonable and constitutionally sustained. The court was of the opinion that the constitutionality of the statute was not properly before the lower court and that the court erred in declaring the statute unconstitutional of its own volition. The importance and significance of the decision were enormous. Were the seizure ruled unreasonable, alcoholic beverages could be purchased wherever they were legal and carried into dry areas for consumption, even where a majority of the people had voted to maintain such areas dry. The court would not thwart the will and rights of the people by destroying their freedom of choice. It was also error to return the vehicle to respondent pending a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders dismissing the commission's forfeiture petition and ordering the vehicle returned to the respondent. Decision was rendered in favor of the commission.

Powell v. State


No. 07-KA-58305


Supreme Court of Mississippi


566 So. 2d 1228; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 461



August 15, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 25, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 19672 from Judgment dated January 22, 1987, Arthur B. Clark Ruling Judge, Washington County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Washington County Circuit Court (Mississippi) for the rape of a female child under the age of fourteen years. On appeal, defendant asserted that the identification testimony by the victim should not have been admitted and that the jury's verdict was against the overwhelming weight of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: A ten-year old female child reported that defendant tricked her into coming to his house and then he dragged her into the house and raped her. After the rape, she immediately ran to a nearby relative's house and reported the rape. She then identified defendant from a photo array that a police officer had put together. During the preliminary hearing, the prosecutor led the victim to a holding room, where she identified defendant. That identification was ruled inadmissible, but the victim was permitted to make an in-court identification at the trial. Defendant presented an alibi defense and claimed that the photo array and the identification at the preliminary hearing were impermissibly suggestive and made the in-court identification improper, but he was convicted. The court, holding that reliability was the linchpin in determining the admissibility of identification testimony, found that the victim had a detailed and prolonged view of defendant in daylight when he raped her, and the totality of the circumstances made her in-court identification admissible. The court also ruled that there was clearly sufficient credible evidence for the jury to find defendant guilty of rape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for rape.

Andrew Jackson Life Ins. Co. v. Williams


No. 07-CA-58758


Supreme Court of Mississippi


566 So. 2d 1172; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 435



July 25, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected August 21, 1990. As Corrected August 27, 1990.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer appealed a judgment entered in the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi) which, after a jury trial, determined that defendant was liable to plaintiff for allegedly unauthorized misrepresentations by agents of defendant in an action where plaintiff sought punitive and compensatory damages when defendant refused to honor plaintiff's insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: Defendant insurer offered life insurance policies through agents at plaintiff's place of employment. Defendant refused to insure plaintiff after plaintiff made a claim on the policy. Defendant alleged that plaintiff was refused insurance because plaintiff had health conditions and alleged that the agents made unauthorized misrepresentations. Plaintiff sought compensatory and punitive damages under the policy. The court reviewed the conditions under which the policy was made. The jury could have found that the formation of the insurance contract was sufficient to hold defendant liable. The actions of defendant's agents bound defendant. The court held that, based on defendant's actions, the issue of punitive damages was properly submitted to the jury. The court affirmed the jury verdict and awarded plaintiff compensatory and punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered by the circuit court that awarded punitive and compensatory damages to plaintiff because a reasonable juror could have properly found that the formation of the insurance contract was sufficient, that the agents bound defendant, and the issue of punitive damages was properly submitted and accepted by the jury.

In Interest of T.L.C.

DISPOSITION:  [**1] AFFIRMED; MOTION OF NICK CRAWFORD, GUARDIAN AD LITEM, AND VERNITA JOHNSON, YOUTH COURT PROSECUTOR, TO DISMISS APPEAL DENIED; MOTION OF WASHINGTON COUNTY DEPARTMENT OF HUMAN SERVICES TO BE DISMISSED AS PARTY TO APPEAL DENIED; MOTION FOR ATTORNEY FEES DENIED; MOTION OF ROY CORTESI FOR REFUND OF FEES CHARGED BY COURT REPORTER GRANTED.

164 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Goodson v. State


No. 07-KA-58650


Supreme Court of Mississippi


566 So. 2d 1142; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 413



July 11, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended October 3, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal No. 3250 from Judgment dated April 17, 1987, Frank A. Russell Ruling Judge. Tishomingo County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded to Circuit Court for a New Trial on All Issues.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought reversal of his rape conviction, imposed on him by the Tishomingo County Circuit Court (Mississippi), on the grounds that the evidence was insufficient, inadmissible prejudicial evidence was used at his trial, and he was improperly denied the opportunity that the complainant's physical injuries had another source.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his forcible rape conviction. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial. In so doing, it first rejected defendant's contentions that the evidence against him was legally insufficient. However, it granted relief on the grounds that prejudicial error occurred when a physician was permitted to testify that the complainant had suffered sexual trauma. That testimony was inadmissible both because the physician was not qualified as an expert on the subject and because the point itself went to the ultimate issue. In addition, the physician should not have been permitted to testify that the complainant seemed truthful in her claims that she had been raped, and defendant should have been permitted to introduce evidence of the complainant's sexual activity after the alleged rape in order to demonstrate that her hymeneal ring had been lost via that sexual activity rather than via rape.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and a new trial was ordered.

 

165 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


No. 07-KA-59491


Supreme Court of Mississippi


564 So. 2d 848; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 292



June 27, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 12148 from Judgment Dated April 22, 1988, Thomas J. Gardner, III Ruling Judge, Monroe County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: Conviction Affirmed; Reversed and Remanded for Proper Sentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a conviction of the Monroe County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which found him guilty of selling four ounces of marijuana and sentenced him to 20 years' imprisonment with 5 years suspended. Defendant also was ordered to pay a fine of $ 50,000 and court costs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the jury verdict was against the overwhelming weight of the evidence. However, the court determined that it was the duty of the jury to resolve conflicts and discrepancies in the testimony. The court found that the circuit court had not erred in imposing the prison term for defendant's conviction. Nonetheless, the court held that the $ 50,000 fine was in excess of the $ 30,000 fine authorized by Miss. Code Ann. § 41-29-139(b)(2) (Mississippi). The court determined that pursuant to Ch. 501, Laws 1979, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-20 (Mississippi), it was permissible for the circuit court to order that defendant pay the fine prior to being released from prison. However, in no event was the period of imprisonment to exceed one day for each $ 10.00 of the fine. In addition, the court held that the circuit court was required to inquire as to whether defendant was in fact able to pay the fine.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, but the case was reversed and remanded for proper sentencing.

 

166 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Underwood v. Foremost Financial Services Corp.


No. 89-CA-0053


Supreme Court of Mississippi


563 So. 2d 1387; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 286



June 20, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 2, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 6215 from Judgment dated May 31, 1988, Robert T. Mills Ruling Judge, George County Circuit Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, Reversed and Remanded in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtors sought review of the decision of the George County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which entered judgment against the debtors in their action against appellee creditor for the allegedly unconstitutional ex parte seizure of their home.


OVERVIEW: The debtors became delinquent in making monthly payments on a contract. The delinquency led the creditor to seize the debtors' home without serving the debtors with notice. The debtors sued the creditor for compensatory and punitive damages, arguing that the seizure of their home was violative of the due process rights afforded under the Fourteenth Amendment. The circuit court entered judgment against the debtors, and they appealed. The court held that the circuit judge's decision concerning liability disregarded applicable and established constitutional law. The court stated that an evidentiary hearing should have been held, and the creditor's claim of good-faith reliance on a presumptively-valid statute should have been considered in light of not only the sincerity in its belief that it was acting properly, but the reasonableness of its actions under the circumstances. The court affirmed the circuit judge's decision that the seizure transpired in an constitutionally-impermissible manner, but reversed the decision that the creditor could not have been subjected to liability for an injurious seizure and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the circuit court's decision that the seizure transpired in an constitutionally-impermissible manner. The court reversed the part of the decision that the creditor could not have been subjected to liability and remanded for the judge to decide whether the creditor's unconstitutional seizure was an act for which the creditor should have been subjected to liability and the extent of that liability.

 

167 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. State


No. 07-KA-58975


Supreme Court of Mississippi


561 So. 2d 1037; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 258



May 16, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 10562 from Judgment dated DECEMBER 02, 1987, CLINTON E LOCKARD RULING JUDGE, Jackson County Circuit Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a sentence of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Mississippi), which was imposed after defendant's original sentence was set aside. Defendant had pleaded guilty to armed robbery with a deadly weapon in violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-79 (1972).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to a seven-year term of imprisonment after he pleaded guilty to armed robbery with a deadly weapon. The sentence was to run consecutively with the life sentence that defendant was serving in Canada, which life sentence was later commuted. The circuit court set aside the sentence on the ground that it was an unconstitutional application of an ex post facto law insofar as it was mandatory. Defendant declined to withdraw his plea, the circuit court sentenced him to a 20-year term. On appeal, the court held that the original sentence was lawful because there was nothing in the sentencing order that dictated that the sentence was without parole. Moreover, the original sentence was within the range provided in § 97-3-79. Accordingly, the court further held that the circuit court lacked authority to resentence defendant. Furthermore, the original sentence in conjunction with the controlling parole statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 47-7-3(1)(d) (1972), as amended, was not an illegal application of an ex post facto law. Defendant was not "sentenced" under § 47-7-3, and his parole rights were not restricted by § 47-7-3.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's resentencing of defendant and reinstated the original sentence with the possibility of parole.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to four years in prison; the sentence was suspended and he was placed on four years' probation. A hearing was held during which defendant told the trial court that he did not want to return to the program, where he felt uncomfortable, nor did he want to be put in prison. At a second hearing, the trial court offered to permit defendant to complete a program in jail and return to the rehabilitation program. At a fourth hearing defendant was represented by counsel; his appeal from revocation was denied by the trial court. Defendant appealed. The court held that defendant's due process rights had not been violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

169 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Chevron U.S.A., Inc. v. State


No. 07-CA-58036


Supreme Court of Mississippi


1990 Miss. LEXIS 195



April 4, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Withdrawn April 4, 1991; Substituted Opinion Reported at 1991 Miss. LEXIS 223.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal No. 36210 from Judgment dated APRIL 11, 1986, J. SHANNON CLARK RULING JUDGE, Jones County Chancery Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessee challenged a decision from the Chancery Court of the Second Judicial District of Jones County (Mississippi), which cancelled and set aside its oil and gas lease with defendants, state and lessor, as to all non-producing areas in the lessee's action to confirm and quiet its lease interests. The state and the lessor challenged the trial court's decision to allow the lessee to continue operations at the producing reservoir.


OVERVIEW: In 1957 the lessor executed an oil and gas lease that was later assigned to the lessee. The lease had a primary term of six years and so long thereafter as oil and gas were produced. Miss. Const. § 211 (1944), however, prohibited leases longer than 25 years. The lessee filed an action to confirm and quiet the lease interest. The state and the lessor filed a counterclaim and argued that the lease expired in 1982 pursuant to § 211. The trial court held that the lease remained in full force and effect as to the lessee's producing reservoir but cancelled the lease as to all non-producing areas. The lessee appealed the cancellation of the lease as to the non-producing areas, and the state and the lessor appealed the lease extension. The court affirmed. The court held that the lessee had the lawful right pursuant to § 211 and Miss. Code Ann. § 6600 (1942) to continue its production under the lease from the proven reservoir if it continued to comply with the lease terms. The court held that 25 years was the maximum period that Miss. Const. § 211 (1944) authorized the lessee to possess the surface; thus, the lessee was not permitted to continue exploration in non-producing areas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling in favor of the state and the lessor in the lessee's action to confirm and quiet interests in its oil and gas lease and affirmed on the cross-appeal. The court reversed and remanded for the limited purpose of permitting the chancellor to properly frame a decree permitting the lessee's use of the surface so long as oil and gas were commercially produced from the area that was currently in production.

In re Adoption of Minor


No. 07-CA-58992


Supreme Court of Mississippi


558 So. 2d 854; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 156



March 14, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 1128 form Judgment dated AUGUST 11, 1987, J SHANNON CLARK RULING JUDGE, Jones County Chancery Court, Second Judicial District.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, paternal grandparents, filed a petition to set aside a decree of adoption of their grandchild and for visitation rights with their grandchild. The Chancery Court, Jones County (Mississippi) granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, maternal grandparents who adopted the grandchild. The paternal grandparents appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the paternal grandparents' son who was the father of the grandchild was killed, the maternal grandparents received consent of their daughter to adopt their grandchild. The daughter was 16 and the mother of the grandchild. The consent was given on the same date the petition for adoption was filed. The paternal grandparents were not made parties to the adoption petition or proceeding. They filed a petition to set aside the adoption and grant them visitation rights because they had not been named parties. The paternal grandparents sought to assert a right of visitation under 1983 Miss. Laws 497, Miss. Code Ann. §93-16-3. That Act however provided for visitation rights when there had been a termination of parental rights under the 1968 Act, not the general adoption statutes. The paternal grandparents were excluded because neither of the "legal" adoptive parents was a natural parent of the child. Therefore, there was no statutory right of visitation in the paternal grandparents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

171 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Sheffield v. Pass Christian


No. 07-58785


Supreme Court of Mississippi


556 So. 2d 1052; 1990 Miss. LEXIS 35



February 7, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal No. 18920 from Judgment dated JULY 31, 1987, KOSTA N. VLAHOS RULING JUDGE, Harrison County Circuit Court, First Judicial District.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Harrison County, First Judicial District (Mississippi), which reversed a municipal court's judgment that evidence of defendant's prior convictions was inadmissible in his trial for driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor (DUI) under Miss. Code Ann. § 63-11-30 (Supp. 1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with DUI. The City sought a pretrial ruling in a municipal court concerning the admissibility of defendant's three prior DUI convictions and one conviction for driving while his license was suspended. The municipal court ruled that the exhibits were inadmissible because the City could not show that defendant had been represented by counsel or had knowingly and intelligently waived his right to counsel for the prior convictions. On appeal, the circuit court reversed. On further review, the court affirmed the circuit court's judgment. The court held that the prior convictions of defendant when he was without counsel were constitutionally valid in and of themselves and valid for the purpose of enhancing punishment under § 63-11-30. The prior convictions could also be considered for any lesser administrative sanctions, such as suspension of one's driver's license. The court also found that defendant's convictions that had no reference to counsel had a presumption of regularity. Defendant could present evidence to rebut such presumption, shifting the burden to the City to prove that defendant's rights were protected during the course of the convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Supreme Court of Mississippi

January 10, 1990, Decided

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district and employment commission sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of the First Judicial District of Hinds County (Mississippi), which reversed a finding by the employment commission that appellee teacher had been discharged for cause when she refused to stop wearing her headdress which she considered to be a religious and cultural symbol.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's reversal of the employment commission's decision that the discharge was for cause.

Turner v. State

OVERVIEW: Defendant complained that the trial court erred when it convicted him of capital murder and sentenced him to death. In support of that complaint he submitted 22 assertions of error. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court that convicted defendant of capital murder and set a date for the execution of the sentence by the infliction of the death penalty in the manner provided by law.

Fleming v. State


No. 07-KP-59246


Supreme Court of Mississippi


553 So. 2d 505; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 476



November 15, 1989, Decided



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Hinds County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted defendant, based on his guilty plea, of possession of a controlled substance and also as a habitual offender under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 (1972), and which denied defendant's motion for transcripts of sentencing and other court records.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to the denial of his motion seeking transcripts related to his sentencing, defendant challenged the judgment. However, the court dismissed the appeal. The court held that defendant was not permitted to raise his claim on direct appeal, under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-35-101 (1972), concerning the denial of trial transcripts because he pled guilty and failed to directly appeal the conviction. Additionally, the court held that a challenge via the Uniform Post-Conviction Collateral Relief Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-39-1 et seq. (Supp. 1989) was not open to defendant because the Act did not give defendant a right to institute an independent, original action for a free transcript or other documents, and then if dissatisfied with the trial court's ruling, to directly appeal that ruling to this court as a separate and independent action. Thus, the court held that the appeal should be dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. Addressing the merits of the appeal in dicta, the court also noted that the trial court correctly denied the motion for transcripts. The court held that, by pleading guilty and bypassing the opportunity for direct appeal, he forfeited his right to a free transcript.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal on jurisdiction grounds.

Hill v. Thompson


No. 07-58509


Supreme Court of Mississippi


564 So. 2d 1; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 458



October 11, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended November 17, 1989. As Corrected August 8, 1990. Rehearing Denied August 8, 1990, Reported at 1990 Miss. LEXIS 531. As Corrected August 27, 1990.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessee filed an action against defendant school board and its officials (board), for confirmation of his leasehold interest in a property owned by the state. The Chancery Court of Scott County (Mississippi) confirmed title. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The lessee purchased a leasehold interest in property which was covered by a 99-year lease, the consideration for which had been a single payment of $ 7.50. The lessee filed suit to confirm the validity of the lease. The board counterclaimed for cancellation of the lease, and contended that the lease was invalid because the consideration was so inadequate as to make the lease a donation of property, in violation of Miss. Const. art 4, § 95. The trial court found in favor of the lessee and assessed a $ 7,500 sanction against the board for filing a frivolous defense. The court determined that when Mississippi became a state, a section of each township was reserved in the name of the state for the support of schools, and the management of the school lands was delegated to the local school board. The court determined that the lands were held in trust for the benefit of local schools, and that no trustee had the right to lease trust lands for less than fair market value. The court held that the consideration was so grossly inadequate as to shock the conscious. The court remanded the case to the trial court to determine the true value of the land.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, rendered a judgment that the lease was invalid, rendered a judgment that the board was not required to pay sanctions, and remanded for a determination of the fair market value of the leasehold.

Mississippi Judicial Performance Com. v. Thomas


No. 89-CC-684


SUPREME COURT OF MISSISSIPPI


549 So. 2d 962; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 451



October 4, 1989, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Mississippi Judicial Performance Commission, filed a recommendation that defendant, a mayor of certain village who also held the position of a municipal court judge, be suspended from holding office as municipal court judge so long as was mayor. The Commission further recommended that the court declare unconstitutional Miss. Code Ann. § 21-23-5, which permitted mayors to serve as municipal judges.


OVERVIEW: The mayor pled guilty in a federal court to operating an illegal gambling business in violation of 18 U.S.C.S. § 1955. In a separate action, he was convicted of violating state laws pertaining to illegal sales of liquor. The Commission charged the mayor with judicial misconduct, in violation of Miss. Const. art. VI, § 177A (1890), as amended, and recommended a suspension from the bench. The mayor denied that he was a judge, that the Commission had jurisdiction over him pursuant to Miss. Const. art VI, § 177A (1890), and that he was guilty of judicial misconduct. In adopting in part the Commission's recommendation, the court ruled that the mayor was a municipal judge pro tempore, by virtue of Miss. Code Ann. § 21-23-5, and that the Code of Judicial Conduct required compliance with the Code by anyone, whether or not a lawyer, who was an officer of a judicial system performing judicial functions. A judge pro tempore was defined as a person who is appointed to act temporarily as a judge. Thus, the mayor was subject to sanction as a judge by the Commission. The mayor's misconduct, though not official, brought his judicial office into disrepute, and warranted his removal from the bench.


OUTCOME: The court adopted that part of the Commission's recommendation that recommended that the mayor be suspended from serving as a municipal court judge. The court did not pass on the constitutionality of the statute that permitted mayors to serve as municipal judges.

 

178 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Cole v. National Life Ins. Co.


No. 07-58504


Supreme Court of Mississippi


549 So. 2d 1301; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 428



September 13, 1989, Decided



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state treasurer challenged the judgment from the Chancery Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which held that certain funds held by appellee insurance companies were not subject to the reporting and payment provisions of Mississippi's Uniform Disposition of Unclaimed Property Act (Act), Miss. Code Ann. § 89-12-1, et seq. (1972).


OVERVIEW: The insurance companies were holding funds for which the claims of the owners and the payees had become time-barred. The insurance companies sought an adjudication that the funds were not subject to the reporting and payment provisions of the Act. The trial court entered judgment for the insurance companies and permanently enjoined the state treasurer from enforcing the Act with regard to these particular funds. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. Section 16 of the Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 89-12-35 (1972) was to be given a prospective application because retroactive application to lift the bar of the limitations period would have destroyed the insurance companies' vested rights and would have been a violation of Miss. Const. art. IV, § 97, precluding the revival of time-barred remedies. The state treasurer's right to the abandoned funds was derivative from the rights of the owners and payees of said funds. Thus, the insurance companies' reliance on vested rights arising from the running of the limitations period against those owners and payees did not constitute a prohibited direct assertion of the statute of limitations against the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment holding that the funds held by the insurance companies were not subject to the Act and enjoining the state treasurer from enforcing the Act with regard to these particular funds.

Jones v. Meridian


No. 07-KA-58534


Supreme Court of Mississippi


552 So. 2d 820; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 422



August 30, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 4, 1989.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of a decision of the Lauderdale Circuit Court (Mississippi), which affirmed a judgment of a county court that convicted the attorney for breach of the peace and fined him $ 250.00. The attorney challenged the constitutionality of the breach of peace statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-35-13 (1972).


OVERVIEW: The attorney was arrested by a police officer for breach of the peace in a public place after the police officer had attempted to serve a warrant on the attorney's client in the lobby of the county's juvenile center. The attorney asserted that § 97-35-13 was unconstitutionally broad and vague because it regulated constitutionally-protected First Amendment rights, including the right to make an extemporaneous, on-the-scene protest to a policeman's demeanor, conduct, and authority. He also contended that the statute was not tied to an expressed interest of the state nor was its application limited to the extent necessary to serve such an interest. The court rejected the attorney's arguments and held that the statute was constitutional, both facially and as applied. The court specifically found that the statute was not so vague or overbroad that individuals, particularly attorneys, of common intelligence had to guess at its meaning. The attorney's disorderly conduct in a public place was conduct which the state had a compelling interest in proscribing. Also, there was no evidence that the appellate court's enhancement of the fine imposed was a result of judicial vindictiveness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court affirming the county court's judgment of conviction.

 

180 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Great South Fair v. Petal


No. 07-58602


Supreme Court of Mississippi


548 So. 2d 1289; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 395



August 16, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Chancery Court, Forrest County, William Robert Taylor, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant non-profit corporation sued appellee city, seeking a temporary retraining order and a declaration that a city ordinance, which restricted the operation of a carnival or fair to one day of operation, was unconstitutional. The Chancery Court, Forrest County (Mississippi), entered a temporary retraining order. It later entered judgment denying relief to the corporation and declaring the ordinance valid. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation owned 28 acres of land in the city. For many years, it operated an annual fair on the land, which was zoned for commercial use. The fair usually lasted seven to 10 days. The corporation argued that the ordinance effectively prohibited the operation of its fair because it was impractical for the fair to be set up and taken down after only one day. No other business was affected by the ordinance. The city asserted that it passed the ordinance after determining that fairs lasting more than a day were detrimental to the public welfare. It claimed that the fair caused increased traffic and other problems. On appeal, the court held that because the fair was a form of entertainment, it was protected under the First Amendment. The city failed to sustain its burden of showing that its interests in minimizing the effect of fairs could not be met in a less intrusive manner than effectively banning the fair. Moreover, the ordinance was not a lawful exercise of the city's police power because it was not rationally related to its stated interest in promoting public welfare. Though other businesses caused similar problems as the fair, the city had not seen fit to regulate them.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the chancery court's judgment and rendered a judgment that the ordinance was invalid.

 

181 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Leatherwood v. State


No. DP-70


Supreme Court of Mississippi


548 So. 2d 389; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 358



July 19, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Forrest County, Richard W. McKenzie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court, Forrest County (Mississippi), which convicted defendant of rape and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly admitted testimony as to statements that the child victim had made to a teacher and a child behavior expert.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the rape of the victim, an 11 year-old girl. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's conviction because the hearsay testimony regarding statements made by the victim was improperly admitted by the circuit court. The court held that the victim's statements to a child behavior expert were not generically medical and thus, were outside the hearsay exception for statements made for purposes of medical diagnosis or treatment. The court further held that the victim's statements to her teacher six weeks after the incident did not qualify for the excited utterance exception to the hearsay rule. There being no recognized exception to the hearsay rule for victims of a tender age, the circuit court erroneously allowed the victim's statement and failed to address the question of whether the statements made by the victim would qualify under the residual exceptions to hearsay. Thus, the court remanded the case for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's rape conviction and remanded the case for retrial.

Dantzler v. State


No. 59156


Supreme Court of Mississippi


542 So. 2d 906; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 197



April 5, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lamar County, R. I. Prichard, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Lamar County (Mississippi), which denied his motion to dismiss his conviction by the lower court for possession of beer while en route to his home. He was sentenced to 90 days in jail and fined pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 67-3-13 (1972).


OVERVIEW: Defendant purchased the beer in a "wet" city located in a "dry" county. The lower court convicted him for possession of beer. The circuit court denied his motion to dismiss. A motion for interlocutory appeal was granted. The court affirmed. Miss. Code Ann. § 67-3-13 (1972) was plain on its face. If the court accepted defendant's argument, alcoholic beverages could be purchased wherever they were legal and carried into "dry" areas for consumption even though the people had voted to maintain the area as "dry." The court held that this would thwart the will and the rights of the people. The court concluded that Miss. Code Ann. § 67-3-13 did not deny defendant equal protection. The court found no invasion of his constitutional right to privacy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

183 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. State


No. 57,746


Supreme Court of Mississippi


539 So. 2d 1366; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 141



February 27, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Jackson County, Darwin M. Maples, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Mississippi), which entered a conviction on one count of fondling a child and sentenced him to five years in prison.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred by allowing the state to adduce certain hearsay evidence over his objection. He urged that the testimony of the babysitter and the child's mother concerning what the child said about the incident was inadmissible hearsay. The State countered that the evidence fell under the tender years exception to the rule against hearsay in case law. The court ruled that Mississippi's rules of evidence abrogated evidentiary rules set out in caselaw and that the issue had to be decided under the rules of evidence. The testimony did not meet the requirements of Miss. R. Evid. 803(2) because the child did not report the incident while still under the stress of the startling event. The court ruled that the trial court had to determine whether the hearsay statements were admissible under the catchall provisions of Miss. R. Evid. 803(24). The testimony of the babysitter that the child had told her of other occasions defendant had exposed himself to children was improperly admitted. There was no indication that the child spontaneously reported those incidents.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and sentence and remanded the case.

 

184 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Richardson v. Rankin County School Dist.


No. 58337


Supreme Court of Mississippi


540 So. 2d 5; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 133



February 22, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Rankin County; Alfred G. Nicols, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the Circuit Court, Rankin County (Mississippi), which granted partial summary judgment in favor of defendants, a county school district, its superintendent, and all members of its board of trustees in their official capacities, excepting defendant school bus driver. The circuit court found that the movants were entitled to immunity except to the extent provided under Miss. Code Ann. § 37-41-37 et seq. (1986 Supp.).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was injured as a result of a collision involving her automobile and a school bus. She alleged negligence against the school district in failing to properly train the bus driver and insure that she operated the bus in a safe, careful, and lawful manner, as well as in allowing the driver to continue to operate a bus knowing of her prior involvement in traffic mishaps and near accidents. Plaintiff also alleged negligence against the bus driver. Although the court had attempted to abolish governmental immunity in a prior case, the court found that the Mississippi Legislature had, by appropriate legislation, the Immunity Act, Miss. Code Ann. § 11-46-1 et seq. (1988 Supp.), given the state and its political subdivisions immunity from suit on account of any wrongful or tortious act or omission by any employee of the state or its political subdivisions, except to the extent of liability permitted by Miss. Code Ann. § 37-41-37 et seq. (1988 Supp.)


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

185 of 825 DOCUMENTS


McDonald v. State


No. 58195


Supreme Court of Mississippi


538 So. 2d 778; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 90



February 9, 1989, Decided



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In accordance with the jury's verdict, the Second Judicial District of Harrison County (Mississippi) entered a judgment that convicted defendant of feloniously committing an aggravated assault with a deadly weapon and sentenced him to 20 years' imprisonment. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot an alleged victim in the leg. The indictment charged defendant with committing an aggravated assault with a deadly weapon, namely a gun, by knowingly shooting the victim with the intent to cause serious bodily harm. On appeal, defendant argued that he should have been permitted to adduce testimony as to previous specific acts of violence of the victim. In the absence of defendant's justifiable apprehension of his own safety by the victim's conduct, the court held that the victim's character or reputation for violence was irrelevant. Such testimony was not competent unless there was some evidence that the victim had been the aggressor in the affray. Moreover, Rule 405(b) of the Mississippi Rules of Evidence did not allow defendant to show the victim's previous difficulty with third persons unless defendant either saw it or knew of it. Next, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-7(2)(b) only required the State to prove that defendant attempted to cause bodily injury "with a deadly weapon." The indictment's reference to "serious bodily harm" was surplusage. Finally, the State gave a proper and racially neutral reason for excluding three of four blacks on the venire.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

186 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. State


No. 57,940


Supreme Court of Mississippi


539 So. 2d 1338; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 104



February 9, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Hinds County, L. Breland Hilburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR A NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for sexual battery of a child, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-95 (1985), by the Circuit Court, Hinds County (Mississippi).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual battery of a child, Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-95 (1985), after the trial court allowed testimony of two social workers about statements made by the child victim under the Evidence of Child Sexual Abuse Act (Act), Miss. Code Ann. § 13-1-401 et seq. (Supp. 1988). The Act allowed such testimony where the trial court found the victim would experience traumatic distress if forced to testify. The court held that the Act intruded on the province of the court by purporting to change the hearsay rules, which were its prerogative. The testimony was not admissible under any other hearsay exception and the conviction was reversed and remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The sexual battery of a child conviction was reversed and remanded for a new trial.

 

187 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Ashley v. State


No. 58141


Supreme Court of Mississippi


538 So. 2d 1181; 1989 Miss. LEXIS 24



January 25, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Pike County, Joe N. Pigott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF BURGLARY AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED AND CASE REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court, Pike County (Mississippi), which convicted him of burglary of a dwelling and adjudged him an habitual offender and sentenced him to the custody of the Department of Corrections for the remainder of his natural life without benefit of probation or parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary and sentenced as a recidivist to spend the rest of his life in prison. The court stated that a recidivism sentence of life imprisonment without parole was subject to scrutiny under the cruel and unusual punishment clause of the U.S. Const. Amend. VIII. The court vacated the sentence imposed upon defendant and remanded for an additional sentencing hearing and for resentencing consistent with the proportionality analysis, including: harshness of the penalty; the sentence imposed on other criminals in the same jurisdiction; and the sentence imposed for commission of the same crime in other jurisdictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of burglary, but vacated the life sentence and remanded for resentencing.

 

188 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Daniel v. State


No. 58,151


Supreme Court of Mississippi


536 So. 2d 1319; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 611



December 14, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Jackson County, Robert T. Mills, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment by the Circuit Court, Jackson County (Mississippi), which convicted him of sexual battery against a child under the age of 12 years and sentenced him to 30 years imprisonment. Defendant argued that the results of blood tests should not have been admitted, evidence of a sexually transmitted disease should not have been admitted, and that the state had failed to prove the date of the crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of sexual battery against a child under the age of 12 years. On appeal, defendant argued that blood test results should not have been admitted, evidence of a sexually transmitted disease should not have been admitted, and that the state had failed to prove the date of the crime. The court rejected the arguments and affirmed the conviction. First, the court held that blood tests taken of defendant revealing that defendant had gonorrhea were properly admitted because they were taken pursuant to a valid warrant. In any case, the court noted that defendant did not object to the tests and therefore the search was consensual. Second, the court held that evidence that defendant and the minor victim had gonorrhea was properly admitted because such evidence was relevant and corroborated the victim's testimony. Third, the court held that there was no error from the fact that the indictment indicated that the crime occurred on or about January 17, 1986, when in fact the crime occurred on January 21, 1986. The court held that the date on the indictment was specific enough to put defendant on notice of the charge against him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

189 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Reed v. State


No. 58,069


Supreme Court of Mississippi


536 So. 2d 1336; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 610



December 14, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Rankin County; R. L. Goza, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In accordance with the jury's verdict, the Circuit Court of Rankin County (Mississippi) entered a judgment that convicted defendant of armed robbery in violation of Mississippi Code Annotated § 97-3-79 (1972) and sentenced him to life imprisonment. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Upon being shown a photo array, a jewelry store employee identified defendant as one of two men who robbed the store. Defendant's companion drew a gun and forced the employee to lie on the floor during the robbery. On appeal, defendant contended that he had ineffective counsel, that the sentence violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, and that the verdict was against the overwhelming weight of the evidence. The court rejected defendant's contentions, holding that the conduct of defendant's trial counsel fell within the wide range of reasonable professional assistance. Next, defendant's claim that his sentence was unconstitutional was procedurally barred because he did not present such argument to the circuit court. Finally, the evidence overwhelmingly was against defendant, reflecting that he was an active participant in the robbery; that he was positively identified as being one of the robbers; that the stolen items, or many of them, were recovered; and that the guilt issue was fairly resolved against him by the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

190 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Minnick v. State


No. DP-79


Supreme Court of Mississippi


551 So. 2d 77; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 612



December 14, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 25, 1989. Petition for Rehearing Filed January 5, 1989.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from Clarke County (Mississippi), which convicted him of murder while engaged in the crime of robbery and which imposed a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was improperly interrogated. The court found that police interviewed defendant after he requested a lawyer. The court determined, however, that defendant was provided with a lawyer, that the lawyer advised him not to discuss the charges against him with others, and that defendant voluntarily disregarded his lawyer's advice and confessed. The court found that the prosecution's delay in disclosure of witnesses did not prejudice defendant. The court found that an investigative report containing the statements of an unavailable witness was properly excluded as unreliable hearsay. The court determined that the chain of custody regarding two guns was properly established. The court held that a pre-trial identification was sufficiently fair. The court found that defendant had a reasonable opportunity to argue in mitigation and that the jury properly found aggravating circumstances. The court held that defendant received effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and the death sentence.
