Pinkney v. State


No. DP-76


Supreme Court of Mississippi


538 So. 2d 329; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 614



December 14, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended January 17, 1989



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AND SENTENCE OF DEATH AFFIRMED. WEDNESDAY, JANUARY 18, 1989, SET AS DATE FOR EXECUTION OF SENTENCE IN THE MANNER PROVIDED BY LAW.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Hinds County (Mississippi) after he was tried and convicted for capital murder and subsequently sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his capital murder conviction and death sentence, asserting several errors. He argued that the district attorney used a victim advocacy strategy prohibited by the court, and challenged the prosecutor's statements and a physician's testimony as to the victim's injuries. The state argued that defendant failed to make a proper objection as to the statements and thus the issue was procedurally barred. The court held that it had a statutory obligation to review death penalty cases to determine whether the sentence was imposed under the influence of arbitrary or extraneous influences. The court held that the jury's consideration of an improper aggravating factor was harmless error. Defendant also asserted that his confession was obtained in violation of his constitutional rights. The court held that the evidence failed to support defendant's contention that he had not knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily waived his rights, and that his challenge as to the admissibility of the confession was not well taken.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's capital murder conviction and sentence of death.

 

192 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Clemons v. State


No. DP-83


Supreme Court of Mississippi


535 So. 2d 1354; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 576



November 30, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Harrison County on Change of Venue from Warren County, John E. Ellis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. WEDNESDAY, JANUARY 4, 1989, SET FOR EXECUTION OF THE DEATH PENALTY IN THE MANNER PROVIDED BY LAW.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order by the Harrison County Circuit Court (Mississippi), which convicted defendant of capital murder of a pizza deliveryman. The jury in a bifurcated trial imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for capital murder committed during a robbery of a pizza deliveryman. The principal witness was a 17-year-old youth that was also indicted along with defendant and another person. The co-indictee and the state reached an agreement that if the co-indictee testified truthfully against defendant and the other co-indictee, the state would not seek the death penalty in regard to the co-indictee. The witness testified that defendant shot the pizza deliveryman with a sawed-off shotgun. Defendant was convicted and the trial court found two aggravating circumstances and no mitigating circumstances. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: (1) the testimony of the witness as a co-indictee was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction; (2) the jury was free to accept the testimony of the co-indictee; (3) there was no evidence to support a jury instruction on the alleged mitigating circumstance of low intelligence; (4) the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances; and (5) the jury verdict would have been the same even without the aggravating circumstance of especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of capital murder and death sentence.

 

193 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Mississippi State Highway Com. v. New Albany Gas Systems


No. 57,839


Supreme Court of Mississippi


534 So. 2d 204; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 544



November 16, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Chancery Court, Union County, George F. Adams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State Highway Commission challenged a judgment from the Chancery Court of Union County (Mississippi), which, on cross-motions for summary judgment, held that the Commission was estopped by laches from requiring removal of a gas line unless it incurred three-fourths of the cost to appellee city. Suit was first filed in the Chancery Court of Benton County seeking an injunction requiring removal and was transferred on the city's motion.


OVERVIEW: Where the gas pipeline crossed over a railroad line, the pipe was attached to the exterior of a bridge and was totally unprotected. The Commission determined that the pipeline had to be removed pursuant to Standard Operating Procedure No. MND-04-05-00-000, which prohibited attaching utility pipelines to state highway bridges except to carry water. The court found that the statute of limitations concerning adverse possession, § 29-3-7 of Miss. Code Ann. (1972), did not apply against the State and, therefore, the Commission. The matter was governed by Article 4, § 104 of the Mississippi Constitution of 1890. The permit or grant was revocable and could be terminated by the Commission for just cause under § 65-1-8 of Miss. Code Ann. (1988 Supp.). The chancellor found that if the Commission wanted the pipeline removed, it had to bear three-fourths of the cost. This contradicted the law requiring the owner, the city, to bear the cost of removal. The Commission's actions were supported by substantial evidence. The Commission did not act arbitrarily. The Commission acted properly when it requested that the pipeline be removed from the bridge, citing hazards to motorists.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the chancellor's opinion which assessed three-fourths of the costs of the pipeline removal against the Commission. The court affirmed that part of the chancellor's opinion holding that the Commission had a right to request the removal of the pipeline. The court's judgment gave the city a reasonable length of time to implement the court's holding.

 

194 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State


No. 58,009


Supreme Court of Mississippi


534 So. 2d 1019; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 532



November 9, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Filed November 21, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Lauderdale County, Lester F. Williamson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction and sentence from the Circuit Court of Lauderdale County (Mississippi). A jury verdict held defendant guilty of sexual battery of a minor child, a violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-3-95 (Supp. 1986), touching and handling a minor child, a violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 97-5-23 (Supp. 1986), and counts of contributing to the delinquency of a minor, a violation of Miss. Code Ann. § 43-23-25 (Supp. 1986).


OVERVIEW: Defendant showed two victims, a former step-daughter and her girl friend, pictures of nude women and took nude pictures of the victims. Defendant hosted parties for the victims that provided them with alcoholic drinks, marijuana, and drugs before they performed sexual acts with him. The court affirmed the contested judgment because defendant's assignment of errors lacked merit. The trial court correctly overruled defendant's demurrer to the State's multiple count indictment filed under Miss. Code Ann. § 99-7-2 (Supp. 1986). The court found that defendant's conduct toward the victims was part of the same occurrence or scheme. The court found that defendant's methods of seduction were part of a sexual battery. The court decided that, under Miss. R. Evid. 404(b), those methods were relevant to the charges of contributing to the delinquency of a minor. The trial court correctly allowed a trial on all counts because the indictments arose from the same transactions and the evidence was admissible for each of the charges. The court determined that the evidence admitted at trial was not unconstitutionally obtained and that ample probable cause existed to issue the search warrants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

195 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Collier v. Shell Oil Co.


No. 58,824


Supreme Court of Mississippi


534 So. 2d 1015; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 533



November 9, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Addition Time Granted for Petition for Rehearing Filed December 7, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Chancery Court, Rankin County; Billy G. Bridges, Chancellor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant illegitimate heirs sought review of a decree by the Chancery Court, Rankin County (Mississippi), which held in favor of appellee oil companies on the question of title to oil, gas, and minerals on certain land.


OVERVIEW: The legitimate heirs of the decedent executed leased conveying to the first oil companies rights to oil, gas, and minerals. The first oil company then assigned an overriding royalty to the second oil company. The common law wife of one of the illegitimate heirs joined with the other illegitimate heirs and filed an action to establish their right to inherit under Miss. Code Ann. § 91-1-15 (Supp.1988). The oil companies filed motions for summary judgment, which the chancery court granted. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the rights of the oil companies were contract rights protected by U.S. Const. art. I, cl. 1 and Miss. Const. art. 3, § 16 (1890). The court reasoned that any rights the illegitimate heirs might have enjoyed under Miss. Code Ann. § 91-1-15 (Supp.1988) vested after the date when contract rights vested in the oil companies and were wholly subject to those rights. The court concluded that the oil companies were bona fide purchasers for value and because the land records nor accessible law gave them no notice of the illegitimate heirs' claims, they acquired title against the world.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decree, which found that the oil companies held title to the minerals.

 

196 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Fisher v. State


No. 57,679


Supreme Court of Mississippi


532 So. 2d 992; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 438



September 14, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Smith County-Change of Venue from Lauderdale County; Lester F. Williamson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Smith County (Mississippi) convicted defendant of rape and sentenced him to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for the capital murder of a victim and for the rape of a second victim. The trial judge in the rape case continued the trial pending the outcome of the murder trial. When defendant's murder conviction was overturned on appeal, the State proceeded on the rape charge. Defendant argued that he was denied his right to a speedy trial, but the court affirmed his conviction. The court examined four factors for purposes of assessing defendant's constitutional right to a speedy trial. The 790 day delay in bringing defendant to trial was lengthy. However, the reason for the delay, to try defendant on a capital crime, was legitimate. The court assigned little weight to defendant's failure to assert his right to a speedy trial because there was some question as to whether defendant was aware of the continuance. Finally, the court found that the absence of prejudice to defendant weighed heavily in favor of the State. The delay did not violate the speedy trial statute, Miss. Code Ann. § 99-17-1 (Supp. 1987), because the written order of continuance was the equivalent of a judicial determination that good cause existed for granting the continuance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

197 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Burrell v. Mississippi State Tax Com.


No. 58,054


Supreme Court of Mississippi


536 So. 2d 848; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 367



August 10, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing filed August 24, 1988; As amended September 12, 1988; Rehearing Denied January 18, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Chancery Court, Hinds County; Stuart Robinson, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county taxpayers challenged the judgment of the Chancery Court of Hinds County (Mississippi), which, in an action brought against appellee state tax commission, held that a legislative enactment granting tax exempt status to a county nuclear power plant did not violate Miss. Const., art. 4, § 112. The taxpayers also argued that they were improperly denied leave to amend their complaint to include federal constitutional claims.


OVERVIEW: The county taxpayers objected when the state legislature passed a bill that granted tax exempt status to a nuclear power plant within their county. Because it was the only nuclear plant within the state that meet the statute's criteria, and thus they were the only county affected by the statute, the taxpayers argued that the law violated Miss. Const. art. 4, § 122. The court agreed that the statute violated the "old" § 112, but the question was whether earlier amendments to the state constitution did in fact legally change the constitution and thus made the statute valid. The court held that the amendments were valid, that they did apply retroactively, and that the statute was a constitutional "general" law, rather than a "special" law, even though it applied to only the one power plant. However, the court held that the trial court abused its discretion in not permitting the taxpayers to amend their complaint to include 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and Equal Protection claims. Although the motion for leave to amend was filed late in the case, refusal of the federal courts to hear the claim meant that the state court was the only forum open to the taxpayers to resolve the issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further proceedings. The court held that the statute granting tax exempt status to a county nuclear power plant was valid under the recently amended state constitution but that the trial court abused its discretion in not permitting appellant county taxpayers to amend their complaint to included § 1983 and Equal Protection claims in their action against appellee state tax commission.

White v. State


Nos. 57,448, DP-66


Supreme Court of Mississippi


532 So. 2d 1207; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 365



August 3, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing filed August 29, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Grenada County; James C. Sumner, Judge.



DISPOSITION:  CONVICTION OF CAPITAL MURDER AFFIRMED; SENTENCE OF DEATH REVERSED AND RENDERED; CASE REMANDED TO CIRCUIT COURT FOR HEARING ON HABITUAL OFFENDER CHARGE AND FOR IMPOSITION OF LAWFUL SENTENCE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his capital murder conviction and sentence of death from the Circuit Court, Grenada County (Mississippi).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for capital murder, and under the enhancement portion of the indictment he was charged as an habitual offender to be sentenced pursuant to Miss. Code Ann. § 99-19-81 (Supp. 1984). On appeal from his murder conviction and death sentence, defendant challenged the refusal of the trial court to suppress an in-court identification of defendant based upon its being the product of an impermissibly suggestive pre-trial procedure. So much of the judgment as ordered that defendant be put to death was reversed and rendered and the case was remanded for a hearing on the charge laid in the indictment that defendant was a habitual offender. Having failed to satisfy an element of proof, the state was not permitted a second bite at the apple. Due process rights secured to defendant by Miss. Const. art. 3, § 14 (1890) precluded enforcement of the sentence of death against him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of capital murder, reversed his sentence of death, and remanded the case for a hearing on the habitual offender charge and for imposition of a lawful sentence.

 

199 of 825 DOCUMENTS


Calhoun County Bd. of Supervisors v. Grenada Bank


No. 56,228


Supreme Court of Mississippi


543 So. 2d 138; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 340



July 20, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified on Denial of Rehearing May 3, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Calhoun County; William R. Lamb, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant County Board of Supervisors (board) sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court, Calhoun County (Mississippi) that granted appellee taxpayer's motion notwithstanding the verdict concerning the net value of the intangible assets of the taxpayer's two bank branches.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer reported to the county tax assessor that the net value of the intangible assets of its two bank branches was $ 23,991. The tax assessor computed the value as $ 522,561. The taxpayer was charged taxes of $ 50,729.22. The board overruled an objection by the taxpayer and the taxpayer appealed. A jury found the valuation to be fair and reasonable. Upon the taxpayer's motion, the trial court entered judgment for the taxpayer notwithstanding the verdict, reasoning that the valuation and assessment were unconstitutional under Miss. Const. § 112. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded in part. The court held that the trial court reached the right result in assessing the intangibles according to the State Tax Commission formula. However, the court held that in view of the overriding constitutional consideration of equality and uniformity in the application of tax laws, and in view of its duty to construe statutes in accordance with the perceived intent of the legislature, the court, prospectively, required use of the adapted multi-state corporation formula for valuation of branch banks until the legislature determined otherwise.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that the valuation and assessment were unconstitutional under Miss. Const. § 112. The court reversed the trial court in holding that the entire balance of the taxpayer's bad debt reserves was deductible. The court remanded for determination of the amount, if any, disbursed from the taxpayer's bad debt reserves to cover actual bad debts realized during the taxable year and for re-computation of the tax liability.

 

200 of 825 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Smiley


No. 57,539


Supreme Court of Mississippi


530 So. 2d 18; 1988 Miss. LEXIS 333



July 13, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Chancery Court, Jasper County; Dannye L. Hunter, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: In conclusion, we find that the chancellor erred in granting summary judgment in defendants' favor, and in dismissing Plaintiffs' suit. We reverse and remand.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, illegitimate children of the original owner of two tracts of real property, challenged the decision of the Chancery Court, Jasper County (Mississippi), which entered a summary judgment in favor of appellees, established heirs of the original owner of real property and others who took title through them, in an action to determine heirship and redivide assets.


OVERVIEW: In response to the action brought by the illegitimate children, the established heirs and others who took title through them answered and counterclaimed in which they sought cloud removal and quieting of title. The trial court sustained the motions to dismiss and for summary judgment of the established heirs and others who took title through them and denied the motion for partial summary judgment of the illegitimate children of the original owner. An appeal was taken. The court held that it was premature for the trial court to have ruled that Miss. Code Ann. § 91-1-15 was unconstitutional when it was unclear whether the illegitimate children could actually recover. Inasmuch as the court found the trial court's ruling that the statute was unconstitutional, the contingent findings as to res judicata and statute of limitations were also premature. Finally, the court held that the trial court did not err in failing to grant the illegitimate children partial summary judgment because, in a prior action, the issue decided was whether the father of the illegitimate children had a common law marriage with their mother. The issue of paternity for the illegitimate children was not decided.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's decision, which entered summary judgment in favor of the established heirs of the original owner of real property and others who took title through them in an action to determine heirship and redivide assets.
